  - **6W.** Commit. Lock auto-releases. The next admin click in the wizard sees the file marked applied; the live folder's cron is unaffected.
- **Wizard finalize promotion (§4.5 atomic promotion + Phase 2 batch — manifest stays `'staged'` until per-row commit succeeds).** When the wizard finalize endpoint resolves an empty unresolved set per §9.0, it MUST promote ALL `wizard_approved = TRUE` staged rows in one transaction. Inside `withShowSyncTransaction` per session: (i) `SELECT drive_file_id, parse_result, triggered_review_items, staged_modified_time, wizard_approved_by_email, wizard_approved_at, wizard_reviewer_choices FROM pending_syncs WHERE wizard_session_id = $sessionId AND wizard_approved = TRUE ORDER BY drive_file_id` (deterministic ordering for deadlock prevention) — every row carries the durable approval payload thanks to the §4.5 symmetry CHECK. (ii) acquire the per-show advisory lock for EACH approved row's `drive_file_id` (in the SELECT's deterministic alphabetical order); (iii) for EACH row, run §5.2 Phase 2 against `parse_result` exactly as live Apply step 4L would, **passing the row's `wizard_reviewer_choices` as the choices payload** (instead of re-deriving from `triggered_review_items` defaults) AND **passing `wizard_approved_by_email` + `wizard_approved_at` as the sync_audit attribution fields** (so the audit row reflects the operator who clicked Apply, with the timestamp of THAT click — not the operator who clicked Finalize). The §5.2 Phase 2 inserts/updates `shows`, writes `sync_audit` per §6.8.3, DELETEs the `pending_syncs` row, AND in the same per-row sub-statement UPDATEs `onboarding_scan_manifest SET status = 'applied' WHERE wizard_session_id = $sessionId AND drive_file_id = $row.drive_file_id`; (iv) run the §4.5 atomic-promotion CAS (`watched_folder_id = pending_folder_id`, etc.); (v) commit. **Manifest lifecycle: the manifest row stays `'staged'` (or whatever wizard-Apply set it to in step 5W) UNTIL the per-row Phase 2 sub-statement commits the manifest UPDATE in (iii) above; finalize-time `'applied'` is written in the SAME transaction as the corresponding `shows` INSERT/UPDATE. There is NO transient `'promoting'` state and NO pre-commit `'applied'` write that a ROLLBACK would have to compensate for** — if finalize aborts, the manifest naturally stays at the value step 5W wrote (which is also `'applied'` for wizard-Apply approval, but that value already meant "approved for promotion" pre-finalize and continues to mean exactly that post-rollback; the unresolved-gate query treats `'applied'` as resolved AND finalize-time re-entry will re-promote on the next click). For the failure case where a per-row §6.8.1 step-3 Drive re-verify raises `STAGED_PARSE_SOURCE_GONE` / `STAGED_PARSE_SOURCE_OUT_OF_SCOPE` / `STAGED_PARSE_SUPERSEDED`: finalize aborts the entire transaction (ROLLBACK) AND, **in a separate follow-up transaction after the rollback**, UPDATE `onboarding_scan_manifest SET status = 'staged' WHERE wizard_session_id = $sessionId AND drive_file_id = $offending_row.drive_file_id` so the wizard finalize gate re-blocks pending re-review — this UPDATE is OUTSIDE the rolled-back transaction and is therefore a real durable write, not a no-op. Returns 409 with the per-row failure code so the wizard UI can surface the file that failed re-verify. Live folder cron remains uninterrupted because no live writes have happened yet.

**The CAS keys on `base_modified_time`, not `staged_modified_time`.** The two are intentionally different — staging means "the incoming sheet has changed past what's live, but we don't auto-apply the change because it's suspicious." `base` is what Doug compared against; `staged` is what he wants to commit. Equality on `base` proves no other write has slipped in since review.

**Approval never re-parses.** The decision Doug made is bound to the bytes he saw. The CAS in step 2 ensures that even with a concurrent cron run, the apply path commits exactly the staged data or aborts cleanly — never a hybrid.

#### 6.8.2 Approval-metadata contract

**The client never computes auth side-effects, and the server never persists per-attempt approval metadata on the shared `pending_syncs` row.** Persisting metadata before locking would let two concurrent Apply attempts race to overwrite each other's choices before either acquires the advisory lock. Instead, reviewer choices are submitted with the Apply request and consumed entirely inside the locked transaction (§6.8.1).

**Per-item identity.** A staged parse can trigger the same invariant multiple times — e.g., MI-11 firing for two distinct crew with email changes, or two MI-13 rename candidates in one sync. `pending_syncs.triggered_review_items` is a list of items each carrying a stable `id` UUID generated at staging time. Reviewer choices reference these ids; "exactly one choice per item id" is the validation rule, not "exactly one choice per invariant code."

**Client submission shape (the Apply endpoint) — canonical version 1:**

```json
{
  "staged_id": "<uuid>",
  "choices": [
    { "item_id": "<uuid-of-triggered-item>", "action": "apply" },
    { "item_id": "<uuid-of-triggered-item>", "action": "rename", "rename_value": "<target-name>" },
    { "item_id": "<uuid-of-triggered-item>", "action": "independent" }
  ]
}
```

The client sends only `(item_id, action)` pairs (plus `rename_value` when `action === 'rename'`). All other parameters (which crew_name, which removed/added pair) come from the stored `triggered_review_items` row. The client cannot inject names; it can only choose actions.

**Payload-shape version.** This shape is **version 1**. Wizard Apply (step 5W) MUST persist the payload alongside `pending_syncs.wizard_reviewer_choices_version = 1` in the same UPDATE that sets the other approval-payload columns. Finalize-time Phase B replay reads BOTH `wizard_reviewer_choices` AND `wizard_reviewer_choices_version` and dispatches to the version-1 validator + derivation table; any other version → `WIZARD_REVIEWER_CHOICES_VERSION_UNSUPPORTED` (§12.4) with the manifest demoted back to `'staged'` per the manifest-lifecycle rule. The version exists so a future shape revision (e.g., adding a new action for a future invariant, expanding per-item context fields) can coexist with old wizard-staged approvals: the new validator will register a `version: 2` and finalize will refuse to silently replay version-1 payloads through the version-2 derivation table. Live Apply (`wizard_session_id IS NULL`) does NOT persist a version — its validation runs in the same request as Phase 2 and there is no deferred-replay window. The §4.5 symmetry CHECK ensures `wizard_reviewer_choices_version` is NULL on live rows AND non-NULL on every approved wizard row.

**Server-side derivation table** (the only place auth side-effects are computed; runs request-local inside the locked transaction):

| Triggered item invariant                                                | Valid `action` values     | Server-derived auth side-effects                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     |
| ----------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ |
| ~~FIRST_SEEN_REVIEW~~                                                   | ~~`apply`~~               | **Retired per amendment 9 (2026-05-09).** No code path emits this sentinel under the post-amendment routing precedence (§5.2 step 3). First-seen sheets that pass MI-1..MI-14 auto-apply directly via Phase 2 with a 24h `unpublish_token`; the confirmation event is `SHOW_FIRST_PUBLISHED` (admin_alerts info, NOT a `triggered_review_items` entry). First-seen sheets with MI-6..MI-14 trips stage with the relevant MI sentinel, not this one. Onboarding-scan first-seen still stages but with `ONBOARDING_SCAN_REVIEW` (next row), not this one. Row preserved as strikethrough so consumers reading old `pending_syncs.triggered_review_items` JSONB blobs from before the amendment cutover have a migration reference.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  |
| ONBOARDING_SCAN_REVIEW                                                  | `apply`                   | none. Sentinel for files that would have auto-applied except they came from `runOnboardingScan` (`mode: "onboarding_scan"`) which never runs Phase 2 directly. **Apply contract — DEFERRED-UNTIL-FINALIZE (durable approval payload).** A wizard-scope Apply is a Phase-1-only "approval": inside the locked transaction it (a) atomically sets all four approval-payload columns in one UPDATE — `wizard_approved = TRUE`, `wizard_approved_by_email = canonicalize_email($admin.email)`, `wizard_approved_at = now()`, `wizard_reviewer_choices = $validatedReviewerChoices` (the §6.8.2 reviewer*choices payload after the same server-side validation live Apply runs); (b) does NOT mutate `shows`; (c) does NOT mint a fresh `snapshot_revision_id`; (d) does NOT INSERT `sync_audit` (finalize writes audit at promotion time using the persisted approval payload — `wizard_approved_by_email`/`wizard_approved_at` become the audit's attribution fields, NOT whoever clicks Finalize); (e) does NOT DELETE the staged row; (f) does NOT touch the live folder's `pending*\*`partition. The approved row stays in`pending_syncs WHERE wizard_session_id = $session AND wizard_approved = TRUE`carrying its full immutable approval payload. Wizard finalize then promotes ALL approved staged rows atomically (Phase 2 against each of them, **passing each row's`wizard_reviewer_choices` as the choices payload so MI-11/12/13/14 derived_side_effects reflect Doug's actual ACCEPT/REJECT decisions, not the triggered-review-items defaults\*\*) within the same transaction that performs the §4.5 atomic-promotion CAS. Rationale: this preserves the "live folder keeps cron-syncing while wizard runs" guarantee and prevents partial onboarding state from polluting live data when the candidate folder is not yet the watched folder. User-facing copy in §12.4. |
| MI-6, MI-7, MI-7b, MI-8, MI-8b, MI-8c                                   | `apply`                   | none (no auth floor bump). MI-10 is consolidated into MI-9's row below post-amendment-8 (both predicates are the LEAD-bit toggle).                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   |
| MI-9 (LEAD-bit toggle, narrowed per amendment 8) / MI-10                | `apply`                   | none — LEAD propagates via Phase 2 UPSERT, takes effect on next request. Post-amendment-8 MI-9 and MI-10 are the same predicate (LEAD-bit set membership change). Non-LEAD `role_flags` deltas auto-apply via Phase 2 UPSERT and emit an info-severity `ROLE_FLAGS_NOTICE` admin alert without staging.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              |
| MI-11 (email change, same name)                                         | `apply`                   | bump auth floor for `item.crew_name`                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 |
| MI-12 (probable rename, same email)                                     | `rename` \| `reject`      | `rename`: bump auth floor for both `item.removed_name` AND `item.added_name`; record `{from: removed_name, to: added_name}` in audit. `reject`: route to Discard path; the parse is rejected as if the user clicked Discard (an item-level rejection still kills the entire staged parse — partial-applies are out of scope for v1).                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 |
| MI-13 (pre-paired by detector at staging)                               | `rename` \| `independent` | `rename`: bump auth floor for both `item.removed_name` AND `item.added_name` (matches MI-12). `independent`: per §5.2's universal "bump on add" rule, the added name's auth floor is automatically bumped at INSERT time regardless of this item's choice. So the per-item auth side-effect for `independent` is just the standard removal flow — no extra action needed beyond the §5.2 default behavior; the audit record notes the pair was rejected as a rename.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 |
| MI-14 (pre-paired no-email)                                             | `rename` \| `independent` | Same as MI-13.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       |
| MI-13-orphan-remove, MI-14-orphan-remove (single-side leftover removal) | `apply`                   | bump auth floor for `item.removed_name`. (No rename option — there's nothing to pair with.)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          |
| MI-13-orphan-add, MI-14-orphan-add (single-side leftover addition)      | `apply`                   | none — §5.2's universal "bump on add" already handles this name.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     |

**Server-side validation, performed inside the locked transaction:**

1. **Choice completeness.** Every entry in `pending_syncs.triggered_review_items` must have exactly one matching choice (matched by `item_id`). Missing → `MISSING_REVIEWER_CHOICE`. Extra → `EXTRA_REVIEWER_CHOICE`. Duplicate `item_id` in submission → `DUPLICATE_REVIEWER_CHOICE`.
2. **Action validity.** Each choice's `action` must be one of the values listed for the corresponding item's invariant. Wrong `action` → `INVALID_REVIEWER_ACTION`.
3. **No name validation needed** — the names come from the server-stored item, not the client.
4. **Reject handling.** If any choice carries `action: "reject"`, the entire Apply is **routed through the same server-side Discard transaction described below** — it does not just DELETE `pending_syncs`. The Discard path restores `shows.last_sync_status` / `last_sync_error` from the captured `prior_last_sync_status` / `prior_last_sync_error`, then deletes the `pending_syncs` row, all inside the advisory lock. No destructive write, no `sync_audit` row (the action wasn't an apply). This is critical: skipping the Discard restore would leave the show stuck in `'pending_review'` with no `pending_syncs` row, which breaks both the dashboard queue and the show's status indicator. Partial applies are still out of scope; v1 either applies the whole staged parse with all auth side-effects or rejects all of it via the same Discard logic.

After validation passes, the server computes the union of all per-item side-effects, executes the Phase 2 transaction (DELETE-then-UPSERT, `crew_member_auth` floor bumps for the union of names), inserts the `sync_audit` row carrying `triggered_review_items` and `reviewer_choices`, and DELETEs `pending_syncs`. All of this happens inside the same lock + transaction so no concurrent Apply can interleave.

**The Apply transaction's auth-side-effect step** (after the standard DELETE-then-UPSERT in §5.2 Phase 2):

```sql
-- Bump auth floor for every name in revoke_floor_for_names.
-- Idempotent: re-running Apply with the same metadata is a no-op.
UPDATE crew_member_auth
   SET revoked_below_version = current_token_version
 WHERE show_id = $show_id
   AND crew_name = ANY($1::text[]);  -- $1 = derived_side_effects.revoke_floor_for_names (computed request-local from validated choices)
```

The Apply side derives the `revoke_floor_for_names` set request-locally from the validated reviewer choices. Nothing mutable is persisted on `pending_syncs` between staging and Apply, so concurrent Apply attempts can race the lock but cannot poison each other's metadata.

#### 6.8.3 Durable audit record

After Apply commits successfully, the server inserts a row into `sync_audit` (new admin-only table) **before deleting `pending_syncs`**:

```sql
create table sync_audit (
  id                uuid primary key default gen_random_uuid(),
  show_id           uuid references shows(id) on delete cascade,
  drive_file_id     text not null,
  applied_at        timestamptz not null default now(),
  applied_by        text not null,                  -- admin email (Doug or Eric)
  staged_id         uuid not null,                  -- the pending_syncs.staged_id consumed
  triggered_review_items jsonb not null,            -- copy of pending_syncs.triggered_review_items at the moment of Apply (each with id, invariant, item-specific fields)
  reviewer_choices  jsonb not null,                 -- the validated client submission: [{item_id, action}, ...]
  derived_side_effects jsonb not null,              -- the union of server-derived auth side-effects: { revoke_floor_for_names: [...], rename_pairings: [...], independent_changes: [...] }
  parse_result_summary jsonb not null,              -- compact summary of what got applied: { crewMemberCount, hotelCount, ... } — the full parse_result is large and lives in sync_log if needed for forensics
  base_modified_time timestamptz,
  staged_modified_time timestamptz not null
);
create index sync_audit_show_id_idx on sync_audit (show_id, applied_at desc);
create index sync_audit_drive_file_id_idx on sync_audit (drive_file_id, applied_at desc);
```

Every Apply produces exactly one `sync_audit` row. This is the canonical record of "who approved what, with which decisions, against what staged version, with what auth side-effects." If a revoke is later observed to have been missed (or unexpectedly applied), `sync_audit` is the source of truth for forensic recovery. RLS: admin-only.

When admin clicks "Discard" — Discard variants depend on stage type and admin's intent. **Every Discard read AND DELETE on `pending_syncs` MUST use the same source-scoped selector documented in §6.8.1's "Source-scoped selector" prose above.** Dashboard / live-row Discard adds `AND wizard_session_id IS NULL`; wizard step-3 Discard adds `AND wizard_session_id = $myWizardSessionId`.

**Existing-show stage** has one Discard variant:

- Inside the advisory lock + transaction: read `pending_syncs.prior_last_sync_status` / `prior_last_sync_error` **using the source-scoped selector** (existing-show Discard is dashboard-only — `AND wizard_session_id IS NULL`; an existing-show stage cannot live in the wizard partition because the wizard never runs Phase 2 against the live folder). `UPDATE shows SET last_sync_status = $prior_status, last_sync_error = $prior_error WHERE drive_file_id = $1`. DELETE the `pending_syncs` row using the same source-scoped selector. COMMIT. The page continues serving the prior approved snapshot. Status indicator returns to its pre-stage value (which may itself be a non-`ok` state like `sheet_unavailable` — Discard does not falsely make a degraded show look healthy). The next cron run will re-parse the (still-modified) sheet and re-stage if invariants still trip.

**First-seen stage** has THREE Discard variants because the staged data has no prior snapshot to fall back to and we need to control whether the file re-stages on the next cron run. **All three use the source-scoped selector** (`AND wizard_session_id IS NULL` for dashboard Discard; `AND wizard_session_id = $myWizardSessionId` for wizard step-3 Discard).

**`deferred_ingestions` writes are also source-scoped.** With the §4.5 partition shape (live partition `WHERE wizard_session_id IS NULL` vs wizard partition `WHERE wizard_session_id IS NOT NULL`), every INSERT below MUST set `wizard_session_id` to match the source scope: dashboard Discard (origin URL `/admin/show/<slug>` or dashboard first-seen panel) sets `wizard_session_id = NULL` and targets the live partial unique index `deferred_ingestions_live_drive_file_idx`; wizard step-3 Discard (carrying the active `wizard_session_id`) sets `wizard_session_id = $myWizardSessionId` and targets `deferred_ingestions_session_drive_file_idx`. Wizard-scoped deferrals are then DELETEd on wizard finalize (option-A clean slate per §4.5 lifecycle) so a wizard's deferral choices never carry into the newly-active folder.

- **"Discard — try again next sync"** (default if admin doesn't pick): DELETE the `pending_syncs` row (source-scoped). No `deferred_ingestions` row written. The next cron run re-fetches and re-stages from scratch. Use this when admin meant "I'll come back to this." This is the only Discard path that DOES leave the wizard non-finalizable per §9.0 step 3 — the wizard explicitly cannot consider this state "complete."
- **"Discard — skip until edited"** (`defer_until_modified`): DELETE the `pending_syncs` row (source-scoped). INSERT a `deferred_ingestions` row with `deferred_kind = 'defer_until_modified'`, `deferred_at_modified_time = pending_syncs.staged_modified_time`, AND `wizard_session_id` set per the source scope above (NULL for dashboard Discard targeting `deferred_ingestions_live_drive_file_idx`; the active `wizard_session_id` for wizard step-3 Discard targeting `deferred_ingestions_session_drive_file_idx`). Cron skips this `drive_file_id` (live-partition SELECT only) until Doug edits the sheet (Drive bumps modifiedTime); then the live deferral row is auto-DELETEd and processing resumes. Wizard-scoped rows are read by the wizard's step-3 manifest renderer (where applicable) and DELETEd on finalize (clean slate). Use this for WIP sheets Doug isn't ready to review yet.
- **"Discard — permanently ignore"** (`permanent_ignore`): DELETE the `pending_syncs` row (source-scoped). INSERT a `deferred_ingestions` row with `deferred_kind = 'permanent_ignore'` AND `wizard_session_id` set per the source scope above. Cron skips this `drive_file_id` (live-partition SELECT only) indefinitely until admin manually deletes the live deferral row. Wizard-scoped rows are DELETEd on finalize (clean slate) — a wizard's permanent-ignore choice for a candidate folder does NOT survive folder promotion, since the candidate's "wrong file" judgement may not apply post-promotion. Use this for sheets that don't belong (someone shared a wrong file into the folder, etc.).

The §9.0 wizard step 3 considers a sheet "resolved for onboarding completion" if any of: applied (becomes a `shows` row), discarded with `defer_until_modified`, or discarded with `permanent_ignore`. The default "try again next sync" variant does NOT count as resolved — the wizard prompts admin to pick one of the three terminal actions before letting onboarding complete.

Hard errors (`hardErrors[]`) from the parser itself remain reserved for unrecoverable structural failures (e.g., the input wasn't a markdown table at all). The minimum invariants are layered on top of `hardErrors` and catch the "parse succeeded technically but the output is suspicious" case.

Everything that's not a hard error and not an invariant violation is a soft warning — surfaced to Doug, optionally reported to Eric, sync proceeds.

### 6.9 Slug derivation

The crew page URL is `/show/<slug>`; the slug is set on first successful parse and never changes for the lifetime of the show. **Slug is not sheet data** — Doug renaming the spreadsheet in Drive does NOT change the slug, because crew already have URLs in their phones.

`deriveSlug(parseResult, existingSlugs)`:

1. Build a base candidate: `<YYYY-MM>-<title-slug>` where:
   - `<YYYY-MM>` comes from `parseResult.show.dates.set ?? dates.travelIn ?? dates.showDays[0]` formatted as `2026-03`. (One of these is guaranteed by MI-3.)
   - `<title-slug>` is `parseResult.show.title` lowercased, ASCII-folded, non-alphanumeric → `-`, collapsed runs of `-`, trimmed leading/trailing `-`, capped at 60 characters. Example: `RPAS Central 2026` → `rpas-central-2026`.
2. **Collision policy (retry-on-unique-violation loop)**: a naive `existingSlugs` snapshot read followed by an INSERT is racy — two concurrent first-seen Applies for distinct `drive_file_id`s with the same `(year-month, title-slug)` both observe the SAME `existingSlugs` set, both pick the same candidate slug (e.g., `2026-03-rpas-central-2026`), and one INSERT fails with `23505` _unique_violation_ on `shows.slug`. The corrected policy wraps the INSERT in a retry loop:
   ```ts
   // Pseudocode (the implementation lives in lib/sync/applyStaged.ts and lib/parser/slug.ts):
   const baseSlug = buildBaseSlug(parseResult); // step 1 above; deterministic
   for (let attempt = 1; attempt <= 100; attempt++) {
     const candidateSlug = attempt === 1 ? baseSlug : `${baseSlug}-${attempt}`;
     try {
       await tx`INSERT INTO shows (slug, drive_file_id, ...) VALUES (${candidateSlug}, ${driveFileId}, ...)`;
       return candidateSlug; // success
     } catch (err) {
       if (isPostgresUniqueViolation(err) && err.constraint === "shows_slug_key") {
         continue; // race lost; advance to next suffix
       }
       throw err; // any other error (FK violation, NOT NULL, etc.) bubbles up
     }
   }
   throw new SlugCollisionExhausted(baseSlug); // 100 attempts exhausted
   ```
   The retry loop runs INSIDE the per-show advisory lock acquired by `applyStaged` (the same lock that gates Phase 2 commit), so the only race window is between two Applies for DIFFERENT `drive_file_id`s — each holds its own advisory lock keyed on `drive_file_id`. The retry catches Postgres `23505` _unique_violation_ on the `shows.slug` UNIQUE constraint specifically; any other error code bubbles up unchanged. The `existingSlugs` parameter is now informational only (used by `deriveSlug()` callers in tests / dev panels for UX preview); the AUTHORITATIVE collision check is the database's UNIQUE constraint, observed via `23505`. **Terminate at attempt 100** (covering `<base>` and `<base>-2` through `<base>-100`) and emit `SLUG_COLLISION_EXHAUSTED` (renamed from `SLUG_COLLISION_LIMIT` to clarify the new exhaustion semantics — the prior name's literal `-99` ceiling was off-by-one against the `attempt <= 100` loop iterating from `attempt=1` for the bare `<base>` then `attempt=2..100` for `<base>-2..<base>-100`).
3. The selected slug is INSERTed with the `shows` row in Phase 2 / Apply. **It is never updated** by subsequent syncs even if the title changes.

Slug derivation runs only when `shows` doesn't yet exist for the `drive_file_id`. Subsequent syncs of the same `drive_file_id` keep the slug as-is.

Edge cases:

- A subsequent show with the same `(year-month, title)` collides at the slug level; `-2` resolves it. Two shows with literally identical 2-tuples is rare in practice (Doug's templates carry the year in the title).
- A re-share of a previously-deleted show under a fresh `drive_file_id` would produce a fresh `shows` row with a fresh slug; the prior crew URLs from the old `shows` row remain pointed at archived data via the `archived` flag in §11. Doug's choice to re-issue links for the new show is part of the per-show admin flow.

### 6.10 PULL SHEET (per-case packing list) parsing

The PULL SHEET tab is present in only some sheets (`2024-05-east-coast-family-office.md`, `2025-05-redefining-fixed-income-private-credit.md`; absent from 2025-06+). When present, it carries per-case packing rows that are genuinely useful to crew on set/strike days. The parser extracts what's there and stores it in `shows.pull_sheet`; absence is normal and handled gracefully (column stays NULL, tile in §8.1 doesn't render).

**Parse contract:**

```ts
type PullSheetCase = {
  caseLabel: string; // e.g. "CASE 1", "TOTAL COUNT CORP & INS / SALON 1"
  items: PullSheetItem[];
};
type PullSheetItem = {
  qty: number | null; // nullable for malformed rows; renderer treats null as "?" or skips
  cat: string | null; // category, e.g. "AUDIO"
  subCat: string | null; // sub-category, e.g. "MICROPHONE"
  item: string; // line-item name (required; rows with no item are dropped)
  rawSnippet?: string; // verbatim row for fallback render if anything fails to map
};
```

**Detection:**

The PULL SHEET tab uses a **positional column layout, NOT a `QTY / CAT / SUB CAT / ITEM` text header**. Verified against `2024-05-east-coast-family-office.md:207-275` and `2025-05-redefining-fixed-income-private-credit.md:360-430`.

- The pull-sheet block starts with a header row whose ALL cells contain the literal text `PULL SHEET` (the merged case-title is replicated across every column of that markdown row — e.g. `| PULL SHEET/East Coast... | PULL SHEET/East Coast... | PULL SHEET/East Coast... | PULL SHEET/East Coast... | PULL SHEET/East Coast... |`). The case label is extracted from the title text after the `PULL SHEET/` prefix; for nested sub-cases like `TOTAL COUNT CORP & INS / SALON 1`, the parser flattens to one case per sub-section.
- Subsequent rows are positional (5 columns): **`packed_flag | qty | item | sub_cat | cat`**:
  - col 1 (packed_flag): `FALSE`/`TRUE` checkbox indicator (informational; not stored)
  - col 2 (qty): integer (parseable as number; null if blank)
  - col 3 (item): line-item name (REQUIRED; rows with empty col 3 are dropped)
  - col 4 (sub_cat): nullable sub-category (e.g., `SPEAKERS / MONITOR`)
  - col 5 (cat): top-level category (e.g., `AUDIO`, `VIDEO`, `BASES`, `FOH`, `SCENIC`)
- The 2024-05 fixture has nested sub-tabs (`TOTAL COUNT CORP & INS / SALON 1`) — the parser emits one `PullSheetCase` per sub-tab.
- **The GEAR tab (2025-06+) is NOT a pull sheet** — `2025-06-ria-investment-forum.md:366-388` has the explicit text header `QTY | PULLED | INITAL | CAT | SUB CAT | ITEM | NOTES` (7 columns including the PULLED + INITAL audit columns). That table is operations-side packing data and is OUT OF SCOPE for the crew Pack List tile (§2 deferral list). The parser distinguishes the two by header shape:
  - **PULL SHEET** → first cell starts with literal `PULL SHEET` (no `QTY` text header below it).
  - **GEAR** → text header row contains BOTH `PULLED` AND `INITAL` (note the typo — verbatim in the fixture).

**Soft warnings (not hard fails):**

- `PULL_SHEET_PARSE_PARTIAL` — at least one row had unparseable QTY or empty critical column; the row is preserved with `rawSnippet` and `qty: null`. Tile renders the raw snippet for that row.
- `PULL_SHEET_AMBIGUOUS_FORMAT` — the parser detected something pull-sheet-shaped (header contains `PULL SHEET`) but the row column count doesn't match the expected 5. The full block is preserved as a single case with `caseLabel: "Unparsed pull sheet"` and items rendered as raw snippets.

**MI-8c gate (clarification, supersedes any earlier soft-warning-only language).** Per §6.8 MI-8c, structural pull-sheet regressions ARE stage-for-approval invariants — full collapse, case-count halved, case-label dropped, or `PULL_SHEET_AMBIGUOUS_FORMAT` against a previously-non-ambiguous parse all stage. Per-row `PULL_SHEET_PARSE_PARTIAL` warnings on individual rows continue to auto-apply with `rawSnippet` fallback (the row is degraded, not the whole structure).

**Cardinality cap:** v1 renders up to 12 cases inline; "Show more" reveals the rest. Per-case items have no cap (cases typically hold ≤30 line items).

### 6.11 DIAGRAMS — embedded-image extraction

Newer sheets (2026+) carry **floating embedded images** positioned over the DIAGRAMS tab — the FinTech Forum 2026 fixture is the canonical example, with a 2D ballroom layout drawing and a 3D photo of the actual ballroom both pasted directly into the sheet. These images never appear in the markdown export the parser consumes for the rest of the sheet, so they need a separate extraction step.

**Extraction path (production):**

1. Standard parse runs against the markdown export (per §6.1–6.10) and produces the bulk `ParseResult`.
2. **Then** the sync layer (NOT the parser — embedded extraction lives in `lib/sync/enrichWithDrivePins.ts`) calls `spreadsheets.get` with `fields=sheets(properties.title,protectedRanges,charts,embeddedObjects(objectId,position,size,sourceUrl,image(contentUrl,sourceUrl,altText,sheetEmbeddedObject)))` and **NO `ranges=` parameter** (a hardcoded `ranges=DIAGRAMS!A1:Z1000` would be a case-sensitive A1-notation range that fails tab resolution against the corpus's `DIagrams` typo; spec §6.11 below mandates case-insensitive tab resolution). The implementation fetches all sheets and filters client-side via `sheets.find(s => s.properties.title.toLowerCase() === 'diagrams')` to handle the typo. A `files.export(mimeType: 'application/zip')` fallback is rejected: the zip export returns rasterized HTML + an `images/` folder but provides NO content-derived `embeddedFingerprint`, making it incompatible with the fail-closed contract that requires every embedded entry to carry either a non-null content-derived fingerprint OR `recovery_disposition = 'restage_required'`. Falling back to the zip would silently produce entries that look "captured" but cannot be re-verified at Apply or asset_recovery time, defeating the immutable-pin model. **Replacement behavior**: if `spreadsheets.get` returns no `embeddedObjects` for the resolved DIAGRAMS tab, the sync layer treats the result as `embeddedImages = []`. **Additionally**, when the parser had reason to expect images (a DIAGRAMS-tab was resolved by case-insensitive lookup AND the parsed sheet body carries no linked-folder URL — i.e., the sheet appears configured for embedded delivery), emit a `DIAGRAMS_EMBEDDED_NONE_FOUND` warning. Routing for this warning: for **first-seen sheets** carrying the warning, route to Phase 1 stage-for-approval (NOT auto-apply with an empty gallery) so the operator confirms the sheet is intentionally image-free before any `shows` row is created — appending a **`DIAGRAMS_EMBEDDED_NONE_FOUND` triggered review item** (this is its OWN variant, NOT aliased to `DIAGRAMS_EMBEDDED_REVISIONS_UNAVAILABLE`, because the two have DISTINCT Apply contracts — see §6.11.2 below for the per-variant Apply contract). For **existing shows**: the routing splits on whether the prior approved gallery is empty. **(b) Existing show with a non-empty current gallery** (`embeddedImages[].length > 0` OR `linkedFolderItems[].length > 0`): do NOT auto-apply; route to Phase 1 stage-for-approval, appending a `DIAGRAMS_EMBEDDED_NONE_FOUND` triggered review item. The prior approved gallery stays live (`shows.diagrams.snapshot_revision_id` unchanged) until the operator clicks Apply. An ambiguous empty `spreadsheets.get` response MUST NOT silently wipe an approved gallery — a transient API hiccup or a sheet with the DIAGRAMS tab temporarily emptied could otherwise destroy crew-visible imagery without operator review. **(c) Existing show with an already-empty current gallery** (both arrays empty): idempotent no-op auto-apply path — Phase 2 advances `last_seen_modified_time`; the diagrams JSONB shape is unchanged. The snapshot-mutation invariant still applies whenever non-diagram sheet-derived columns change in this Phase 2 (the column is rewritten with the same content + a fresh `snapshot_revision_id`); when the entire Phase 2 is a strict no-op, `shows.diagrams` is NOT touched at all and `snapshot_revision_id` stays the same. When the parsed sheet does carry a linked-folder URL, the empty `embeddedImages` is normal (linked-only sheet) and no warning is emitted. **Step ordering (MANDATORY).** Production runtime MUST call `spreadsheets.get` FIRST (this step) to determine whether the DIAGRAMS tab exists AND whether it contains image-like `embeddedObjects`. ONLY IF at least one embedded image is resolved is `drive.revisions.list` then called to capture `sheetsRevisionId`. For linked-only sheets (DIAGRAMS tab present but only contains a linked-folder URL — zero embeddedObjects), AND for no-DIAGRAMS-tab sheets, `drive.revisions.list` is NEVER called and enrichment/Apply lands successfully even when the revisions API is entirely unavailable. Making `drive.revisions.list` a precondition called BEFORE the embedded-presence check would block linked-only and no-DIAGRAMS-tab sheets behind an embedded-only API prerequisite. **Snapshot-mutation invariant:** EVERY successful Apply that mutates `shows.diagrams` MUST mint a fresh `snapshot_revision_id`; an Apply that does NOT mutate `shows.diagrams` MUST NOT touch the column. The four asset-review variants split cleanly along this axis: `DIAGRAMS_EMBEDDED_REVISIONS_UNAVAILABLE` is non-mutating (prior approved diagrams stay live verbatim); `DIAGRAMS_EMBEDDED_NONE_FOUND` (Apply path) is mutating (operator-confirmed empty gallery — mints a fresh `snapshot_revision_id` and persists `embeddedImages = []`); `DIAGRAMS_LINKED_FOLDER_DRIFT_PENDING` is mutating; standard auto-apply paths are mutating. **Critical: the existing-show-with-prior-gallery branch of `DIAGRAMS_EMBEDDED_NONE_FOUND` is NOT auto-applied** — it routes to stage-for-approval, leaves `shows.diagrams.snapshot_revision_id` unchanged, and only mints a fresh revision when the operator clicks Apply on the staged review item. The idempotent (already-empty-gallery) existing-show branch is a no-op for `shows.diagrams` whenever no other Phase 2 columns change. See §6.11.2 below for the full per-variant Apply contract.
3. For each embedded object on the DIAGRAMS tab whose type is image-like, record `{ sheetTab: "DIAGRAMS", objectId, mimeType, alt?, snapshotPath: null }` in the `parseResult.diagrams.embeddedImages` array. The bytes themselves are **snapshotted into Supabase Storage at Phase 2 (auto-apply) or Apply (staged) time** — not at parse time. This preserves the live-vs-staged snapshot boundary: the crew page for the currently-approved snapshot serves images from the storage path baked at the last successful Apply, never from live Drive state. If Doug edits an image while a stage is pending, the live crew page continues to show the previously-approved bytes. Specifically:

   **Storage layout.** A private Supabase Storage bucket `diagram-snapshots`. Bucket-level policies forbid all anonymous and end-user-session access; only the service role reads/writes. Storage object keys use a per-apply **immutable revision id**, NOT the modifiedTime, because manual/recovery applies are explicitly allowed to replay the same modtime (§5.2). Each successful Phase 2 / Apply mints a fresh `snapshot_revision_id` UUID written into `sync_audit` and into `shows.diagrams.snapshot_revision_id`; storage keys are `shows/<show_id>/<snapshot_revision_id>/<objectId>.<ext>`. Two applies of the same Drive `modifiedTime` get distinct revisions, distinct keys, distinct objects.

   **Linked-folder enumeration freezes at Phase 1 (parse / stage) with the immutable pin tuple, not at Apply.** If we waited until Apply to enumerate the folder, additions/removals between stage and Apply would silently change what Doug actually published. Phase 1 enumerates the folder via `files.list` with `fields='files(id,name,mimeType,modifiedTime,headRevisionId,md5Checksum,trashed)'` and captures the **immutable approval tuple** `(driveFileId, mimeType, alt, drive_modified_time, headRevisionId, md5Checksum)` per item, recorded in `parseResult.diagrams.linkedFolderItems`. `headRevisionId` + `md5Checksum` are the authoritative byte-fence — `drive_modified_time` is informational because Drive can mutate bytes within a metadata read → byte fetch window. Apply downloads either via `revisions.get(fileId, headRevisionId, alt='media')` (preferred, exact bytes) or via `alt=media` followed by buffer-then-verify against `md5Checksum`. Folder content changes between stage and Apply do NOT propagate. If a frozen tuple's file is gone at Apply time (404/unshared/trashed) OR drift is detected, it's preserved with `snapshotPath: null` and contributes to `snapshot_status = 'partial_failure'`.

   **Embedded-image freeze with content-derived fingerprint.** Embedded images on the DIAGRAMS tab carry their own immutable approval pair: `sheetsRevisionId` (captured via `drive.revisions.list(spreadsheetId)` — the spreadsheet's head revision id at extraction time, since the Sheets API does not expose this directly) AND `embeddedFingerprint` — **canonically `base64url(SHA-256(<full image bytes from GET image.contentUrl>))`**. NOT an HTTP ETag (server-controlled, proxies/CDNs can rotate without bytes changing). NOT a HEAD-derived token (HEAD doesn't supply the bytes). NOT a positional/id hash (an in-place image replacement preserves objectId + position). The same SHA-256-of-bytes helper runs at Phase-1 enrichment, at Apply re-verify, and at asset_recovery re-verify — three call sites, byte-stable hash, equal inputs produce equal outputs. If `image.contentUrl` is absent or returns 4xx at extraction time, `embeddedFingerprint` is set to `null` AND that entry is **restage-only**: Apply MUST fail closed (no download) and `asset_recovery` MUST exclude that entry from retry. A fresh sheet edit re-mints `sheetsRevisionId` + `embeddedFingerprint` and the snapshot is re-attempted then.

   **Combined cap upstream of persistence.** `MAX_TOTAL_DIAGRAM_ITEMS = 60` is a budget across BOTH `embeddedImages` AND `linkedFolderItems`. The cap is enforced during Phase 1 enrichment (Task 7.1 reserves up to N for embedded; Task 7.2 consumes the residual budget for linked). Items 61+ MUST NOT be persisted — otherwise hidden overflow can drift / 404 / wedge `snapshot_status='partial_failure'` even though the gallery never emits a URL for them.

   **Per-apply snapshotting flow** (covers BOTH embedded images AND the frozen linked-folder set so the live page never reaches into Drive at view time). **Commit-aware snapshot writes with 3-state lifecycle + all-or-nothing promotion**: every Storage byte upload during Apply targets a per-run **temp prefix** `diagram-snapshots/shows/<show_id>/_pending/<run_uuid>/<asset_key>` (NOT the final `<snapshot_revision_id>/` prefix). **Ledger grain is one row per Apply attempt (NOT one row per asset)**. The Apply inserts EXACTLY ONE row into `pending_snapshot_uploads (show_id, drive_file_id, temp_prefix, snapshot_revision_id, asset_count, uploaded_at, promoted_at, claim_token, claimed_at, claim_expires_at, delete_started_at)` at temp-prefix-allocation time, inside the SAME Phase-2 DB transaction as the eventual `shows.diagrams` UPDATE — so DB rollback unwinds the ledger row alongside the (orphaned) Storage bytes. Asset-level tracking is implicit via Storage `LIST` of the `temp_prefix`; `asset_count` is the **manifest contract** for the all-or-nothing promotion check below. Both `temp_prefix` and `snapshot_revision_id` are unique-per-Apply (DB UNIQUE constraints).

   **3-state lifecycle (CRITICAL — a CAS-after-delete protocol that deletes Storage bytes BEFORE the CAS DELETE detects lost ownership would let a revived GC worker after claim expiry destroy bytes already promoted)**: every ledger row is in exactly one of three states, transitioned via atomic UPDATEs with WHERE-clause state guards:
   - **(a) `unclaimed`**: `claim_token IS NULL AND claimed_at IS NULL AND claim_expires_at IS NULL AND delete_started_at IS NULL`. Initial state on INSERT; also the state a row returns to when a non-destructive worker releases its claim.
   - **(b) `claimed`**: `claim_token IS NOT NULL AND claimed_at IS NOT NULL AND claim_expires_at = claimed_at + interval '5 minutes' AND delete_started_at IS NULL`. A worker has exclusive ownership for non-destructive work (rename retry, sweep evaluation). The 5-minute lease can be extended via heartbeat for long-running work.
   - **(c) `committing_delete`**: `claim_token IS NOT NULL AND claimed_at IS NOT NULL AND delete_started_at IS NOT NULL AND claim_expires_at = delete_started_at + interval '15 minutes'`. The worker has atomically committed to deletion; reclaim-expired refuses to touch this row. ONLY a row in this state may have its Storage bytes deleted.

   **State transitions** (each is a single UPDATE returning the row count; 0 rows = lost ownership, abort):
   - **claim** (unclaimed → claimed): `UPDATE pending_snapshot_uploads SET claim_token = $newToken, claimed_at = now(), claim_expires_at = now() + interval '5 minutes' WHERE id = $id AND claim_token IS NULL AND delete_started_at IS NULL RETURNING *`.
   - **heartbeat** (claimed → claimed, lease extended): `UPDATE pending_snapshot_uploads SET claim_expires_at = now() + interval '5 minutes' WHERE id = $id AND claim_token = $token AND delete_started_at IS NULL RETURNING *`. Workers MUST heartbeat every < 5 minutes for long-running work.
   - **reclaim-expired** (stale claimed → fresh claimed): `UPDATE pending_snapshot_uploads SET claim_token = $newToken, claimed_at = now(), claim_expires_at = now() + interval '5 minutes' WHERE id = $id AND claim_expires_at < now() AND delete_started_at IS NULL RETURNING *`. The `delete_started_at IS NULL` guard is critical: reclaim REFUSES to take a row away from a worker that has committed to delete, even if its `claim_expires_at` slipped (clock skew).
   - **commit-to-delete** (claimed → committing_delete): `UPDATE pending_snapshot_uploads SET delete_started_at = now(), claim_expires_at = now() + interval '15 minutes' WHERE id = $id AND claim_token = $token AND promoted_at IS NULL AND delete_started_at IS NULL RETURNING *`. Atomically transitions to delete state IF still owner AND not promoted; 0 rows = lost ownership (someone promoted, deleted, or reclaimed concurrently), abort BEFORE touching Storage. **THIS is the gate that protects bytes — Storage DELETE runs ONLY after this UPDATE returns 1 row.**
   - **delete** (committing_delete → row gone): AFTER commit-to-delete returns 1 row, perform Storage DELETE under the temp prefix; then `DELETE FROM pending_snapshot_uploads WHERE id = $id AND claim_token = $token`. The post-Storage row delete is now safe — no other worker can touch a row with `delete_started_at IS NOT NULL` because reclaim refuses, promote refuses, and re-claim refuses.
   - **promote** (claimed → promoted): the post-commit promoter (or a GC re-attempt) runs the all-or-nothing rename per the next paragraph, then `UPDATE pending_snapshot_uploads SET promoted_at = now(), claim_token = NULL, claimed_at = NULL, claim_expires_at = NULL WHERE id = $id AND claim_token = $token AND delete_started_at IS NULL RETURNING *`. The `delete_started_at IS NULL` guard ensures a row mid-delete cannot be promoted — symmetric to reclaim's guard.

   **All-or-nothing promotion with manifest verification (HIGH)**: the post-commit promoter / GC re-attempt MUST treat the canonical prefix as either fully populated or empty — a partial canonical gallery (some assets renamed, others missing) MUST NOT become live. The contract includes a per-show promotion lock with a CAS predicate on rollback, and decouples promotion from the Apply HTTP response. **Async promotion contract**: the Apply HTTP route DOES NOT block on the post-commit promoter. After the Phase-2 DB transaction commits (writing the `pending` sub-payload + ledger row), the route returns `202 Accepted` immediately with `{ status: 'apply_committed_pending_promote', apply_id, snapshot_revision_id }` — the operator's client polls the idempotent status endpoint described below to learn the promotion outcome. Without decoupling, Apply B that lands while Apply A's promoter holds the `promote:` advisory lock would block the HTTP request behind A's full Storage rename + manifest verify (potentially many seconds). If B's client times out / disconnects mid-block, the promoter's outcome is ambiguous to the operator: did B's `pending` sub-payload land? Did promotion succeed or rollback? With the async split, NO state mutation is lost — B's Phase-2 commit happened before the 202 was sent; the promoter runs to completion in the background regardless of client connectivity. **Background worker contract**: the route fires-and-forgets a per-request worker (Next.js route's `waitUntil` / Vercel background function / equivalent) that acquires the `promote:` lock (BLOCKING — queues behind in-flight promoters for the same show) and runs the (P0)–(P5) promotion protocol. **Idempotent status endpoint** (new in §7.3): `GET /api/admin/show/[slug]/apply/[applyId]/status` — admin-authenticated; returns `{ status: 'pending' | 'promoted' | 'rolled_back' | 'stuck_admin_repair_required', snapshot_revision_id, ledger_row_id, diagnostics? }` derived from the live `pending_snapshot_uploads` row state. Status mapping: `promoted_at IS NOT NULL` → `'promoted'`; `(diagrams->'pending'->>'revision_id')::uuid != $applyId AND promoted_at IS NULL` → `'rolled_back'` (the rollback cleared my staging slot); `promote_started_at >= now() - interval '15 minutes' AND promoted_at IS NULL AND (diagrams->'pending'->>'revision_id')::uuid = $applyId` → `'pending'` (still in flight under the healthy promotion window); `promote_started_at < now() - interval '15 minutes' AND promoted_at IS NULL` → `'stuck_admin_repair_required'` (the admin-only `/api/admin/snapshot-rollback/[id]/repair` endpoint resolves this). The status endpoint does NOT trigger any work — pure read. The operator UI polls with backoff (e.g., 1s → 2s → 5s, capped at 10s) until status leaves `'pending'`. If the client times out / disconnects between Apply 202 and final status, the operator can resume polling at any time — the `apply_id` is the ledger row's `snapshot_revision_id`. **`APPLY_PROMOTE_PENDING`** is the admin-log entry the route emits when it returns 202; the status endpoint emits no admin log per poll (would spam the log). Protocol:
   - **(P0) Per-show promotion lock (CRITICAL — closes the same-show concurrent-Apply race)** — the Phase-2 Apply advisory lock keyed `show:` is released at DB commit, BEFORE any Storage rename runs; without an additional serialization layer, two parallel Applies for the same show could commit `pending_revision_id = R1` then `pending_revision_id = R2` back-to-back, and A's rollback path could clear B's just-staged JSONB slot or reverse-rename bytes that already promoted under B. The promoter MUST acquire a separate per-show advisory lock keyed `promote:` BEFORE any Storage I/O: `pg_advisory_xact_lock(hashtext('promote:' || $showId))` (blocking, NOT try-variant — promoters for the same show queue rather than racing). The promotion lock is held for the entire (P1)–(P5) window — across manifest pre-flight, forward rename, post-check, atomic JSONB cutover, OR reverse-rename rollback — and auto-releases at the enclosing DB transaction boundary (commit OR rollback). When a promoter for a NEWER Apply (R2) arrives while an OLDER Apply's promoter (R1) is mid-promote, the new promoter BLOCKS on the lock until the old promoter finishes; on lock acquisition the new promoter re-reads `shows.diagrams->'pending'->>'revision_id'` (which now belongs to itself — the older promoter has either advanced `current ← pending` (lifting R1 into `current` and clearing `pending` to NULL), OR rolled back and cleared `pending` to NULL; either way the slot is now NULL or holds R2's pending sub-payload) and proceeds. The CAS predicates inside (P4) and (P5) are defense-in-depth against misimplemented lock patterns.
   - **(P1) Manifest pre-flight** — Storage `LIST` the temp prefix `diagram-snapshots/shows/<show_id>/_pending/<run_uuid>/`. Record the enumerated `(asset_key, size)` tuples; assert `count(enumerated) === asset_count` from the ledger. If mismatch → ABORT promotion (the temp prefix itself is incomplete; wait for the next sweep).
   - **(P2) Forward rename** — for each enumerated asset, Storage rename `<temp_prefix><asset_key>` → `<canonical_prefix><asset_key>` where `<canonical_prefix> = diagram-snapshots/shows/<show_id>/<snapshot_revision_id>/`. Track the running set of successfully renamed `asset_key` entries.
   - **(P3) Manifest post-check** — after all renames complete, Storage `LIST` the canonical prefix; assert `count(canonical) === asset_count` AND every enumerated asset_key from (P1) is present. If pass: proceed to (P4). Otherwise: ROLLBACK via (P5).
   - **(P4) Promote** — run the **promote** state transition above. ONLY when this UPDATE returns 1 row, ALSO run the **atomic JSONB cutover** that advances the canonical revision. The cutover copies the entire `pending` sub-payload over `current` (NOT just the revision id), so the new manifest entries, snapshotPaths, embeddedFingerprints, snapshot_status, and revision id all become live in one atomic write — no broken pairing of OLD revision id with NEW manifest is possible: `UPDATE shows SET diagrams = jsonb_set(jsonb_set(diagrams, '{current}', diagrams->'pending'), '{pending}', 'null'::jsonb) WHERE drive_file_id = $1 AND (diagrams->'pending'->>'revision_id')::uuid = $newRevId` in the same DB transaction as the promote-state-transition UPDATE. The CAS predicate uses `pending->>'revision_id'` (the new sub-payload's revision id field). After the JSONB cutover commits, the `current.snapshot_revision_id` (lifted from `pending.revision_id`) becomes live; clear `promote_started_at` (set to NULL); `promoted_at` is set; the canonical gallery is now authoritative. There is no `shows.pending_snapshot_path` column; the `pending` JSONB sub-payload is the cutover staging slot, and the asset route never reads it.
   - **(P5) Rollback (any individual rename failure in P2 OR manifest mismatch in P3)** — for each successfully renamed `asset_key` in the running set, reverse-rename `<canonical_prefix><asset_key>` → `<temp_prefix><asset_key>`. Do NOT advance the JSONB cutover; do NOT set `promoted_at`. Then clear ONLY my own `pending` sub-payload so a future Apply can stage a fresh one without colliding: `UPDATE shows SET diagrams = jsonb_set(diagrams, '{pending}', 'null'::jsonb) WHERE drive_file_id = $1 AND (diagrams->'pending'->>'revision_id')::uuid = $newRevId`. The `(diagrams->'pending'->>'revision_id')::uuid = $newRevId` CAS predicate is a byte-protection invariant adapted to the sub-payload split: under the (P0) promotion lock the slot should always still hold my revision when I rollback, but the CAS is defense-in-depth against misimplemented lock patterns — without it, A's rollback would orphan B's just-staged `pending` sub-payload if the lock pattern were skipped. **Critically `current` is NEVER touched during rollback** — only the `pending` key is cleared, so the prior approved revision's manifest, snapshotPaths, snapshot_revision_id, and snapshot_status keep serving verbatim. Clear `promote_started_at` (set to NULL) and release the claim (heartbeat with `claim_expires_at = now()` so the next sweep can re-claim). The canonical prefix MUST be empty post-rollback so a subsequent GC observing it knows nothing was promoted, and `shows.diagrams.current.snapshot_revision_id` still points at the prior approved revision (which has kept serving uninterrupted throughout). **(P5-stuck) Reverse-rename failure contract** — if the reverse-rename ITSELF fails mid-flight (some assets reverse-renamed back to temp, then a subsequent reverse-rename returns 5xx / network failure), the row is left in a split-prefix state with assets straddling temp + canonical. In this case the promoter MUST: (a) NOT clear `promote_started_at` (the row stays non-reclaimable to the GC sweep); (b) NOT clear `pending_revision_id` (so the admin repair flow can identify which revision was being promoted); (c) NOT release the claim; (d) emit an `admin_alerts` row coded `PENDING_SNAPSHOT_ROLLBACK_STUCK` with `(row_id, snapshot_revision_id, assets_reverted[], assets_still_canonical[])` so Eric sees the stuck state. The reclaim-expired GC sweep refuses to act on rows with `promote_started_at IS NOT NULL`, so a stuck-rollback row is invisible to automated reclamation. Recovery is admin-only: the operator runs `/api/admin/snapshot-rollback/[id]/repair` (admin-authenticated POST). **The repair endpoint MUST gate on PROVEN-stuck state**: (a) reject with 409 if `promote_started_at IS NULL`; (b) reject with 409 if `promote_started_at >= now() - interval '15 minutes'` (still inside the healthy promotion window — could be a slow-but-legitimate promoter); (c) MUST acquire the same `promote:` advisory lock the post-commit promoter uses (`pg_advisory_xact_lock(hashtext('promote:' || show_id))`, BLOCKING) so a healthy promoter mid-rename is queued behind, NOT raced; (d) after acquiring the lock, MUST re-read the row state — if `promote_started_at IS NULL` (the prior promoter cleared it on success) return 200 `{ status: 'no_repair_needed' }` (idempotent), if `promoted_at IS NOT NULL` return 200 `{ status: 'already_promoted' }`, only proceed when the row is genuinely stuck (`promote_started_at < now() - interval '15 minutes' AND promoted_at IS NULL`). Then the route LISTs both the canonical and temp prefixes, computes the union manifest, decides per-asset which prefix is authoritative based on the rename audit log, performs final reverse-renames of remaining canonical-side assets, then clears `promote_started_at`, clears `pending_revision_id` from the JSONB, and releases the claim. Once `promote_started_at` is NULL again, the GC sweep can route the row through (iv-a) RENAME-RETRY or (iv-b) DELETE-ORPHAN normally.

   **GC observing a partial canonical prefix** (post-rollback or after an orphan from a prior crash): the canonical prefix exists with some bytes BUT `shows.diagrams.snapshot_revision_id` was never updated to this revision (because (P4) never ran). The GC deletes the canonical prefix entirely — the prior revision stays authoritative since `shows.diagrams.snapshot_revision_id` still points there. **No partial gallery is ever live.** **Stuck-rollback inhibition**: the GC orphan-blob sweep AND the reclaim-expired pass MUST both refuse to act on `pending_snapshot_uploads` rows with `promote_started_at IS NOT NULL` (i.e., still in a non-reclaimable promotion state, including the stuck-rollback case where reverse-rename failed mid-flight). Acting on these rows would race the admin repair flow OR delete bytes that the admin repair routine intends to reverse-rename back to temp. The orphan-blob sweep specifically MUST NOT delete blobs whose `<revision_id>` segment matches the `pending_revision_id` of any row whose `promote_started_at IS NOT NULL` — those bytes are mid-rollback and the admin repair flow will reconcile them.

   **Phase-2 abort path**: temp-prefix blobs remain orphan; ledger row still carries `promoted_at IS NULL` AND `delete_started_at IS NULL`. The §6.11 GC sweep walks the 3-state lifecycle to safely reclaim these orphans without racing a concurrent promoter or a revived-after-expiry worker — see plan Task 7.3 / Task 7.8 for the regression tests covering abort-after-upload, promote-on-commit, rename-failure recovery, the GC sweep paths, the three race regressions, AND the two reclaim regressions (revived-worker-after-expiry-vs-committing-delete; partial-canonical-rollback-via-reverse-rename).
   - Generate `snapshot_revision_id = gen_random_uuid()` AND `run_uuid = gen_random_uuid()` (the temp-prefix discriminator).
   - For each entry in `parse_result.diagrams.embeddedImages[]` (full immutable-pin re-verify under the per-show advisory lock; mirrors plan Task 7.3. Drift detection happens BEFORE any byte fetch):
     - **Restage-only short-circuit**: if the entry's `recovery_disposition = 'restage_required'` (set when `embeddedFingerprint` was null at extraction time), Apply does NOT download. Leave `snapshotPath = null`, mark `snapshot_status = 'partial_failure'`, and exclude the entry from any retry path. The entry converges only when a fresh sheet edit re-mints `sheetsRevisionId` + `embeddedFingerprint` via Phase 2.
     - **Re-fetch the spreadsheet head revision via `drive.revisions.list(spreadsheetId)` UNDER THE LOCK** and compare the latest `revision.id` to the entry's stored `sheetsRevisionId`.
     - **Re-run `spreadsheets.get`** to verify the entry's `objectId` is still present on the DIAGRAMS tab AND the entry's stored `embeddedFingerprint` matches the live content-derived token.
     - **All three checks must pass** (revision unchanged AND objectId present AND fingerprint matches) before any byte download. Drift in any of the three → leave `snapshotPath = null`, mark `snapshot_status = 'partial_failure'`, AND emit `EMBEDDED_ASSET_DRIFTED` warning. No bytes are fetched in the drift case.
     - On verified-pin match: download bytes → upload to `diagram-snapshots/shows/<show_id>/<snapshot_revision_id>/embedded-<objectId>.<ext>` → set `snapshotPath` to that path.
   - For each entry in `parse_result.diagrams.linkedFolderItems[]` (the frozen set from Phase 1):
     - **Immutable-revision download (fail-closed):** Pattern A — `revisions.get(driveFileId, headRevisionId, alt='media')` downloads the exact bytes the freeze tuple pinned regardless of current head; 404 from Drive at this call indicates the revision was deleted (drift case). Pattern B — `files.get(alt='media')` then recompute md5 of the streamed bytes; if computed md5 ≠ `md5Checksum`, discard the bytes and treat as drift. **Never use `(modifiedTime, trashed)` as the fence — it has a TOCTOU window.** On drift in either pattern: leave `snapshotPath = null` AND mark `snapshot_status = 'partial_failure'` AND emit `LINKED_ASSET_DRIFTED` warning. asset_recovery follows the same revision-pinned download path.
     - On verified-pin match: upload bytes to `diagram-snapshots/shows/<show_id>/<snapshot_revision_id>/folder-<driveFileId>.<ext>` and set `snapshotPath`.
     - On any failure: leave `snapshotPath = null` and mark `snapshot_status = 'partial_failure'`.
   - Phase 2's UPDATE on `shows` writes the new `diagrams` JSONB with all per-entry `snapshotPath` values, the frozen `linkedFolderItems[]` (with snapshotPaths populated), the top-level `snapshot_revision_id`, and `snapshot_status`. **No source type is exempt from snapshotting**; the previous "linked-folder live-fetch" path is replaced.

   **Partial-failure retry path.** Two terminal sub-states exist:
   - `snapshot_status = 'partial_failure'` — at least one entry has `snapshotPath = NULL` AND at least one such null entry has `recovery_disposition = 'normal'` (retryable). **Auto-syncs (cron, push) IGNORE the watermark gate for this show** and keep re-attempting the retryable failed snapshots without waiting for Doug to edit the sheet. On each retry pass: re-attempt only the entries whose `snapshotPath IS NULL` AND `recovery_disposition = 'normal'`. Successful retries fill the path. Once every entry has a non-null `snapshotPath`, flip `snapshot_status` to `'complete'`; subsequent auto-syncs return to normal watermark behavior.
   - `snapshot_status = 'partial_failure_restage_required'` — at least one entry has `snapshotPath = NULL` AND every remaining null entry has `recovery_disposition = 'restage_required'` (no retryable nulls left). **Cron SKIPS this show — does NOT route into asset_recovery and does NOT advance any retry counter.** A null-fingerprint entry cannot be healed by re-downloading; only a fresh sheet edit can re-mint `sheetsRevisionId` + `embeddedFingerprint`, which advances `modifiedTime`, fires Phase 2, and either resolves the entry or keeps it stuck (still detectable via the same gate). The `EMBEDDED_RECOVERY_REQUIRES_RESTAGE` admin alert is raised so Doug sees the stuck state.
