   - **Crucially, the prior snapshot's bytes are NOT immediately deleted.** Until `snapshot_status = 'complete'`, the diagram GC (below) suppresses deletion of the prior revision's blobs — so on the gallery, the missing image renders the placeholder per AC-7.7, but at least one consistent revision still has all bytes available for forensic recovery if needed.
   - This means a transient Drive/Storage failure can never permanently degrade the live view, because retries continue automatically rather than being gated by file modtime.

   **Service endpoint** is the revision-versioned `/api/asset/diagram/<show>/<snapshot_revision_id>/<assetKey>` per §7.3 routing. Auth + cache contract is documented there in full; the canonical bullet is `Cache-Control: private, max-age=0, must-revalidate` so each fetch re-authenticates with the server (revocation propagates immediately). Drive is never called at request time. The crew page emits URLs at render time using the current `shows.diagrams.snapshot_revision_id`; prior-revision URLs return 410 and naturally fall out of use.

   **Diagram garbage collection cron** (`30 * * * *`, hourly, offset to avoid collisions):
   - For each `(show_id)` in `shows`, list its `diagram-snapshots/shows/<show_id>/` prefix.
   - For each blob whose `<revision_id>` segment does NOT match the current `shows.diagrams.snapshot_revision_id`: it's an orphan from a prior revision.
   - Delete orphan blobs older than **7 days** (grace window for in-flight reads + forensic recovery). Suppress deletion if the current revision has `snapshot_status = 'partial_failure'` OR `snapshot_status = 'partial_failure_restage_required'` — both states leave the prior complete revision as the only consistent fallback while the current revision is intentionally incomplete; deleting prior-revision bytes would produce a user-visible asset-loss path. The terminal-restage variant is a stuck-waiting-for-sheet-edit state, NOT a recovered state, so GC suppression must extend to it for the same reason.
   - For shows whose row is `archived = true`: orphan deletion runs at 30 days instead of 7.

4. Linked-folder diagrams (older sheets where the DIAGRAMS tab carries `LINK` to an external Drive folder) populate `parseResult.diagrams.linkedFolder` instead.
5. A sheet may have both: e.g., a few embedded photos on the DIAGRAMS tab AND a linked folder for additional layouts. The UI in §10 renders both sources merged into one gallery in the Diagrams tile.

**Soft warnings (not hard fails):**

- `DIAGRAMS_EMBEDDED_OBJECT_INACCESSIBLE` — the API returned a description of an embedded image but the download URL 4xx'd (rare, but possible if the image was inserted via a service the service account can't read). The objectId is preserved with a flag and the gallery renders a placeholder slot.
- `DIAGRAMS_TAB_MISSING` — the sheet has no tab matching `DIAGRAMS` (case-insensitive, includes typo `DIagrams` per the schema-diff). `embeddedImages: []`. Linked-folder source still extracted from the markdown export if present.

No MI invariant gates destructive write on diagrams content because absence is normal (most fixtures don't have any embedded images at all).

**Cardinality cap:** the DIAGRAMS tab realistically holds ≤10 images per the FinTech Forum example. v1 caps `embeddedImages.length` at 60 to prevent an absurd sheet from blowing up storage; beyond 60, surface a `DIAGRAMS_EMBEDDED_CAP_EXCEEDED` warning to admin and truncate.

#### 6.11.1 Apply-time reel drift re-verify (full immutable pin tuple)

The reel pin captured at Phase 1 carries the full immutable tuple `parseResult.openingReel = { driveFileId, drive_modified_time, headRevisionId, mimeType }` — a four-field tuple matching the four `shows.opening_reel_*` columns. Apply MUST re-verify the immutable components before persisting into `shows.opening_reel_drive_file_id`, `shows.opening_reel_drive_modified_time`, `shows.opening_reel_head_revision_id`, AND `shows.opening_reel_mime_type` (all four columns per §4.1):

1. **Null reel staged** — if `parseResult.openingReel === null` → set ALL FOUR `shows.opening_reel_*` columns to NULL atomically. No Drive call needed.
2. **Re-fetch under the lock** — if `parseResult.openingReel !== null`, call `files.get(parseResult.openingReel.driveFileId, fields='mimeType,modifiedTime,trashed,headRevisionId,md5Checksum')`.
3. **Pinned-tuple comparison** — drift case if ANY of:
   - `trashed = true` OR file gone (404), OR
   - reel revoked / private / permission-denied (403 / `permissionDenied` / equivalent), OR
   - `current.headRevisionId !== staged.headRevisionId` (authoritative immutable check), OR
   - `current.modifiedTime !== staged.drive_modified_time` (defense-in-depth — revision check above is the primary fence), OR
   - `!current.mimeType.startsWith('video/')` (MIME re-verify — covers the case where the operator replaced the same Drive URL with a non-video file between stage and Apply; matches the OPENING_REEL_NOT_VIDEO contract).

   On drift: persist ALL FOUR columns as NULL atomically (not just two or three), emit `REEL_DRIFTED` warning to `parse_warnings` for trashed / 404 / revision / modtime cases, emit `OPENING_REEL_PERMISSION_DENIED` (§12.4) for 403 cases, emit `OPENING_REEL_NOT_VIDEO` for MIME-mismatch cases. Continue Phase 2. Crew page falls back to text-only opening_reel value; the asset route returns 410 if hit.

4. **Success path** — pin tuple matches AND mimeType is video: persist the full quadruple `(driveFileId, drive_modified_time, headRevisionId, mimeType)` into the four columns atomically. The route at §7.3 (`/api/asset/reel/[show]`) streams bytes via `revisions.get(fileId, headRevisionId, alt='media')` on every request — `headRevisionId` is the immutable byte-fence, NOT modtime alone.

This guards the same class of bug the linked-folder revision-pin closes: an asset edited between stage and Apply must NEVER produce an "approved but immediately broken" state on the live page, AND the route must never serve drifted bytes against the approved revision pin.

---

## 7. Auth model

### 7.1 Identities

- **Crew member (FXAV staff)** — has email in sheet (required field 2025-06+). Signs in with Google **or** uses a signed link Doug shared with them. Both paths resolve to a row in `crew_members`.
- **Doug (the PM)** — admin role, Google login. Email pre-allowlisted (`dlarson@fxav.net`).
- **Eric (the developer / operator)** — admin role, Google login. Email pre-allowlisted (`edweiss412@gmail.com`).

**Out of scope for v1: external stakeholders** (non-FXAV drivers like James Wells from `2025-03-dci-rpas-central.md`, client contacts, in-house AV, vendor reps). They are not modeled as identities in v1 — there is no signed-link or login path that recognizes them. Doug continues to share documentation with these people through email/text the way he does today. This is intentional: the v1 auth/data model assumes every viewer is either an admin or a row in `crew_members`. Adding a separate `external_viewers` table with its own issuance, revocation, and rendering rules is a v2 candidate (§16.2). The "driver, client contact" framing from earlier brainstorm rounds was retired during adversarial review when the auth flow couldn't represent it without leaking pseudo-rows into crew-facing UI.

### 7.2 Signed link format

```
crew.fxav.show/show/<slug>/p#t=<jwt>
```

**The JWT lives in the URL fragment, never the query string.** This is non-negotiable. Fragments are never sent in `Referer` headers, never logged by Vercel/Drive/CDN access logs, and never indexed in browser address-bar history search the way query strings can be. Since the page embeds external content (Drive PDFs, diagram images, optional opening-reel video), a token in `?t=` would leak to those origins via `Referer` even before any explicit mitigation.

**First-load bootstrap exchange:**

1. Doug shares `https://crew.fxav.show/show/dci-rpas-2026/p#t=<jwt>` with the crew member.
2. Browser navigates; `/show/<slug>/p` server-renders a minimal bootstrap shell (no PII, no role-gated data) that includes a small client-side script.
3. The bootstrap script reads `location.hash`, POSTs the token to `/api/auth/redeem-link` with `credentials: same-origin`. **The POST MUST originate same-origin.** The server enforces this with TWO independent checks before the per-request authz flow runs:
   - **Origin/Sec-Fetch check.** The route REJECTS any request whose `Sec-Fetch-Site` header is not `same-origin`, OR (when `Sec-Fetch-Site` is absent — pre-Fetch-Metadata browsers) whose `Origin` header is not equal to the site's canonical origin (`https://crew.fxav.show`). Cross-site or null-origin requests get **403 with §12.4 code `CSRF_DENIED`**. **Why both:** `SameSite=Lax` does NOT prevent login-CSRF — it only constrains _existing_ cookies. An attacker can force a victim's browser to POST a JWT they (the attacker) control to `/api/auth/redeem-link` via a hidden cross-origin form, mint a `__Host-fxav_session` cookie bound to the attacker's identity, and then trick the victim into viewing data through that cookie. Origin pinning is the standard defense for state-changing endpoints that mint cookies.
   - **Bootstrap nonce (multi-instance + show-bound; signing-key-id pinned for rotation discrimination).** Server-rendering of `/show/<slug>/p` mints a one-time bootstrap nonce — a 128-bit random value scoped to that specific show. Each render INSERTs a row into `bootstrap_nonces (nonce_hash, show_id, issued_at, signing_key_id)` (composite PK on `(nonce_hash, show_id)` per §4.1; `signing_key_id` is captured atomically from `app_settings.active_signing_key_id` in the same INSERT, mirroring the read-with-INSERT pattern that `link_sessions.signing_key_id` uses) AND APPENDS an entry `{ nonce_hash, show_id, issued_at, signing_key_id }` to a short-lived (30-second) signed cookie `__Host-fxav_bootstrap_v` whose value is a JSON-encoded ARRAY of recent nonce entries (cap at 5 most-recent — evict oldest). The cookie envelope's `signing_key_id` field carries the same kid the bootstrap shell signed the cookie under; the redeem-link route compares the cookie envelope's kid against `app_settings.active_signing_key_id` AT REDEEM TIME and against the row's `signing_key_id` AT THE SAME TIME to discriminate three branches: (i) cookie kid matches NO row in `bootstrap_nonces` for this `(nonce_hash, show_id)` → `CSRF_DENIED` (forgery / tampering); (ii) cookie kid = row kid AND cookie kid = active kid → proceed with normal nonce evaluation; (iii) cookie kid = row kid AND cookie kid ≠ active kid → `CSRF_KEY_ROTATED` (benign §7.2.3 rotation race; transient — same recovery as `CSRF_NONCE_EXPIRED`). The same nonce value is also embedded in the bootstrap shell HTML so the client-side script can echo it back in the redeem-link POST body alongside the show context. The redeem-link route consumes by the COMPOSITE key: it verifies the body's `(nonce, show_id)` matches a non-consumed row in `bootstrap_nonces` AND that the cookie array contains a matching `(nonce_hash, show_id)` entry; consumption uses `UPDATE bootstrap_nonces SET consumed_at = now() WHERE nonce_hash = $1 AND show_id = $2 AND consumed_at IS NULL RETURNING nonce_hash`. **Outcome routing per AC-5.13's `CSRF_DENIED` vs `CSRF_NONCE_EXPIRED` producer matrix**: missing-row / replay (already-consumed) / body-cookie nonce_hash mismatch / wrong-show-id (attacker swap) → **403 `CSRF_DENIED`**; benign age-eviction (otherwise-valid nonce >30s past `issued_at`, OR cookie-array entry age-evicted while the underlying row is otherwise valid) → **403 `CSRF_NONCE_EXPIRED`** (so the surface can render a friendly "refresh and click again" UX instead of the generic CSRF failure). **Why the array + composite key:** earlier draft used a single-slot cookie (`__Host-fxav_bootstrap`) and a single-PK table — a second render of `/show/<slug>/p` (same browser, second tab; or different show in another tab) clobbered the first cookie slot, so the first tab's redeem POST 403'd even though it carried a valid nonce. The array-cookie + composite-PK design lets multiple live nonces coexist (multi-tab same-show; multi-show same-browser) so each tab's own nonce is independently valid and consumable. **Required regression tests:** (a) two tabs of `/show/<slug>/p` open back-to-back → both mints succeed, both rows live, both redeems succeed (each consumes its own nonce); (b) `/show/A/p` and `/show/B/p` open in same browser → both bootstrap rows live, A redeems first, A's nonce consumed, B's nonce still valid and redeemable. The bootstrap nonce ensures even a same-origin replay (e.g., a malicious browser extension that happens to read the same origin) cannot mint a session cookie without first having loaded the bootstrap page server-rendering as the victim.

   On success: sets an HTTP-only `__Host-fxav_session` cookie carrying the URL-encoded JSON envelope `{ v: 1, token, show_id }` (single host-wide cookie; show-binding lives in the JSON value, NOT in the cookie name; the `v: 1` envelope-version field is canonical and MANDATORY on every mint, matching the decoder's `v === 1` strict-equality gate), 15-minute idle TTL refreshed on activity, and returns `200 OK` with the matched `crew_member.id`.

4. The bootstrap script calls `history.replaceState(null, '', location.pathname)` to strip the fragment from the URL bar, then reloads the route as `/show/<slug>` — the cookie is now the credential and the JWT is no longer in any URL.
5. All subsequent requests in the session use the cookie. Page response carries `Referrer-Policy: no-referrer` so any future external-asset loads don't leak even cookie-free URLs.

**Cookie semantics (single host-wide cookie with show-id-bound JSON payload):**

- **Single host-wide cookie:** the cookie name is the literal `__Host-fxav_session` (no show suffix). Per-show NAMING (`__Host-fxav_session_<slug>`) is rejected because browsers index cookies by `(domain, path)` and send EVERY cookie whose `(domain, path)` scope matches the request. Under `__Host-` (which mandates `Path=/`), every `__Host-fxav_session_<slug>` cookie on the same host attaches to every same-host request regardless of name. With many shows over a long-lived browser, the Cookie request header grows linearly until the browser/server cap is hit (typical 8 KB / `400 Request Header Fields Too Large` / `431` outcomes). Per-show naming therefore offers ZERO client-side isolation while introducing an unbounded-cookie-header DOS vector. A single cookie eliminates the growth.
- HTTP-only, `Secure`, `SameSite=Lax`, `__Host-` prefix; `Path=/` is mandatory under the `__Host-` prefix. There is exactly ONE `__Host-fxav_session` cookie on the host at any time.
- **Cookie value is a JSON-encoded `{ v: 1, token, show_id }` envelope (URL-encoded into the `Set-Cookie` value), NOT the JWT.** `v` is the envelope version — currently exactly `1`; `token` is the random opaque server-side session token; `show_id` is the UUID of the show this session was minted for. The `link_sessions` row lookup still happens by `token`, but the validator additionally checks that the cookie's decoded `show_id` matches both the URL's show AND the row's `show_id` column. Storing `show_id` IN the cookie payload is what enables the §7.2.2 step-4 cross-show check — the route compares `cookie.show_id === request.show_id` BEFORE the DB read so even a tampered or stale cookie cannot leak across shows. **Why the version field:** v=1 reserves the wire shape so the post-v1 multi-show upgrade (an array-cookie `{ v: 2, sessions: [{ token, show_id }, ...] }`) ships without breaking older readers. The decoder accepts ONLY `v === 1` in v1; an unrecognized `v` is treated as a parse fault (decoder returns null, validator emits `{ kind: 'continue', clearCookie: true }`), and dual-read v=1+v=2 support MUST land BEFORE any writer ever emits v=2. Without the version field, the v=2 upgrade would either need a cookie rename (forced re-mint for every active session) or a sniff-then-parse hack that violates the strict-shape decode contract. Sessions are stored in `link_sessions` keyed by the random `token`, mapping to `(show_id, crew_member_id, jwt_token_version, expires_at, last_active_at)`. Per-request authz still re-derives role from current `crew_members.role_flags`; the cookie is identity, not authorization.
- **A→B→A burn pattern is acceptable for v1.** When a user with a redeemed-link session for show A briefly navigates to show B's route, the show-A cookie's `show_id` will not match show-B's URL slug; the validator returns `{ kind: 'continue', clearCookie: true }`, the chain adapter clears the cookie, and the validator DELETEs the show-A `link_sessions` row (single canonical contract — see §7.2.2 step 4). The user must re-mint show A's session by re-opening the original signed link to access show A again. **Multi-show navigation is rare** (a single crew member usually works one show at a time); this burn cost is acceptable in v1. **Future versions (post-v1) MAY upgrade the envelope to `{ v: 2, sessions: [{ token, show_id }, ...] }`** so that multi-show users do not pay the re-mint cost; the validator would scan the `sessions` array for a matching `show_id`. The array upgrade is non-breaking on the wire (cookie name is unchanged) — the v=1 envelope-version field is what keeps the v=2 path open without a rename. **Migration sequence**: dual-read decoder (`v === 1` OR `v === 2`) MUST land BEFORE any writer emits v=2; writers flip on a feature flag with the dual-read decoder fully deployed for at least one cookie-TTL window (12h absolute) so no in-flight v=2 cookie hits a v=1-only reader. The deferred upgrade is gated on usage data.
- **Helper API (`lib/auth/cookies.ts`; envelope-versioned):** `setSessionCookie(value, opts)` and `clearSessionCookie()` — neither helper takes a slug parameter; the cookie name is the literal `__Host-fxav_session`. The `value` parameter is the URL-encoded JSON envelope `{ v: 1, token, show_id }` (callers serialize via a shared `encodeSessionCookieValue({ token, show_id })` helper that emits the v=1 envelope and lives alongside in `lib/auth/cookies.ts`; a paired `decodeSessionCookieValue(raw)` returns `{ token, show_id } | null` — null on JSON parse failure, missing fields, fields of the wrong type, OR an unrecognized envelope version, which the validator treats as a client-side parse fault per §7.2.2 step 1's tri-state classification). The decoder accepts ONLY `v === 1` in v1; the v=2 dual-read upgrade lands BEFORE any v=2 writer ships per the migration-sequence note above. **Size cap is 1024 bytes** on the raw cookie value (relaxed from the earlier 256-byte cap to leave headroom for the post-v1 v=2 array-envelope which can carry 5+ `{ token, show_id }` entries; still well under the 4KB browser cookie limit and the typical `Cookie:`-header growth concern). Banned-identifier audit (X.3): the literal substring `__Host-fxav_session` outside `lib/auth/cookies.ts` and `lib/auth/constants.ts` MUST fail the audit. The exact regex `/__Host-fxav_session/` (no slug suffix variant) covers all hand-rolled producers; the helpers remain the only legitimate producers.
- **`/auth/sign-out` clears the single cookie:** sign-out emits exactly one `clearSessionCookie()` call (no iteration needed) plus the Supabase Auth session clear plus the `__Host-fxav_bootstrap_v` clear. There is at most one `__Host-fxav_session` cookie on the request.
- TTL: 15 minutes idle (enforced via §7.2.2 step 9), 12 hours absolute (enforced via §7.2.2 step 3). After either expires the bootstrap exchange runs again on next visit (provided the original JWT hasn't expired and isn't revoked).
- Logout: deleting the cookie revokes the session locally but does not touch `revoked_links` or `crew_member_auth.revoked_below_version`. To revoke the underlying JWT, Doug uses §7.2.3.

This means the `?t=` form NEVER appears anywhere — not in spec examples, not in admin UI, not in copy-link affordances. Admin "Copy share link" generates URLs with `#t=`.

**A request with any `?t=` query parameter is treated as a compromise event, not just a bad link.** Vercel's runtime logs include search params in request log entries, so any URL of the form `/show/<slug>/p?t=<jwt>` (or `/show/<slug>?t=<jwt>` or any other path under `/show/<slug>/...?t=...`) that reaches the platform exposes the JWT to anyone with log access — regardless of how quickly middleware rejects the request. We cannot guarantee non-logging at the platform level on Vercel.

**Compromise-event handler** (single place in middleware that handles **any request whose pathname matches `^/show/[^/]+`** carrying a `t` search param — not just `/show/<slug>/p`). Vercel's request log records the full URL regardless of which Next.js route handles it, so a copy-paste leak landing on the root crew page (`/show/<slug>?t=...`), a typo-trailing path (`/show/<slug>/p/anything?t=...`), or any future `/show/<slug>/<subroute>?t=...` would still expose the JWT to platform logs and must trigger revocation. Runs inside the per-show advisory lock so a concurrent Apply can't collide. After verifying the JWT signature and parsing `(showId, name, tokenVersion)` from its claims, the handler routes on the comparison of `jwt.tokenVersion` against `crew_member_auth.current_token_version` for that `(show_id, name)`:

**Branch A — `jwt.tokenVersion === current_token_version` (leaked link IS the currently-active version).** The row must also be auto-rotated to "no live link" state — not just an exact-version revocation, because the admin UI's `Copy share link` would still surface this token until Doug manually rotated. In one transaction: insert the surgical `revoked_links` row at the exact `token_version` (idempotent `ON CONFLICT (show_id, crew_name, token_version) DO NOTHING`) with reason `leaked_via_query_string`, AND set `revoked_below_version = current_token_version` (no auto-mint of a fresh version — `current_token_version` and `max_issued_version` stay unchanged):

```sql
INSERT INTO revoked_links (show_id, crew_name, token_version, revoked_reason)
VALUES ($1, $2, $3, 'leaked_via_query_string')
ON CONFLICT (show_id, crew_name, token_version) DO NOTHING;

UPDATE crew_member_auth
   SET revoked_below_version = current_token_version
 WHERE show_id = $1 AND crew_name = $2;
```

The row enters the same "no live link" state defined in §5.2 — Doug must click "Issue new link" before any sharing affordance appears for that crew member. A SINGLE Issue-New-Link click then bumps both `current_token_version` and `max_issued_version` to `floor + 1`, immediately producing a usable token.

**Branch B — `jwt.tokenVersion < current_token_version` (leaked link is a stale historic version).** Insert ONLY the surgical `revoked_links` row at the exact `token_version` (idempotent `ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING`) with reason `leaked_via_query_string`. The current shareable version is unaffected; an older leak must NOT kick everyone off the live link. `crew_member_auth` columns remain unchanged in this branch.

**Branch C — `jwt.tokenVersion > current_token_version` (future-version leak; locked by plan Task 5.6).** The carried JWT claims a version higher than the row knows about. Treat this as the same no-live-link state as Branch A but with the floor lifted to the future version, so a SINGLE manual "Issue new link" still fully recovers. In one transaction:

- Insert the surgical `revoked_links` row at the exact future `tokenVersion` (idempotent `ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING`) with reason `leaked_via_query_string`.
- Lift ALL THREE fields to `jwt.tokenVersion` in the same step: `current_token_version = jwt.tokenVersion`, `max_issued_version = jwt.tokenVersion`, `revoked_below_version = jwt.tokenVersion`.

After this transition, ONE manual "Issue new link" click bumps both `current_token_version` and `max_issued_version` to `jwt.tokenVersion + 1`, immediately producing a usable replacement (the new JWT carrying `tokenVersion = jwt.tokenVersion + 1` is `> revoked_below_version` AND `=== current_token_version`, so it passes both the floor check and the strict-equality check). Multi-click recovery would be a regression. An earlier draft only lifted `revoked_below_version` while leaving `current/max` unchanged, requiring multiple Issue-New-Link clicks to clear the floor — that was a real auth-lockout bug. Use the canonical `LEAKED_LINK_DETECTED` user copy — do NOT invent a `SUSPICIOUS_FUTURE_VERSION` code (operator-only future-version anomaly metadata belongs in the structured log payload, not the user-facing message catalog).

All three branches use the service-role DB client; the user is unauthenticated at this point. After the appropriate branch executes:

1. **Return 410 Gone** with the message: "This link format is no longer supported and the link has been revoked. Ask Doug for a new link." Do not redirect.
2. **Log a `LEAKED_LINK_DETECTED` warning** to `sync_log` (or a dedicated `security_events` table) so Eric sees it in admin. Include the branch taken (A / B / C) and, for Branch A or C, `auto_rotated_to_no_live_link: true` (Branch C also includes the lifted floor value) so admin can spot it.

The JWT in Vercel's request logs is now equivalent to a known-revoked token. After the handler completes, Doug's admin view of the affected crew row reflects "no live link" state and prompts an explicit "Issue new link" — the admin UI cannot accidentally re-distribute the dead token.

**Doug's UX guarantees**:

- Admin "Copy share link" only ever generates URLs with `#t=`. There is no path in the admin UI to produce a `?t=` URL.
- Sample/demo URLs in docs and the spec all use `#t=`.
- The compromise-event handler is the safety net for typos, copy-paste corruption, or legacy links that escaped pre-rollout.

JWT payload (intentionally minimal — **no role claim**):

```json
{
  "iss": "fxav-crew-pages",
  "sub": "crew_member:<show_id>:<crew_name>",
  "showId": "<uuid>",
  "crewMemberKey": { "showId": "<uuid>", "name": "Eric Weiss" },
  "displayName": "Eric Weiss",
  "tokenVersion": <int, monotonic>,
  "iat": <unix-ts>,
  "exp": <unix-ts, default 90 days>
}
```

Why no `role` in the token: roles change. If Doug demotes a LEAD to A1, an outstanding signed link with `role: lead` would keep showing PO/invoice data until the token expired. Instead, **the route handler re-derives role from the current `crew_members` row on every request.** The token only identifies _who_ is requesting, not _what they can see_.

**Per-request authz flow** (signed-link path) — every check is required, in order:

1. Verify JWT signature and expiry. Reject (401) if either fails.
2. Look up `crew_members` by `(showId, name)` natural key. The JWT carries the natural key, not the UUID, so it survives the upsert/delete sync logic in §5.2.
3. If no row matches → 410 Gone with the "you've been removed from this show — contact Doug" message (§11).
4. **Strict-equality check against `crew_member_auth.current_token_version`** for `(showId, crew_members.name)`. If the auth row doesn't exist (defensive — should always exist alongside a crew_members row, but guard anyway) → 410 Gone "ask Doug for a new link." If `jwt.tokenVersion !== crew_member_auth.current_token_version` (whether older OR newer) → 410 Gone "this link has been replaced — ask Doug for a new one." **Strict equality is required** — a `<`-only comparison would let stale JWTs resurrect after a remove/re-add cycle, because a recreated crew row would default to a low version while old JWTs carry a higher one. The auth state lives in `crew_member_auth`, which survives crew_members deletion and never resets.
5. **Revocation-floor check**: if `jwt.tokenVersion <= crew_member_auth.revoked_below_version` → 410 Gone with "this link has been revoked. Ask Doug for a new one." This is the recoverable wildcard-equivalent: "Revoke all links for this person" sets `revoked_below_version = current_token_version`; "Issue new link" bumps `current_token_version` past the floor, so the freshly issued JWT (carrying the new higher version) passes both this check and the strict-equality check at step 4. Without this floor design, a wildcard revocation would permanently brick the (show, name) tuple's auth.
6. Check the `revoked_links` table (see §7.2.3) for surgical exact-version revocations:
   - Row with exact match on `(showId, name, tokenVersion)` → 410 Gone "this link has been revoked."
   - This handles the rare case Doug wants to revoke ONE historic version without affecting the current one. **The legacy wildcard token_version=0 row form is DEPRECATED and not implemented in v1** — its use case is fully covered by `revoked_below_version`, which is recoverable.
7. **Resolve identity only** — produce `{ kind: 'crew', crewMemberId, showId }` for the cookie-mint step. Role is NOT derived in the redemption path; downstream `getShowForViewer` re-derives it from `crew_members.role_flags` on every call (§4.4 / Task 4.3).
8. Mint the cookie session (write `link_sessions`; emit `__Host-fxav_session`) and render.

Signed with HS256 using `JWT_SIGNING_SECRET`.

#### 7.2.1 Per-link revocation (v1, not deferred)

A `revoked_links` table:

```sql
create table revoked_links (
  show_id        uuid not null references shows(id) on delete cascade,
  crew_name      text not null,
  token_version  int not null check (token_version > 0),  -- exact-version revocations only. The legacy "0 = wildcard" form is REMOVED in v1; use crew_member_auth.revoked_below_version for wildcard-equivalent semantics.
  revoked_at     timestamptz not null default now(),
  revoked_reason text,
  primary key (show_id, crew_name, token_version)
);

-- Per-link redeemed sessions (set after the bootstrap exchange in §7.2).
-- The opaque cookie value maps here, not the JWT. Sessions are short-lived
-- and idle-expire; the JWT lifetime gates how long new sessions can still
-- be redeemed from the original signed link.
create table link_sessions (
  token             text primary key,             -- random opaque value (cookie content)
  show_id           uuid not null references shows(id) on delete cascade,
  -- M5 batch-10 finding: crew_member_id is NULLABLE and uses ON DELETE SET NULL
  -- (NOT cascade). Earlier draft used `not null ... on delete cascade`, which
  -- silently deleted the link_sessions row whenever the underlying crew_members
  -- row was removed by sync — making §7.2.2 step 5 ("crew row gone → 410
  -- LINK_NO_CREW_MATCH; DELETE the session") unreachable: the session row the
  -- validator's step 5 expects to observe never exists at validator time
  -- because cascade already deleted it. SET NULL preserves the session row
  -- across crew deletion so the validator can detect the deletion and respond
  -- with the documented 410 + "you've been removed" copy. The same
  -- audit-preservation principle applies that motivated crew_member_auth's
  -- natural-key design (line 237-238 above): auth-related state survives
  -- cascade deletion intentionally so the validator can render the correct
  -- user-facing failure. Validator semantics (§7.2.2 step 5): if
  -- crew_member_id IS NULL OR no row exists in crew_members for that id,
  -- return 410 LINK_NO_CREW_MATCH and DELETE this link_sessions row at
  -- validator time (step 5 already DELETEs on every fail path; the preserved
  -- session is short-lived audit data observed only by the validator, not a
  -- permanent grant).
  crew_member_id    uuid references crew_members(id) on delete set null,
  jwt_token_version int not null,                 -- the tokenVersion at the time of redemption. Validated on every request against crew_member_auth.current_token_version (strict equality) AND against crew_member_auth.revoked_below_version (must be greater). See §7.2.2 steps 6-7.
  signing_key_id    text not null,                -- the JWT signing key id that actually verified the signature at redemption time. Captured from `verifyLinkJwt`'s `verifiedKid` return field (the JOSE header `kid` of the JWT whose signature was verified), NOT from a fresh `SELECT active_signing_key_id FROM app_settings` at INSERT time. The redeem-link route additionally enforces a kid-rotation gate that compares `verifiedKid` to `app_settings.active_signing_key_id` BEFORE the INSERT and rejects with `LINK_REDEEM_KEY_ROTATED` (§12.4) on mismatch — so the only rows that ever land here carry a `signing_key_id` that matches the active kid at INSERT time. §7.2.2 step 3a compares this against the CURRENT `app_settings.active_signing_key_id`; mismatch (operator ran §7.2.3 global rotation since redemption) → DELETE the row, 401 LINK_SESSION_KEY_ROTATED. This is the per-row half of the atomic global-rotation contract documented in §7.2.3 ("Global rotation"). Without this column AND the verifiedKid-source-of-truth contract AND the redeem-time gate, a JWT_SIGNING_SECRET rotation cannot terminate already-redeemed sessions atomically; with all three, the operator's single-transaction UPDATE on app_settings invalidates every live session on its next request.
  expires_at        timestamptz not null,         -- absolute expiry (12h from creation), enforced by §7.2.2 step 3
  last_active_at    timestamptz not null default now(),  -- idle TTL anchor, enforced by §7.2.2 step 9 (15-minute window)
  created_at        timestamptz not null default now()
);
create index on link_sessions (crew_member_id);

-- M5 batch-10 finding: bootstrap_nonces is the login-CSRF defense for
-- /api/auth/redeem-link. /show/<slug>/p server-rendering INSERTs a row with the
-- SHA-256 hash of the freshly minted nonce; the redeem-link route atomically
-- consumes it via `UPDATE ... SET consumed_at = now() WHERE nonce_hash = $1
-- AND consumed_at IS NULL RETURNING nonce_hash`. Read-time expiry: rows with
-- issued_at + 30 seconds < now() reject regardless of consumed_at. Periodic
-- cron DELETEs rows older than 5 minutes (hygiene; the read-time expiry is
-- the security gate). Admin-only RLS per §4.3.
create table bootstrap_nonces (
  -- M5 batch-11: composite PK (nonce_hash, show_id) — earlier single-PK on nonce_hash forced a single live nonce per browser regardless of show, breaking multi-tab/multi-show flows; the composite key + consume-by-(nonce_hash, show_id) lets multiple live nonces coexist.
  nonce_hash     text not null,                                               -- SHA-256(nonce); the raw nonce never lands at rest
  show_id        uuid not null references shows(id) on delete cascade,
  issued_at      timestamptz not null default now(),
  consumed_at    timestamptz,                                                 -- NULL until single-use consumption
  -- Captured at INSERT time from app_settings.active_signing_key_id. The bootstrap shell signs
  -- the __Host-fxav_bootstrap_v cookie under THIS kid; the redeem-link route reads the cookie
  -- envelope's kid field and compares against this row's signing_key_id to discriminate the
  -- benign "operator rotated the signing key between mint and redeem" case (CSRF_KEY_ROTATED,
  -- transient) from the malicious "attacker forged a bootstrap cookie" case (CSRF_DENIED).
  -- Without this column, a §7.2.3 global rotation that happens to land between bootstrap
  -- shell render and redeem POST produces a benign cookie-decode failure that 403's as
  -- CSRF_DENIED — a misleading security-telemetry signal that operators cannot distinguish
  -- from an actual cross-site attack. The column is sourced via the same read-with-INSERT
  -- pattern used by link_sessions.signing_key_id (see line 2014 region) so the per-row
  -- capture is atomic with the cookie write.
  signing_key_id text not null default 'k1',
  primary key (nonce_hash, show_id)                                           -- M5 batch-11
);
create index on bootstrap_nonces (issued_at);                                  -- supports the cleanup cron's range scan

-- Staged parse results pending admin approval. Used when any of MI-6..MI-14
-- (§6.8) trip but the parse otherwise looks valid. The two modified_time
-- columns are both required for the CAS in §6.8.1:
--   base_modified_time   = the prior shows.last_seen_modified_time at the
--                          moment of staging. CAS target on Apply.
--   staged_modified_time = the incoming file's modifiedTime that produced
--                          this parse. The new last_seen_modified_time
--                          after Apply succeeds.
-- These differ by design: staged content is a NEWER version than the live
-- snapshot, which is exactly why review is needed before destructive write.
-- Round-50 / M6 batch-9 retry-2 amendment: composite uniqueness with wizard_session_id.
-- Earlier draft used drive_file_id as the PK, but that prevented coexistence of a live
-- (NULL-session) row and a wizard (UUID-session) row on the same drive_file_id during
-- Re-run Setup, when spec §9.0 explicitly allows the live folder to keep cron-syncing
-- while the wizard runs. The new schema uses a surrogate `id` PK plus two partial unique
-- indexes that treat NULL as distinct: one for live rows (NULL session), one for
-- wizard rows (UUID session). The (drive_file_id) live partial index keeps cron/push/manual
-- single-row-per-file semantics; the (drive_file_id, wizard_session_id) onboarding partial
-- index isolates each wizard session's rows from both the live row and other sessions.
create table pending_syncs (
  id                   uuid primary key default gen_random_uuid(),  -- surrogate PK (round-50)
  drive_file_id        text not null,                   -- intentionally NOT FK'd to shows: a first-seen stage may exist for a drive_file_id with no shows row yet (slug derivation is deferred to Apply per §6.9). App-layer invariant: at most one live (NULL-session) row per drive_file_id, plus at most one onboarding row per (drive_file_id, wizard_session_id).
  parsed_at            timestamptz not null default now(),
  base_modified_time   timestamptz,                 -- prior shows.last_seen_modified_time; NULL only when staging the very first parse for a brand-new show row
  staged_modified_time timestamptz not null,        -- file.modifiedTime at parse time
  parse_result         jsonb not null,              -- full ParseResult, ready to apply verbatim on approval
  triggered_review_items jsonb not null default '[]'::jsonb,  -- structured list of review items, each with a stable id. Computed at staging time, immutable. See shape below. Each item is a single per-occurrence decision Doug must make.
  prior_last_sync_status text,                       -- snapshot of shows.last_sync_status at the moment of staging. Used by Discard to revert without guessing. NULL when staging a first-seen show (no shows row yet).
  prior_last_sync_error  text,                       -- snapshot of shows.last_sync_error at the moment of staging. Same lifecycle as prior_last_sync_status.
  staged_id            uuid not null default gen_random_uuid(),  -- Apply UI passes this back; admin click that references a no-longer-current staged_id is rejected (defends against multi-tab "Apply" against a superseded staged version)
  source_kind          text not null check (source_kind in ('cron', 'push', 'manual', 'onboarding_scan')),  -- which sync mode created this staging row
  wizard_session_id    uuid,                          -- ONLY non-NULL when source_kind = 'onboarding_scan'. Carries the app_settings.pending_wizard_session_id at staging time. Apply / Discard for these rows MUST CAS against current app_settings.pending_wizard_session_id; if mismatch, the wizard that created the row was superseded and the row is purged before any other action runs.
  wizard_approved      boolean not null default false,  -- M11 batch-11 finding 1 (DEFERRED-UNTIL-FINALIZE Apply). For wizard-scope rows (`wizard_session_id IS NOT NULL`), `applyStaged` flips this to TRUE inside the locked transaction WITHOUT running Phase 2 and WITHOUT deleting the staged row. The approved row remains in `pending_syncs` until wizard finalize promotes ALL approved rows atomically. For live-scope rows (`wizard_session_id IS NULL`) this column MUST stay FALSE — live Apply runs Phase 2 and DELETEs the row in one transaction; `wizard_approved` is meaningless for live rows. Enforced by CHECK (`wizard_session_id IS NOT NULL OR wizard_approved = false`).
  -- M11 batch-12 finding 1: durable wizard-approval payload. `wizard_approved = TRUE` alone loses the validated reviewer_choices, the operator identity, and the timestamp the operator clicked Apply — finalize cannot reconstruct sync_audit rows nor replay MI-11/12/13/14 derived side-effects (those derivations consume `reviewer_choices`). The three columns below are NULL until step 5W (the wizard Apply transaction) sets all four (these three + `wizard_approved = TRUE`) atomically. Once set, they are immutable for the remaining lifetime of the row (finalize reads them; finalize commit DELETEs the row). Live-scope rows (`wizard_session_id IS NULL`) MUST keep all three NULL — these columns are meaningful only for wizard-scope rows. Enforced by the symmetry CHECKs below.
  wizard_approved_by_email text,                       -- M11 batch-12 finding 1: admin email captured at step 5W (canonicalize_email(session.user.email)). NULL until approved. Survives the deferred-until-finalize window so finalize-time sync_audit can attribute the approval to the operator who actually clicked Apply, not to whoever happened to click Finalize (which may be a different admin).
  wizard_approved_at       timestamptz,                -- M11 batch-12 finding 1: now() captured at step 5W. NULL until approved. Used by finalize as the sync_audit `approved_at` and as a per-row recency check if multiple approvals stack across a long-running wizard.
  wizard_reviewer_choices  jsonb,                      -- M11 batch-12 finding 1: validated reviewer_choices payload (§6.8.2 client-submission shape, post server-side validation against `triggered_review_items` ids). NULL until approved. Captured at step 5W after schema validation passes; finalize-time Phase 2 consumes this exact payload to compute MI-11/12/13/14 derived_side_effects and the sync_audit row. WITHOUT this column, finalize would have to re-derive auth side-effects from `triggered_review_items` defaults, silently overriding Doug's ACCEPT/REJECT choices for each item. The JSONB shape MUST round-trip through the §6.8.2 validator unchanged — a fresh wizard approval and a finalize-time replay produce the same derived_side_effects.
  -- M11 batch-13 finding 3: payload-shape versioning. A wizard Apply can stage approvals that sit in `pending_syncs` for an arbitrary window before finalize promotes them. If the §6.8.2 reviewer-choices shape ever evolves (new actions for future invariants, expanded per-item context fields), finalize-time replay MUST dispatch to the version that actually validated the payload, NOT to whichever validator the current build implements. WITHOUT this column, a future shape revision would silently mis-validate (rejecting a still-valid old payload) OR mis-replay (re-deriving auth side-effects against fields that were not present at Apply time). Version 1 is the canonical shape defined in §6.8.2 (`{ item_id: string, action: 'apply' | 'reject' | 'rename' | 'independent', rename_value?: string when action='rename' }`); any other shape is a future version and MUST NOT be written under version 1. Finalize refuses to promote a row whose version is not in the current code's supported set, emitting `WIZARD_REVIEWER_CHOICES_VERSION_UNSUPPORTED` (§12.4) so the operator must re-review and re-Apply under the current version. Live-scope rows (`wizard_session_id IS NULL`) MUST keep this NULL — meaningful only for wizard-scope rows.
  wizard_reviewer_choices_version smallint,            -- M11 batch-13 finding 3: payload-shape version. NULL on live rows. Set to 1 (current canonical shape) at step 5W in the SAME UPDATE that sets the other three approval-payload columns. Finalize dispatches validation + replay through a versioned handler keyed on this column; unknown version → `WIZARD_REVIEWER_CHOICES_VERSION_UNSUPPORTED` and the operator must re-Apply.
  warning_summary      text not null,               -- human message shown in the admin "review and approve" UI
  check (wizard_session_id IS NOT NULL OR wizard_approved = false),  -- live rows never carry wizard_approved=true
  -- M11 batch-12 finding 1 invariants: payload columns are NULL on live rows AND symmetric with `wizard_approved`.
  -- M11 batch-13 finding 3: `wizard_reviewer_choices_version` is part of the symmetry pair (NULL on live rows, NOT NULL when approved).
  check (wizard_session_id IS NOT NULL OR (wizard_approved_by_email IS NULL AND wizard_approved_at IS NULL AND wizard_reviewer_choices IS NULL AND wizard_reviewer_choices_version IS NULL)),
  check (wizard_approved = false OR (wizard_approved_by_email IS NOT NULL AND wizard_approved_at IS NOT NULL AND wizard_reviewer_choices IS NOT NULL AND wizard_reviewer_choices_version IS NOT NULL))
);
create index pending_syncs_wizard_session_idx on pending_syncs (wizard_session_id) where wizard_session_id is not null;
-- Round-50 / M6 batch-9 retry-2 amendment: live-row vs wizard-row partial unique indexes.
-- Live partition: one row per drive_file_id with NULL wizard_session_id (cron/push/manual paths).
create unique index pending_syncs_live_drive_file_idx
  on pending_syncs (drive_file_id) where wizard_session_id is null;
-- Wizard partition: one row per (drive_file_id, wizard_session_id) for onboarding-scan paths.
create unique index pending_syncs_session_drive_file_idx
  on pending_syncs (drive_file_id, wizard_session_id) where wizard_session_id is not null;
-- triggered_review_items shape (see §6.8.2). Each entry has a stable per-item id
-- so multiple instances of the same invariant in one parse are independently
-- representable and auditable:
--   [
--     { "id": "<uuid>", "invariant": "MI-11", "crew_name": "Alice" },
--     { "id": "<uuid>", "invariant": "MI-11", "crew_name": "Bob" },
--     { "id": "<uuid>", "invariant": "MI-13", "removed_name": "Cara", "added_name": "Carla" },
--     { "id": "<uuid>", "invariant": "MI-7",  "section": "hotel_reservations", "prior_count": 4, "new_count": 1 },
--     { "id": "<uuid>", "invariant": "MI-1..MI-5a", ... }  // MI-1..MI-5a never appear here; they hard-fail
--   ]
-- The "id" is generated at staging time and is what the Apply submission references.
-- approval_metadata is NOT a column on this table. It is computed transiently
-- inside the locked Apply transaction from validated reviewer choices (§6.8.2)
-- and consumed immediately, then written into sync_audit (§6.8.3). Persisting
-- it on pending_syncs would create a TOCTOU race between concurrent Apply
-- attempts.

-- First-seen sheet hard-fail surface. When a brand-new sheet (no shows row
-- exists) parses with MI-1..MI-5a hard failures, the spec deliberately
-- does NOT create a shows row. Without a separate visibility surface, the
-- failure would only appear in sync_log, which Doug doesn't watch.
-- This table backs an /admin "Sheets we couldn't parse" panel so brand-new
-- sheets that fail parsing are visible alongside successfully-parsed shows.
-- Round-50 / M6 batch-9 retry-2 amendment: composite uniqueness with wizard_session_id.
-- Same rationale as pending_syncs above — live (NULL-session) hard-fails and wizard
-- (UUID-session) hard-fails coexist for the same drive_file_id during Re-run Setup.
-- The wizard_session_id and discovered_during_folder_id columns were added by Task 10.4
-- (M9+M10 batch-8); this amendment adds the surrogate id PK + partitioned uniqueness.
create table pending_ingestions (
  id                uuid primary key default gen_random_uuid(),   -- surrogate PK (round-50)
  drive_file_id     text not null,                    -- not FK'd to shows: the row precisely captures the case where shows row doesn't exist
  drive_file_name   text not null,                    -- from files.list, displayed in admin
  first_seen_at     timestamptz not null default now(),
  last_attempt_at   timestamptz not null default now(),
  attempt_count     int not null default 1,
  last_error_code   text not null,                    -- "MI-1_VERSION_DETECTION_FAILED" | "MI-2_TITLE_MISSING" | "MI-3_NO_PARSEABLE_DATE" | "MI-4_NO_CREW" | "MI-5_NO_ROOMS" | "MI-5a_DUPLICATE_CREW_NAME" | "DRIVE_FETCH_FAILED" | etc.
  last_error_message text not null,                   -- human-readable
  last_warnings     jsonb default '[]'::jsonb,        -- full ParseWarning[] from the failing parse so Doug can drill in
  wizard_session_id uuid,                             -- ONLY non-NULL when source is `runOnboardingScan`. Live cron/push/manual paths set NULL. Round-50 isolation key.
  discovered_during_folder_id text,                   -- folder id at scan time (onboarding provenance; NULL for live rows). Set by Task 10.4 / M9+M10 batch-8.
  last_seen_modified_time timestamptz                 -- M6 batch-10 fix-2: the Drive `modifiedTime` at the moment of the most recent UPSERT (Phase 1 hard-fail, handleDriveFetchFailure, runManualStageForFirstSeen, runOnboardingScan hard-fails). NULL only on legacy rows from before this column was added; new INSERTs/UPSERTs MUST populate it from `fileMeta.modifiedTime`. Read by `/api/admin/pending-ingestions/[id]/discard` to populate `deferred_ingestions.deferred_at_modified_time` when kind='defer_until_modified' (mirrors how `pending_syncs.staged_modified_time` is consumed by the first-seen `pending_syncs` Discard variant per §6.8.1).
);
-- Round-50: live-row vs wizard-row partial unique indexes (mirror pending_syncs).
create unique index pending_ingestions_live_drive_file_idx
  on pending_ingestions (drive_file_id) where wizard_session_id is null;
create unique index pending_ingestions_session_drive_file_idx
  on pending_ingestions (drive_file_id, wizard_session_id) where wizard_session_id is not null;
-- Lifecycle: row is INSERTed/UPDATEd by §5.2 Phase 1 hard-fail when no shows
-- row exists for the drive_file_id. Row is DELETEd by Phase 2 / Apply when
-- the same drive_file_id eventually succeeds and produces a shows row.
-- Onboarding hard-fail rows (wizard_session_id IS NOT NULL) are DELETEd by
-- the wizard's Retry/Defer/Ignore endpoints (Task 10.4) or purged by the
-- next wizard's session-purge (Task 10.3).
```

#### 7.2.2 Cookie-session validation (every subsequent request)

The redemption step in §7.2 mints a `link_sessions` row and a cookie. **That cookie is not a permanent grant — it is re-validated against current state on every page render.** Any of these checks failing aborts the request and deletes the offending session:

For every request to `/show/<slug>` (or any data fetch behind a redeemed link), the server:

1. Reads `__Host-fxav_session` from the cookie (single host-wide cookie name; per-show cookie naming would not isolate cookies because browsers send all matching `(domain, path)` cookies to every same-host request regardless of name, which made per-show naming both ineffective for isolation and a Cookie-header growth vector). If no cookie is present → `{ kind: 'continue' }` (no session; chain falls through to Google/admin). If the cookie IS present, decode the URL-encoded JSON value via `decodeSessionCookieValue(raw)`. Decode failure (null return — JSON parse error, missing fields, wrong field types) → `{ kind: 'continue', clearCookie: true }` (client-side parse fault per §7.2.2 step 1's tri-state classification — clear the offending cookie; no DB row exists to delete because we have not yet looked one up). On successful decode, the validator now holds `{ token, show_id }`.
2. Looks up `link_sessions WHERE token = $cookie`. If not found → 401, redirect to "this link has expired — ask Doug for a new one."
3. Verify `link_sessions.expires_at > now()`. If not → DELETE the row, 401.
   3a. **Signing-key rotation check.** Read `app_settings.active_signing_key_id`. If `link_sessions.signing_key_id <> app_settings.active_signing_key_id` → DELETE the row, **401 with code `LINK_SESSION_KEY_ROTATED`** (§12.4). This is the per-request enforcement point for the §7.2.3 global-rotation contract: when the operator runs `UPDATE app_settings SET active_signing_key_id = '<new-id>'`, every existing `link_sessions` row carries the OLD id and is terminally killed on its next request. The validator's `clearCookie:true` outcome is mandatory. User copy: "Sessions have been rotated; please open your original signed link again." The next open of the original signed link re-runs §7.2 redemption under the new key id and writes a fresh `link_sessions` row carrying the current `active_signing_key_id`. Without this step, `JWT_SIGNING_SECRET` rotation is NOT a nuclear option — already-redeemed sessions continue to validate via the OPAQUE `link_sessions.token` cookie until the 12h absolute / 15min idle TTL elapses.
4. **Live cross-show check.** Look up the show by `slug` in the URL. Verify (a) `cookie.show_id === show.id` (the cookie's payload-bound `show_id` matches the URL's show) AND (b) `show.id === link_sessions.show_id` (the DB row's binding matches). On any mismatch in either check → `{ kind: 'continue', clearCookie: true }` AND DELETE the offending `link_sessions` row. **This is the single canonical contract for the cross-show case**: the show-A cookie WILL be sent to a `/show/<show-b-slug>` request (browsers send all same-host cookies regardless of name), so step 4 is the active enforcement point — not a defense-in-depth guard. The clear-cookie+DELETE outcome trades a re-mint cost (the user must re-open the original signed link to access show A again — the **A→B→A burn pattern** documented in §7.2 cookie semantics) for the simplicity of a single host-wide cookie. **Multi-show navigation is rare** (a single crew member usually works one show at a time); this v1 burn cost is acceptable. Future versions MAY upgrade the cookie value to a JSON-encoded array of `{ token, show_id }` entries (cap N, evict oldest) so that a multi-show user does NOT pay the re-mint cost — see §7.2 cookie semantics future-version note. Under this contract the cookie's `show_id` is wrong for show B and the row is unrecoverable from the client anyway, so DELETE is the correct cleanup; the wrong-show cookie class is fully reachable.
5. Look up `crew_members WHERE id = link_sessions.crew_member_id`. **The lookup MUST handle BOTH the NULL case AND the row-missing case:** if `link_sessions.crew_member_id IS NULL` (the crew row was removed by sync, and the FK's ON DELETE SET NULL preserved the session row for the validator to observe), OR the lookup returns zero rows (defensive — should be unreachable when the FK constraint is enforced) → DELETE the session, 410 Gone with the "you've been removed" message. The schema's `ON DELETE SET NULL` (line 1490 above) is intentional: cascade-delete would have silently destroyed the session before step 5 could observe the deletion, making the documented 410 unreachable. The preserved-then-deleted-at-validator-time path is audit-correct: the user gets the actionable 410 copy, and the session is reaped immediately afterward by step 5's DELETE.
6. **Strict-equality `link_sessions.jwt_token_version === crew_member_auth.current_token_version`** (looked up by `(show_id, crew_members.name)`). If unequal in either direction → DELETE the session, 410 Gone with "this link has been replaced." Strict equality matches step 4 of the redemption flow and protects against the same remove/re-add reset attack.
7. **Revocation-floor check**: if `link_sessions.jwt_token_version <= crew_member_auth.revoked_below_version` → DELETE the session, 410 Gone "this link has been revoked." Same semantics as the redemption-flow step 5; protects active sessions against "Revoke all links."
8. **Surgical revoked_links check**: if a row exists in `revoked_links` with `(show_id, crew_members.name, token_version = link_sessions.jwt_token_version)` → DELETE the session, 410 Gone "this link has been revoked." (No wildcard form here either.)
9. **Idle-timeout check**: if `link_sessions.last_active_at < now() - interval '15 minutes'` → DELETE the session, 401 with "Your session has timed out due to inactivity. Open the original signed link again." This is the rolling-idle TTL the §7.2 cookie semantics promised; without this check, a stolen or forgotten cookie remains usable for the full 12-hour absolute TTL.
10. Update `link_sessions.last_active_at = now()` (advances the idle window for the next request).
11. **Resolve identity only** — the validator returns `{ kind: 'success', viewer: { kind: 'crew', crewMemberId, showId } }`. Role is NOT derived here; downstream `getShowForViewer(showId, viewer)` re-derives it from `crew_members.role_flags` on every call (§4.4 / Task 4.3).
12. Render (after `getShowForViewer` returns its role-filtered payload — see §7.4).

**Every numbered step above is a mandatory security check.** Steps 1–4 prove the cookie corresponds to a still-existing session, scoped to the right show, for an existing crew member. Steps 5–7 prove revocations and rotations have not invalidated the underlying authority. Step 8 is the surgical exact-version revocation. Step 9 is the rolling idle TTL. Skipping any step reopens a real attack surface:

| Skipping | Reopens                                                                                                                                                                                                        |
| -------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| 1–2      | Forgotten/cleared sessions still grant access                                                                                                                                                                  |
| 3        | Sessions outlive the 12h absolute cap                                                                                                                                                                          |
| 3a       | `JWT_SIGNING_SECRET` rotation cannot terminate already-redeemed sessions; an attacker holding a redeemed cookie keeps minting fresh subscriber JWTs after rotation until 12h absolute / 15min idle TTL elapses |
| 4        | Cross-show cookie reuse                                                                                                                                                                                        |
| 5        | Removed crew can keep accessing                                                                                                                                                                                |
| 6        | Strict version mismatch (resurrection after remove/re-add)                                                                                                                                                     |
| 7        | "Revoke all" wildcard never takes effect on active sessions                                                                                                                                                    |
| 8        | Surgical exact-version revocations never take effect on active sessions                                                                                                                                        |
| 9        | Stolen/forgotten cookies usable for full 12h                                                                                                                                                                   |

**Implementation note:** all 12 steps are encapsulated in a single `lib/auth/validateLinkSession(req)` helper that returns a **tri-state outcome** (locked by plan Task 5.2):

- `{ kind: 'success', viewer: { kind: 'crew'; crewMemberId; showId } }` — auth passes. **Identity-only payload (no `viewerRole`)**: per §4.4 / Task 4.3's locked contract, `getShowForViewer` re-derives role from `crew_members.role_flags` on every call; passing a pre-derived role from the validator would reopen the stale-role hole.
- `{ kind: 'continue', priorFailure?, clearCookie?: true }` — this branch doesn't apply or recovered cleanly; the caller's chain falls through to `validateGoogleSession` / `requireAdmin`. Steps 1-9 (cookie missing, decode failure, session not found, expired, cross-show binding mismatch, removed crew, version mismatch, revoked, idle past TTL) produce `continue` with `clearCookie: true`. **Server-side `link_sessions` row deletion is per-step (single canonical contract: every step 3-9 with a found row DELETEs it, including step 4): step 3 (expired), step 4 (cross-show binding mismatch — see §7.2.2 step 4 above), step 5 (removed crew), step 6 (version mismatch), step 7 (revoke floor), step 8 (surgical revoke), step 9 (idle TTL) all DELETE the offending row.** Under the single host-wide cookie design (with `{ token, show_id }` JSON payload), the cookie's bound `show_id` is wrong for show B's route AND the cookie is being cleared anyway, so the row is unrecoverable from the client and DELETE is the correct cleanup. The cost is the **A→B→A burn pattern** — a user who briefly visits show B must re-open show A's original signed link to re-mint show A's session — explicitly accepted as a v1 trade-off (see §7.2 cookie semantics; multi-show navigation is rare; future versions may upgrade to an array-cookie design that avoids the burn). Steps 1-2 have no row to delete (no row was found in the first place; step 1 covers cookie-missing AND decode-failure cases, step 2 covers session-not-found). **Client-side cookie parse/format faults are also `continue + clearCookie:true`, NOT `terminal_failure`** — every malformed-cookie failure mode that originates with the client (corrupted/legacy/truncated cookie value, wrong issuer or audience claim, expired-signature decode error, missing required claims, base64 decode failure, JSON parse error on the session lookup, stale cookie from a prior cookie-format version) MUST clear the offending cookie via `clearSessionCookie()` and fall through to `validateGoogleSession` / `requireAdmin`. The same trust-model rationale that covers stale/wrong-show/revoked cookies applies here: §7.3 authorizes via "Google session OR redeemed-link cookie OR admin," so a corrupt cookie value MUST NOT deny a user whose Google or admin session is independently valid. Reserving `terminal_failure` for client-driven cookie corruption would let a single bad cookie permanently block the entire `/show/<slug>` chain even though the other credential classes would otherwise succeed.
- `{ kind: 'terminal_failure', status, code, message }` — reserved exclusively for **server-side faults** that block the validator from making a determination at all: DB connection failure, Supabase service outage, signing-key fetch failure for the cookie format (when key rotation is added), or any infrastructure error where the validator literally cannot reach the data it needs. Client-side cookie corruption is NOT a terminal failure (see preceding bullet) — by definition the validator has already classified the cookie as "this cookie is unusable," which is exactly what `continue + clearCookie:true` is for. Routes never short-circuit on a stale/wrong-show/revoked/malformed cookie; §7.3 explicitly authorizes via "Google session OR redeemed-link cookie OR admin," so a bad cookie shouldn't deny a user whose Google or admin session is valid.

Only steps 11-12 produce `kind: 'success'` (with the identity-only viewer payload above — no role). **The helper is the only correct way to authenticate a redeemed-link request; routes must never re-implement subsets.** It is called from every signed-link page route and any server action that mutates state on behalf of a redeemed user.

**Google-session authorization is structurally different and uses its own validator** (`lib/auth/validateGoogleSession(req)`):

1. Verify the Supabase Auth session is present and unexpired.
2. Look up `canonicalize(supabase.user.email)` against `crew_members.email` for the requested show. The DB column is already canonical per §4.1.1, so the comparison is exact-match on canonical form. If no match → 403 with "your email isn't on the crew list for this show." **If multi-match → 500 with `AMBIGUOUS_EMAIL_BINDING`** (this should be impossible because of the `crew_members_show_email_unique` partial index plus MI-5b, but the validator must explicitly reject rather than pick a row to defend against any future schema regression). The notification path is concrete (see §4.6 below): the validator INSERTs into `admin_alerts` keyed on `(show_id, code)` with the colliding crew rows captured in `context` JSONB. The dashboard renders any unresolved `admin_alerts` row as a top-bar critical banner that cannot be dismissed without clicking through to the affected show.
3. **Removal is the only revocation primitive for Google sessions.** When Doug removes a crew member from the sheet, sync's `delete-not-in-set` step removes the `crew_members` row, which causes step 2 to fail on the user's next request. There is no separate "revoke Google login" affordance.
4. **Resolve identity only** — return `{ kind: 'success', viewer: { kind: 'crew', crewMemberId, showId } }`. Role is NOT derived here; downstream `getShowForViewer(showId, viewer)` re-derives it from `crew_members.role_flags` on every call (§4.4 / Task 4.3).
5. Render (after `getShowForViewer` returns its role-filtered payload — see §7.4).

The signed-link revocation tables (`revoked_links`, `crew_member_auth.revoked_below_version`) are **signed-link-specific** and do NOT apply to Google sessions. They reference `tokenVersion`, which Google sessions don't carry. Implementation must NOT cross-wire these tables to the Google validator. The two validators share only `crew_members` lookup helpers and role-derivation; revocation logic is intentionally separate because the threat model is different (Google login = identity verified by Google, revocation = remove from sheet; signed link = portable token, revocation = explicit token-version invalidation).

**Cross-show identity-only validator — `lib/auth/validateGoogleIdentity(req)`.** `validateGoogleSession` is **strictly show-bound**: step 2 requires a `requestedShowId` parameter and looks up `crew_members WHERE show_id = $requestedShowId AND email = canonicalize(...)`. Every cross-show signed-in surface — most notably `/me` (the user's signed-in show list per §7.3) — has NO show parameter at validator-call time, because the entire purpose of the surface is to enumerate which shows the signed-in identity belongs to. Calling `validateGoogleSession` from such a surface is a structural error: there is no show ID to bind against. The corrected design defines a separate `validateGoogleIdentity(req)` validator that returns `{ kind: 'success', email, providerSub }` from the Supabase Auth session ONLY (no show binding, no `crew_members` lookup, no revocation check) and is used EXCLUSIVELY by cross-show signed-in surfaces. Show-bound surfaces (`/show/<slug>`, every `/api/asset/...`, every `/api/report/...`, every `/show/<slug>/p` redemption follow-up) MUST keep using `validateGoogleSession` so the `crew_members`-membership-for-this-show check still runs. The two validators intentionally do NOT share a common implementation: `validateGoogleIdentity` is small enough that "DRY-up" temptation reopens the show-binding hole. X.3's audit allowlist (plan Task X.3) classifies `app/me/page.tsx` as `me` chain `[validateGoogleIdentity]` (NOT `[validateGoogleSession]`); a route file under `app/me/**` that imports `validateGoogleSession` fails X.3 immediately. Test fixtures: `bad-me-route-uses-validateGoogleSession.tsx` MUST FAIL the audit; `good-me-route-uses-validateGoogleIdentity.tsx` MUST PASS.

#### 7.2.3 Revocation summary

Two independent mechanisms invalidate prior links:

- **Routine rotation (`current_token_version` bump)** — Doug's "Issue new link" button: `UPDATE crew_member_auth SET current_token_version = max_issued_version + 1, max_issued_version = max_issued_version + 1 WHERE show_id = $1 AND crew_name = $2`. Issues a fresh JWT carrying the new version. Older AND newer JWTs immediately fail strict equality. **No row inserted into `revoked_links`** — version mismatch handles this case for free.
- **Surgical revocation (`revoked_links` row, exact version)** — used when Doug wants to invalidate without issuing a replacement, or to revoke the currently-active version (e.g., a compromised link that he hasn't yet rotated). Doug's per-show admin page has "Revoke link" → inserts a row with the exact `current_token_version`.
- **Wildcard revocation via floor (`crew_member_auth.revoked_below_version`)** — used by "Revoke all links for this person." Sets `revoked_below_version = current_token_version`. Every currently-issued JWT (which carries `current_token_version` or older) is below the floor and rejected. Critically, this is recoverable: "Issue new link" bumps `current_token_version = max_issued_version + 1` and `max_issued_version = max_issued_version + 1`. The new JWT is `> revoked_below_version` and passes. The floor only invalidates versions ≤ its value, never future versions. **No `token_version = 0` row is written.**

**Global rotation (`JWT_SIGNING_SECRET` key-id rotation)** — total-system invalidation that immediately terminates EVERY active redeemed-link session, not just the un-redeemed JWTs. Steady-state redeemed-link auth validates the OPAQUE `link_sessions.token` cookie via §7.2.2 — it never re-verifies the original JWT signature — so rotating the JWT-signing secret alone only blocks NEW redemptions; already-redeemed sessions continue to pass `validateLinkSession` until the 12h absolute / 15min idle TTL elapses. The Realtime subscriber-token mint AND the version route reuse the same `validateLinkSession`, so an attacker holding a redeemed cookie keeps minting fresh subscriber JWTs after rotation. To make rotation actually atomic, the schema carries TWO bound key-id columns:

- `link_sessions.signing_key_id text NOT NULL` — captured at redemption time from the **`verifiedKid` returned by `verifyLinkJwt`** (the JOSE header `kid` of the JWT whose signature was actually verified), NOT from a fresh read of `app_settings.active_signing_key_id`. Persisting `verifiedKid` makes the per-row column truthful about which key signed the underlying JWT; persisting a fresh `active_signing_key_id` instead would open a verify→INSERT rotation race (operator flips `k1`→`k2` between JWT verification and the INSERT; row gets labeled `k2` even though the JWT was actually verified under `k1`; §7.2.2 step 3a never kills it because `row.signing_key_id == active_signing_key_id == k2`). The redeem-link route ADDITIONALLY enforces a redeem-time kid-rotation gate that compares `verifiedKid` to `app_settings.active_signing_key_id` BEFORE the INSERT and rejects with `LINK_REDEEM_KEY_ROTATED` (§12.4) if they don't match — the JWT's signing kid has been rotated away from since mint, so the user must re-open the original signed link to mint a fresh JWT under the new key. Together the verify-time `verifiedKid` capture AND the redeem-time gate ensure the only rows that ever land in `link_sessions` carry a `signing_key_id` that matches the active kid at INSERT time AND truly reflects the kid that signed the JWT.
- `app_settings.active_signing_key_id text NOT NULL DEFAULT 'k1'` — singleton-row, mutated only by the operator rotation workflow.

`validateLinkSession` (§7.2.2) adds a new step between the absolute-expiry check and the cross-show check: `if link_sessions.signing_key_id <> app_settings.active_signing_key_id` → DELETE the row, 401 with code `LINK_SESSION_KEY_ROTATED` (§12.4 — user-facing: "Sessions have been rotated; please open your original signed link again"). Operator rotation workflow (single transaction): (a) generate a new key id (`k2`); (b) write the new secret to the secret store keyed by the new id; (c) `UPDATE app_settings SET active_signing_key_id = 'k2', updated_at = now()`. The single CAS atomically invalidates every live session: every existing `link_sessions` row was minted under `'k1'` (because `signing_key_id` is sourced from the JWT's `verifiedKid`, not a fresh `app_settings` read at INSERT time), so the next request from any of them mismatches `'k2'` and is terminally killed with `LINK_SESSION_KEY_ROTATED`. Newly-minted JWTs sign under `'k2'` and redeem to rows carrying `signing_key_id = 'k2'`. **Redeem-time race coverage:** a JWT signed under `'k1'` that is in-flight when the operator flips to `'k2'` is rejected at redeem time with `LINK_REDEEM_KEY_ROTATED` (the redeem-link route compares `verifiedKid='k1'` against `active_signing_key_id='k2'` BEFORE the INSERT); the user must re-open the original signed link to re-mint a JWT under `'k2'`. The compromised-secret window is bounded by the time it takes the operator to run the UPDATE — not by the 12h cookie TTL — AND by the redeem-link kid-rotation gate that closes the verify→INSERT race. Without these columns AND the redeem-time gate, `JWT_SIGNING_SECRET` rotation is NOT a nuclear option for already-redeemed sessions; with them, it is.

| ------------- | | ----- | |
| `/`                                                       | none                                                                                                                                | Marketing/landing. Optional in v1.
