| `/auth/sign-in`                                           | none                                                                                                                                | Google OAuth entrypoint via Supabase Auth (implemented by plan Task 5.8; reads canonical `?code=` URL param; the `next` regex includes `/me`; pathname canonicalization + bootstrap-surface exclusion). Server Component reads any active session and short-circuits to the validated `next` target (redirect-loop guard); otherwise renders a "Sign in with Google" affordance that calls `supabase.auth.signInWithOAuth({ provider: 'google', options: { redirectTo: '<origin>/auth/callback?next=<validated-next>', queryParams: { prompt: 'select_account' } } })`. **Error-explainer rendering:** the page reads `searchParams.code`, validates against the regex `^[A-Z_]{1,64}$` AND against an explicit allowlist `{ OAUTH_STATE_INVALID, OAUTH_REDIRECT_INVALID }` (the only §12.4 codes this surface emits); on a valid code, the page renders `<ErrorExplainer code={code} />` next to the sign-in CTA so the canonical §12.4 message ("Something interrupted your sign-in…" / "Sign-in landed somewhere we don't recognize…") surfaces inline; on miss / regex-fail / out-of-allowlist, no error block renders (defense against attacker-driven `?code=ARBITRARY_STRING` copy injection). **`next` param validation:** the validator runs FIVE pre-allowlist guards in order, then matches against a canonicalized allowlist. (1) reject non-string / empty / null / undefined; (2) reject if input contains backslash `\`, percent-encoded dot-segment (`%2e%2e`, `%2E%2E`), or any non-printable character (`/[\x00-\x1f\x7f]/`) — these never appear in legitimate paths and avoid URL-parser quirks that may decode `%2e%2e` into `..` mid-resolution; (3) parse via `new URL(input, NEXT_PUBLIC_SITE_ORIGIN)` inside try/catch — the parser canonicalizes dot-segments per RFC 3986; (4) reject if `parsed.origin !== NEXT_PUBLIC_SITE_ORIGIN` — catches absolute URLs (`https://attacker.example/show/x`) AND protocol-relative (`//attacker.example`); (5) explicitly reject `parsed.pathname` matching `^\/show\/[a-z0-9-]+\/p$` — the bootstrap surface mints a session ONLY when the URL fragment carries `#t=<jwt>`, but fragments don't survive the OAuth round-trip (the callback's redirect target is set server-side; the fragment is dropped), so landing post-OAuth on `/show/<slug>/p` is structurally useless and the route is reserved for fragment-bootstrap surface area; (6) match `parsed.pathname` against `^\/(show\/[a-z0-9-]+                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 | admin(\/.\*)? | me(\/.\*)?)$`—`/show/<slug>`slug-only (no sub-paths because the only sub-path is`/p`which step 5 already rejected),`/admin`and any sub-path,`/me`and any sub-path. On match → return canonicalized pathname (query + fragment stripped). On any failure → return literal fallback`/admin`AND log structured operator entry`OAUTH_REDIRECT_INVALID`with the rejected value verbatim. **Why pathname canonicalization:** a regex like`^\/(show | admin | me)(\/[^?#]_)?$`matches the raw input string and cannot resolve`..`segments —`/show/x/../../auth/sign-in`would pass`[^?#]_`and silently land users on`/auth/sign-in`(self-referential loop) or, worse, on attacker-controlled paths after a future allowlist expansion. Parsing via`new URL(...)`resolves dot-segments before the allowlist test, so the test always operates on the canonical form. **Why bootstrap-surface exclusion:**`/show/<slug>/p`cannot be a useful OAuth`next`target — fragments don't survive the OAuth round-trip, so the bootstrap branch's`#t=<jwt>`consumer never fires, and the empty-fragment branch is a dead-end. Including it in the allowlist gives attackers a same-origin landing-pad that could be confused with the bootstrap mint flow. Required positive tests (return canonicalized pathname unchanged):`/show/dci-rpas-2026`, `/admin`, `/admin/show/foo`, `/admin/onboarding/wizard`, `/me`, `/me/profile`. Required negative tests (return `/admin`): `/show/dci-rpas-2026/p`(step 5 — bootstrap surface),`/show/x/../../auth/sign-in`(step 3 canonicalizes to`/auth/sign-in`; step 6 rejects), `/show/x/..`(canonicalizes to`/show/`; step 6 rejects), `https://attacker.example/show/x` (step 4 — origin mismatch), `//attacker.example/show/x` (step 4), `/auth/sign-in` (step 6 — self-referential), `/api/foo` (step 6), `/random` (step 6), `/admin\..\..\foo` (step 2 — backslash), `/show/x%2e%2e/p` (step 2 — percent-encoded dot-segment), `/show/x\x00/p` (step 2 — control char), empty string, `null`, `undefined`. |
| `/auth/callback`                                          | none (sets session on success)                                                                                                      | OAuth code-exchange route handler (canonical error-code URL handoff). Reads `code` and `next` from search params, calls `supabase.auth.exchangeCodeForSession(code)` (Supabase SSR client handles PKCE state/verifier cookies internally), then 302-redirects to the re-validated `next` (defensive belt-and-suspenders against tampering between sign-in and callback). **On any error path → 302 redirect to `/auth/sign-in?code=<§12.4-code>&next=<validated-next>`** where `<§12.4-code>` is `OAUTH_STATE_INVALID` (PKCE / state errors) or `OAUTH_REDIRECT_INVALID` (`next` validation failures) — the param name is `code` (NOT `error`) and carries the canonical §12.4 code so the sign-in page can render `<ErrorExplainer code={code} />` with the matching message. The structured operator log ALSO carries the canonical code. A generic `?error=oauth_callback_failed` flag is rejected because it forces one-size-fits-all error copy regardless of which §12.4 code actually fired. The Supabase `sb-*-auth-token` and `sb-*-auth-token-code-verifier` cookies set by the SDK MUST carry `__Host-`-equivalent attributes (`Path=/`, `Secure`, `HttpOnly`, `SameSite=Lax`, no `Domain`); CI pins this contract so a future SDK update that loosens cookie attributes fails the test. | `/auth/sign-out`                                          | POST, signed-in (any class)                                                                                                         | Atomically clears BOTH cookie families. Calls `supabase.auth.signOut()` (clears the Supabase `sb-*-auth-token` family) AND emits the `Set-Cookie` header from `clearSessionCookie()` in `lib/auth/cookies.ts` so any `__Host-fxav_session` cookie is cleared in the same response. GET → 405 (CSRF defense — sign-out via image tag is not a thing). 302 redirects to `/`. Without the dual-clear, a user who signs out while ALSO carrying a stale link cookie ends up partially signed in: Google session gone, but the residual `__Host-fxav_session` cookie still re-authenticates them as crew on the next page render. | `/me`                                                     | signed-in                                                                                                                           | Lists shows where the user's email matches a `crew_members` row. | `/show/<slug>`                                            | signed-in (Google session) OR redeemed-link session cookie (`__Host-fxav_session`) OR admin                                         | Crew page. **No token-bearing form on this route** — `?t=`/fragment-bearing entrypoints live exclusively at `/show/<slug>/p` per §7.2. **Admin precedence over crew credentials**: when an admin session is present alongside a valid redeemed-link cookie or matching Google session for the same show, the route MUST resolve to the admin viewer (full admin-tier visibility), NOT crew-mode. The auth chain therefore checks admin status FIRST (via the shared `lib/auth/isAdminSession.ts` predicate — `app_metadata.role='admin'` OR email-allowlist match), and only falls through to `validateLinkSession` / `validateGoogleSession` when admin detection returns false. Admins click share links during preview/QA workflows and would otherwise lose admin-only behavior every time they happen to also carry a redeemed-link cookie for the show. The cookie itself is left in place — it remains valid for crew-mode use if `isAdminSession` later returns false. | `/show/<slug>/p#t=<jwt>`                                  | valid JWT (from fragment) + current matching `crew_members` row + tokenVersion match + not in `revoked_links`                       | Crew page via signed link. JWT lives in URL fragment only; immediately exchanged for an HTTP-only session cookie via `/api/auth/redeem-link` (§7.2). The JWT alone is insufficient. | `/api/auth/redeem-link`                                   | POST with JWT in body                                                                                                               | Per-request authz flow (§7.2). On success: sets `__Host-fxav_session` cookie + writes `link_sessions` row. | `/api/asset/diagram/<show-slug>/<revision_id>/<assetKey>` | signed-in OR valid signed-link cookie OR admin (per §7.2 / §7.2.2 / Google validator); show match enforced server-side              | Streams snapshotted diagram-image bytes from the private `diagram-snapshots` Storage bucket. **Canonical URL shape: the `<revision_id>` segment is a BARE UUID — NO `r=` prefix, NO query parameter, NO key=value pair.** The route handler (Plan Task 7.5: `app/api/asset/diagram/[show]/[rev]/[key]/route.ts`) does a literal equality compare of `params.rev` against `shows.diagrams.snapshot_revision_id`. Any URL containing an `r=` prefix in the rev segment MUST 410 (the `r=` token is reserved as a hard-rejection marker so any historical URL that leaked into a cache or a hand-rolled link cannot accidentally resolve). Storage object keys mirror the same shape: `diagram-snapshots/shows/<show_id>/<snapshot_revision_id>/<assetKey>` — the storage prefix is the bare UUID, no `r=`. **The URL is revision-versioned** — every Apply mints a fresh `snapshot_revision_id` and the rendered crew page emits URLs with the current revision. `<assetKey>` is `objectId` (embedded — resolved via the entry's `sheetsRevisionId`/`embeddedFingerprint` pair per §6.11) or `driveFileId` (linked-folder — resolved via `headRevisionId`/`md5Checksum` pair); the route resolves the matching `snapshotPath` AND verifies the URL's revision_id matches `shows.diagrams.snapshot_revision_id` (mismatch → 410). **Every request re-runs the show-auth check.** **Cache header `Cache-Control: private, max-age=0, must-revalidate`** — the browser MUST revalidate with the server on every use. Long-lived freshness on auth-gated assets would let a revoked session keep displaying already-fetched diagrams from local browser cache for the cache lifetime; `must-revalidate` forces an authenticated round-trip every time. Server-side: a successful revalidation with matching auth+revision returns the bytes again (Storage read is cheap and the bytes themselves are immutable per revision); a revoked session gets 410. Drive is NEVER called at request time. **Prior-revision-authoritative-until-promote-succeeds contract:** the prior approved revision stays authoritative until the rename completes and atomically cuts over via the JSONB `pending_revision_id` field. Serving new-revision bytes from a temp prefix would expose an unpromoted revision as the live gallery to crew the moment the new `snapshot_revision_id` was committed — defeating the all-or-nothing-promotion safety guarantee, since a process crash or rename failure mid-cutover would leave mixed canonical/temp/410 visible to crew (some assets renamed to canonical, others still in temp, others missing entirely). **Route precedence (uses `current.*` sub-payload reads)**: (a) verify `params.rev` matches `(shows.diagrams->'current'->>'snapshot_revision_id')::uuid` — literal equality on the bare UUID. **The route NEVER reads `shows.diagrams->'pending'`** — that sub-payload exists only as the cutover staging slot for the post-commit promoter and is invisible to crew. URLs carrying the prior `current.snapshot_revision_id` keep returning 200; URLs carrying the new (still-pending) revision id return 410 until promotion succeeds. (b) Resolve `assetKey` against `shows.diagrams->'current'->'embeddedImages'` and `shows.diagrams->'current'->'linkedFolderItems'` (NEVER from `pending`); read the matching entry's `snapshotPath`. (c) Try the canonical Storage path `diagram-snapshots/shows/<show_id>/<rev>/<assetKey>`; on success return 200. (d) **NO temp-prefix fallback.** On canonical-path 404, return 410 (single missing-bytes contract; never 404). Crew see the placeholder for the missing entry; the prior revision's other entries still resolve from their canonical paths and the gallery degrades gracefully entry-by-entry. Until the post-commit promoter atomically advances the `current` sub-payload to the new revision (after Storage manifest verification passes), the prior revision's bytes AND manifest both remain authoritative end-to-end — there is no window during which crew see partial-canonical / mixed-revision content, AND no window during which a NEW manifest entry pairs with an OLD revision id. |
| `/api/asset/reel/<show-slug>`                             | Same auth requirements as `/api/asset/diagram/...`: signed-in OR valid signed-link cookie OR admin; show match enforced server-side | Streams the opening-reel video. **Same auth + cache contract as the diagram route** — every request re-runs show-auth; `Cache-Control: private, max-age=0, must-revalidate` so revocation propagates immediately. **Revision-pinned byte streaming.** The route reads `shows.opening_reel_drive_file_id`, `shows.opening_reel_drive_modified_time`, `shows.opening_reel_head_revision_id`, AND `shows.opening_reel_mime_type` (all four columns per §4.1). If any of the four is NULL → 410 (single contract for NULL and drift; `mime_type` NULL covers the `OPENING_REEL_NOT_VIDEO` branch). Else: live drift gate via `files.get(reelFileId, fields='modifiedTime,trashed,headRevisionId,md5Checksum')` on every request — if `trashed=true` OR `current.headRevisionId !== shows.opening_reel_head_revision_id` OR `current.modifiedTime !== shows.opening_reel_drive_modified_time` → 410. Streaming path: Pattern A (preferred) `revisions.get(reelFileId, headRevisionId, alt='media')` — exact revision bytes. Pattern B (fallback when Pattern A unavailable for the mimeType) `files.get(alt='media')` then **buffer the full body and recompute md5 against `current.md5Checksum` BEFORE serving any bytes** — comparing headRevisionId before stream is insufficient because Drive can mutate mid-stream; buffer-then-verify is mandatory. v1 doesn't snapshot reel bytes into Storage (large videos, rarely edited per show); the immutable revision pin + buffer-then-verify guarantee crew see only the bytes Doug approved at the last Apply. v2 candidate: snapshot reels into Storage if the live path becomes operationally noisy. | `/api/admin/show/<slug>/apply/<applyId>/status`           | admin role                                                                                                                          | **Idempotent Apply-promotion status endpoint.** GET-only; reads from `pending_snapshot_uploads` joined to `shows.diagrams->'pending'`. Returns `{ status: 'pending' \| 'promoted' \| 'rolled_back' \| 'stuck_admin_repair_required', snapshot_revision_id, ledger_row_id, diagnostics? }` per the §6.11 status mapping. Pure read — does NOT trigger any work; safe to poll on backoff (1s → 2s → 5s, capped at 10s). The operator UI polls this endpoint after receiving the 202 from Apply until status leaves `'pending'`. If the client times out / disconnects between Apply's 202 and the final poll, the operator can resume polling at any time using the durable `applyId` returned in the 202 (which is the same UUID minted as `snapshot_revision_id` and durably stored on the ledger row).                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               |

### 7.4 Role-based field hiding

Server-side, in the data layer. **Role is always derived fresh from the current `crew_members.role_flags`, never from a token claim.**

- The matched `crew_members` row has `LEAD` in `role_flags`, OR the viewer is admin → `viewerRole === 'lead'`. The data fetcher joins `shows_internal` and includes `financials` in the response.
- Otherwise: the data fetcher does not query `shows_internal` at all; `financials` is absent from the response by construction. **`shows.coi_status` is in the response for every crew viewer regardless of role**, because it's operational status (per §4.4). RLS on `shows_internal` (admin-only) is the second line of defense in case the fetcher is wrong; physical separation per §4.4 is the third.

The matched-row lookup is identical for signed-in and signed-link paths: signed-in matches by `email`, signed-link matches by JWT-carried `(showId, name)`. In both paths the _current_ `role_flags` is the source of truth, so a role demotion takes effect on next request — no token revocation required for ops-field hiding (revocation in §7.2.1 is for entirely cutting access, not for downgrading).

This is the **first** line of defense (omit at fetch). RLS is the **second** (deny if a non-admin client tries to query directly). URL obscurity is **not** a line of defense in this app.

### 7.5 Doug's preview impersonation

When an admin opens `/admin/show/<slug>/preview/<crew-id>`, the server fetches data **as if** the viewer were that crew member (same role-based filtering applied). A sticky banner reads `Previewing as Eric Weiss (A1) · [Exit preview]` and the URL is admin-only. Crew never see this banner; admins always do.

---

## 8. Crew page UX

Direction **B** from the brainstorm: time-aware home + drill-down tiles. Mobile-primary at ~390px target width; desktop is supported but secondary.

**Realtime subscription contract (Broadcast topic, NOT postgres_changes; composite version token).** The crew page is a **Next.js App Router Server Component** (`app/show/[slug]/page.tsx` calls `getShowForViewer` directly server-side via the service role per §7.4 — no client data layer, no TanStack/React Query, and crucially **no Supabase Auth session for redeemed-link viewers**). The bridge MUST NOT use `postgres_changes` because (a) `postgres_changes` subscriptions are RLS-gated and a redeemed-link viewer carries only a `__Host-fxav_session` cookie — they have no Supabase Auth session that RLS could authorize, and (b) `crew_member_auth` is admin-only per §4.3, so even if a viewer COULD authenticate to the channel, RLS would deny the subscription.

**Transport: server-owned Realtime Broadcast topic, viewer-opaque payload.** Every crew page mounts a thin client component `<ShowRealtimeBridge showId={...} slug={...} renderVersion={string} />` (implementation: `components/realtime/ShowRealtimeBridge.tsx` + `lib/realtime/subscribeToShow.ts` + new server-side publish helper `lib/realtime/showInvalidation.ts` per plan Task 4.16) that subscribes to a SINGLE Supabase Realtime Broadcast topic named `show:<showId>:invalidation`. The bridge does NOT subscribe to any database table directly — it has no `from(...)` access at all. Publish-side: Phase 2 sync writes (cron / push / Apply commit per §5.2 / §5.5.1 / §6.8.3) AND auth-mutation triggers (DB triggers on `crew_member_auth.current_token_version` UPDATE and on `crew_members.role_flags` UPDATE) call a single helper `publishShowInvalidation(tx, showId)` that resolves the current `viewer_version_token` (see finding 2 below) and emits `pg_notify('realtime:broadcast', json_build_object('topic', 'show:<showId>:invalidation', 'event', 'invalidate', 'payload', json_build_object('show_id', <showId>, 'version_token', <token>))::text)`. **The publishing helper is the SOLE producer of these notifies; no other call site writes to the `realtime` schema.**

**Topic ACL.** Broadcast topics on Supabase Realtime are gated by a JWT verified at WebSocket-handshake time. The bridge mints a short-lived **Broadcast subscriber JWT** by calling `POST /api/realtime/subscriber-token` (a new server route, plan Task 4.16) which verifies the request's `__Host-fxav_session` cookie via the existing `validateLinkSession` (signed-link viewers) or `validateGoogleSession` (signed-in viewers) helpers, derives `(showId, crewMemberId)`, and returns a Supabase Realtime JWT with custom claims `{ show_id: <uuid>, sub: <crewMemberId>, exp: now+5min }`. The Realtime server's topic ACL policy (configured in Supabase Dashboard → Realtime → Authorization, or equivalently a Postgres `realtime.broadcasts_authorization` row): `topic ~ '^show:([0-9a-f-]{36}):invalidation$' AND ((regexp_match(topic, '^show:([0-9a-f-]{36}):invalidation$'))[1])::uuid = (auth.jwt() ->> 'show_id')::uuid`. Admins use the standard admin path (Supabase Auth session with `role='admin'` claim) and their own Broadcast policy admits any `show:*:invalidation` topic. The topic name is INTENTIONALLY non-secret — knowing the showId is not access; only a server-issued JWT subscribes.

**Payload is viewer-opaque.** The Broadcast message body is `{ "type": "invalidate", "show_id": "<uuid>", "version_token": "<monotonic-token>" }` — NO sheet contents, NO crew names, NO role flags, NO auth state. The bridge's only response is to call `router.refresh()` (which re-executes the Server Component server-side, where `getShowForViewer` re-applies role-flag filters using the service role per §7.4). The viewer learns nothing from the message they didn't already have permission to learn from a re-render.

**Composite `viewer_version_token`.** The token MUST advance on EVERY mutation that could change what a viewer sees — including auth-only mutations that don't touch `shows`. A version derived solely from `shows.last_synced_at` would leave auth-only mutations (Issue New Link, role_flags edits without a paired `UPDATE shows`) un-versioned and let the `T0 → T1` catch-up false-positive-clean. The corrected token is **composite**: `viewer_version_token := GREATEST(shows.last_synced_at, MAX(crew_member_auth.last_changed_at) FOR show_id, MAX(crew_members.last_changed_at) FOR show_id)` for the show, encoded as a stringified ISO-8601 timestamp (or epoch ms) — comparable for equality and ordering. Two new columns are added in §4.1 (Plan Task 2.2 propagation):

- `crew_member_auth.last_changed_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now()` — bumped to `now()` by an UPDATE trigger on every UPDATE of any other column. (The trigger MUST exclude its own update to avoid recursion; `WHEN (OLD.* IS DISTINCT FROM NEW.*)` predicate.)
- `crew_members.last_changed_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now()` — same trigger pattern, fires on UPDATE of any other column.

A SECURITY-DEFINER SQL helper `viewer_version_token(show_id uuid) returns text` computes the composite from the three sources. **Plan Task 2.2 (DDL) and Task 2.5 (introspection) carry these two columns + their UPDATE triggers + the helper function as a single unit; the trigger DDL MUST appear in the canonical migrations and not as application-layer code.** Live cron / push / manual Apply ALWAYS bump `shows.last_synced_at` per §5.2, so the existing Phase 2 path keeps working; the new columns + triggers add coverage for auth-only mutations.

The `/api/show/[slug]/version` route (Plan Task 4.16) returns `{ version_token: <composite> }` from a single SECURITY-INVOKER SQL call to `viewer_version_token(<showId>)` — no auth-gated payload, single-string response. The Server Component renders `<div data-render-version="<token>">` on the page root using the same composite token captured at SSR time. After `subscribe()` resolves AND on reconnect events, the bridge calls `GET /api/show/[slug]/version`, compares to the SSR'd `data-render-version`, and on mismatch calls `router.refresh()` once. This closes the (T0, T1) render-vs-subscribe race AND covers reconnect catch-up AND covers auth-only mutations whose effects can be missed by a Broadcast that fired before subscribe-completion.

**Render-vs-subscribe race fix.** Composite-token catch-up replaces any `last_synced_at`-only logic. Same flow: SSR renders `data-render-version`; bridge subscribes; on subscribe-success the bridge fetches `/api/show/[slug]/version`; mismatch → single `router.refresh()`. The Supabase Realtime client's `system.reconnected` event re-runs the same catch-up so a transient WebSocket drop that suppressed broadcasts while disconnected is reconciled on resume. **The catch-up MUST read the LATEST `renderVersion` for the page, not a stale closure value.** The bridge maintains `renderVersionRef = useRef(renderVersion)` updated on every render; reconnect / subscribe-success / renewal-success catch-up handlers all read `renderVersionRef.current` at call time. Without this, every handler closes over the T0 `renderVersion` from the bridge's first mount; after a `router.refresh()` advances the SSR-rendered token to T1, a subsequent disconnect+reconnect would force an unnecessary `router.refresh()` because the closed-over comparison `T0 !== T1` looks stale.

**JWT renewal on disconnect / channel-error.** The subscriber JWT signs with `exp = now+5min` — page sessions open longer than 5 minutes will eventually carry an expired token over the WebSocket. Without an explicit renewal flow, any routine WiFi blip past the 5-minute mark drops the subscription silently and the bridge stops delivering invalidations until the user navigates. The bridge MUST therefore listen for both Supabase `system` `disconnected` events AND any channel-level auth-failure error event (subscribe-status callback returning `'CHANNEL_ERROR'` / `'TIMED_OUT'` / `'CLOSED'`) and on either signal run the renewal sequence: re-`POST /api/realtime/subscriber-token` (the route enforces idempotency — multiple renewals within the same client session are fine), `client.realtime.setAuth(newJwt)`, `removeChannel(oldChannel)` and re-create the channel via `subscribeToShow(showId, newJwt, onInvalidate)` with the same topic name `show:<showId>:invalidation`, AFTER the new `subscribe()` resolves run the `/api/show/[slug]/version` catch-up so any invalidations missed during the disconnect window are reconciled, and on success clear any "stale connection" UI state — the entire flow is transparent to the user (no pop-up, no manual action). On renewal mint-failure: log `SHOW_REALTIME_JWT_RENEWED` with `outcome: 'failed'` (admin-log-only; §12.4) and fall back to no-op; the next navigation or `router.refresh()` self-heals via the 410 → bootstrap path. Successful renewals log `SHOW_REALTIME_JWT_RENEWED` with `outcome: 'success'`. Renewal does NOT retry-loop — a single failure terminates the renewal sequence and the next disconnect/error event triggers a fresh attempt.

**Renewal is a single-flight state machine — channel-generation gating is mandatory.** A naive renewal flow re-triggers itself on the channel it is intentionally tearing down: `removeChannel(oldChannel)` synchronously fires a `'CLOSED'` status callback on the retired channel, which (without gating) re-enters the renewal path while the previous renewal is still mid-flight, producing overlapping JWT mints, overlapping `setAuth` calls, and a thrashing channel-create/destroy cycle that never converges. The bridge MUST implement single-flight gating with TWO refs and ONE invariant:

- `currentChannelGenerationRef: useRef<number>` — monotonically increments on every new `subscribe()` call. Each channel and each subscribe-status / system-event callback closure captures the generation number it was created at; callbacks compare `closureGeneration === currentChannelGenerationRef.current` and short-circuit (return) when not equal.
- `isRenewingRef: useRef<boolean>` — set to `true` at the START of the renewal sequence (BEFORE `removeChannel(oldChannel)` is called) AND only set back to `false` AFTER the new channel reaches `SUBSCRIBED` status (renewal-success path) OR the renewal terminates with `outcome: 'failed'` (mint-failure path). When `true`, every additional disconnect / error / CLOSED event that arrives is dropped (return early) — the in-flight renewal owns the renewal lock.
- Mandatory ordering: the renewal sequence increments `currentChannelGenerationRef.current` IMMEDIATELY BEFORE calling `removeChannel(oldChannel)`. The synchronous `'CLOSED'` callback from the remove fires under the OLD generation, the closure's generation comparison fails (`oldGen !== currentChannelGenerationRef.current`), and the callback returns without touching renewal state. The same gating drops any straggling `'CHANNEL_ERROR'` / `'TIMED_OUT'` / `'CLOSED'` event that arrives on the retired channel after `removeChannel` returns control.
- The catch-up version-fetch (run AFTER the new `subscribe()` resolves) does NOT bypass the gating — it reads `currentChannelGenerationRef.current` at call time and is therefore self-cancelling on a subsequent renewal that supersedes it.

Without this gating, a rapid disconnect → reconnect → disconnect cycle (commonly observed on flaky WiFi) produces 3+ overlapping renewal flows, multiple subscriber-token mints in flight, channel-thrash, and the bridge effectively stops delivering invalidations until the user navigates. With it, EXACTLY ONE renewal is in flight at any time regardless of how many disconnect/CLOSED events arrive during the renewal window.

**Unmount-safe cleanup ordering.** The single-flight gating above prevents in-flight renewals from re-entering during steady-state disconnect events but does NOT cover the unmount path — the `useEffect([showId])` cleanup function produces its own re-entry vector. When React invokes cleanup (StrictMode dev-cycle dismount, ordinary client navigation away, parent unmount during route transition, HMR), the cleanup calls `removeChannel(currentChannel)` whose synchronous `'CLOSED'` callback (per Supabase JS client documented behavior) would otherwise enter the renewal path against an unmounted React tree — leaking a channel, leaking a JWT, and risking `setState` on a dead component. The bridge therefore holds a third ref `isMountedRef: useRef<boolean>` and the `useEffect` cleanup MUST execute in this exact order: (1) `isMountedRef.current = false`; (2) increment `currentChannelGenerationRef.current` (so the synchronous `'CLOSED'` from step 4 captures a stale generation); (3) cancel the pending `router.refresh` debounce timer; (4) only THEN `removeChannel(currentChannel)`. Every status / system / disconnect / renewal-step callback's first guard is `if (!isMountedRef.current || closureGeneration !== currentChannelGenerationRef.current) return;`. The renewal flow's mint-then-subscribe sequence ALSO checks `isMountedRef.current` after each `await` boundary (post-mint `fetch`, post-`setAuth`, post-`subscribe`) — an unmount during an in-flight renewal aborts the renewal silently before creating a new channel. Regression tests cover (a) StrictMode dev-cycle unmount → no spurious renewal-mint; (b) ordinary client navigation → no `/api/realtime/subscriber-token` request after cleanup; (c) unmount during in-flight renewal → renewal aborts cleanly with no leaked channel.

**Per-Apply invalidation dedup via 100ms client-side debounce.** A single Apply that touches `shows` AND multiple `crew_member_auth` rows AND multiple `crew_members` rows fires the publish path once per row plus once for the `UPDATE shows` — an Apply that touched 5 crew rows + 2 auth rows + the shows row emits 8 Broadcasts, each of which would naively trigger a separate `router.refresh()`. The bridge therefore wraps every Broadcast `onInvalidate` callback in a 100ms `setTimeout` debounce: each new Broadcast clears any pending timer and schedules a new one, so the burst of triggers fired within a single transaction's commit window coalesces into ONE `router.refresh()`. The version-mismatch catch-up paths (subscribe-success and `system.reconnected`) bypass the debounce — they're already a single deliberate refresh by construction. The `useEffect` cleanup MUST cancel any pending timer on unmount. Server-side AFTER-STATEMENT triggers + transaction-local touched-show queue were considered but rejected for v1 in favor of the simpler client-side approach; the UX outcome is identical (one refresh per Apply) and the failure surface is smaller (no Postgres deferred-trigger lifecycle).

**Shared `resolveShowViewer` auth helper.** Both `/api/realtime/subscriber-token` and `/api/show/[slug]/version` MUST gate on a single helper `lib/auth/resolveShowViewer(req, slug)` that mirrors the `/show/<slug>` Server Component's auth chain — `isAdminSession(req)` FIRST (`app_metadata.role='admin'` OR canonicalized email allowlist match — admin precedence), then `validateLinkSession`, then `validateGoogleSession`. The discriminated-union return shape is FIVE-armed: `{ kind: 'admin' | 'crew_link' | 'crew_google' | 'denied' | 'forbidden', email?, show_id?, crew_member_id?, reason? }`. `denied` is returned when no credentials apply (no `__Host-fxav_session` cookie + no Supabase Auth session, OR the slug doesn't resolve to any show row). `forbidden` is returned when the validator chain succeeded for a DIFFERENT show than the slug-resolved show — `validateLinkSession` or `validateGoogleSession` returned `success` but their resolved `show_id` does NOT match the slug-resolved show (cross-show cookie reuse, cross-show subscriber-token request). The two arms map to distinct HTTP status codes: `denied` → **401** (no credentials — re-prompt for sign-in), `forbidden` → **403** (credentials valid, wrong show — different operator response and different admin-info vs admin-debug log severity). Conflating them is forbidden because the downstream UX surfaces, log severity, and security-telemetry signal all diverge. Both routes' first action is `await resolveShowViewer(req, slug)`; `denied` → 401 (subscriber-token uses `SHOW_REALTIME_BROADCAST_AUTH_FAILED`; version route uses a generic 401), `forbidden` → 403 with a distinct cross-show code (subscriber-token: `SHOW_REALTIME_CROSS_SHOW_FORBIDDEN`; version: `SHOW_VERSION_CROSS_SHOW_FORBIDDEN`), admin/crew_link/crew_google → 200 (subscriber-token mints JWT with `viewer_kind` claim; version returns the composite token). This closes three bugs: (a) admins-via-allowlist (no `app_metadata.role='admin'`) could not subscribe under the prior ad-hoc form because the routes only ran the crew-side validators; (b) cross-show probes (signed in for show A, requesting `/api/show/B/version`) were not rejected; (c) under a 4-armed union (`denied` covering both no-credentials and cross-show), the routes could not distinguish 401 from 403 deterministically — the new `forbidden` arm makes the discrimination structural rather than a route-side guess.

The bridge renders nothing (`return null`); on subscription failure it logs a warning (code `SHOW_REALTIME_SUBSCRIPTION_FAILED` — admin-log-only; see §12.4) and falls back to no-op (no retry storm; v1 fails open). On Broadcast-subscriber-token mint failure it logs `SHOW_REALTIME_BROADCAST_AUTH_FAILED` (admin-log-only; §12.4). On JWT renewal events it logs `SHOW_REALTIME_JWT_RENEWED` with `outcome` (admin-log-only; §12.4). **No polling fallback** — tests that exercise live sync (Task 4.12 step 4b end-to-end) MUST require a real Supabase Realtime Broadcast mock and assert the page re-renders via `router.refresh()` within 2s WITHOUT `page.reload()`. An Apply that flips `crew_members.role_flags` from `['A1']` to `['A2']` MUST propagate to an open viewer's page within 2s without manual refresh; LEAD-only tiles MUST disappear from a demoted viewer's page on the next Broadcast event. **An admin "Issue new link" click for Alice (which mutates `crew_member_auth` only, NOT `shows`) MUST also propagate to Alice's open page within 2s** — the `crew_member_auth` UPDATE trigger fires the publish helper, the Broadcast goes out, the bridge calls `router.refresh()`, and the catch-up `version_token` (now incorporating `crew_member_auth.last_changed_at`) closes any T0/T1 race. The auth check happens at server fetch time (`getShowForViewer` per §7.2), not at subscription time — so a revoked-mid-session user still gets a fresh server render → 410 → bootstrap page.

### 8.1 Section inventory

**Top:**

- **Header strip:** show title + "you" badge (`EW · A1`). Tap "you" badge → show role legend tooltip.
- **Right Now card:** time-aware. See §8.2.

**Tile grid (2 cols on mobile, 3+ on desktop):**

- **Lodging tile** — your hotel only (filtered from `hotel_reservations` by `names` substring match on viewer name). Shows hotel, check-in→check-out, confirmation #.
- **Venue tile** — name, address line, loading dock, "Open in Maps" link, Diagrams gallery entry point.
- **Schedule tile** — days filtered by `date_restriction.kind`:
  - `none` → all days (travel-in, set, show day(s), travel-out).
  - `explicit` → only the listed dates plus a small "Restricted to <dates>" sublabel.
  - `unknown_asterisk` → **per-day schedule is hidden entirely.** The tile renders a single message: "Your assigned days aren't confirmed yet. Doug needs to add a parenthetical like `(6/24 and 6/26 ONLY)` to your name in the sheet — once he does, this will fill in." This is a deliberate refusal to render guesses; the alternative (showing all days with a small warning) was rejected in adversarial review because crew might rely on incorrect call times. The same warning surfaces loudly in Doug's parse panel per §6.6 with a one-click report-to-Eric path; Doug fixes the sheet, the next sync clears the state.
    Within each day (when shown), call time is extracted from the inline `TIME / AGENDA` cell when available.
    **Scope tile visibility — canonical rule.** A single shared predicate `SCOPE_TILE_VISIBILITY_RULE` governs every scope tile and is referenced verbatim by Task 4.6, Task 4.12's capability-predicate matrix, and the §17.1 acceptance criteria. There is **exactly one rule**, no per-task variants:

- `audioScopeVisible = hasA1 || hasLead` — LEAD is scope-tile-eligible on Audio per §8.1.
- `videoScopeVisible = hasV1 || hasLead` — LEAD is scope-tile-eligible on Video per §8.1.
- `lightingScopeVisible = hasL1 || hasLead` — LEAD is scope-tile-eligible on Lighting per §8.1 (amended 2026-05-13; see Amendment §8.1-A1 below).

> **Amendment §8.1-A1 (ratified 2026-05-13):** The Lighting scope tile is now LEAD-readable, symmetric with Audio and Video. The original rule excluded LEAD ("lighting is a discipline LEADs don't manage hands-on"), but LEADs need read-in to lighting scope details to coordinate across disciplines — the operational-separation rationale did not survive review. The AVL triad is now uniformly `hasX || hasLead`. Code (`lib/visibility/scopeTiles.ts:lightingScopeVisible`), unit tests (`tests/visibility/scopeTiles.test.ts`), the capability-flip matrix (`lib/visibility/capabilityTransitions.ts` `hasLead × hasL1` entry), and the e2e suite (`tests/e2e/scope-tiles.spec.ts`) all reflect the amendment. The matrix's single-flip definitive deltas for hasLead and hasL1 are now both empty on the Lighting axis (Lighting is jointly unlocked, conditionally on the held predicate); the composed-flip tests cover the actual visibility transitions.

`hasA1`, `hasV1`, `hasL1`, `hasLead` are atomic-flag predicates over `crew_members.role_flags[]` per §6.6 (`hasA1 = role_flags.includes('A1') || role_flags.includes('A2')`, etc.). Compound viewers like `['LEAD','A1']` get Audio + Video + Lighting + Financials. LEAD-only viewers (`['LEAD']`) see Audio AND Video AND Lighting scope tiles AND Financials unconditionally.

- **Audio scope tile** — visible per `audioScopeVisible`. Aggregates `rooms[*].audio` across GS, breakouts, additional rooms.
- **Video scope tile** — visible per `videoScopeVisible`. Same for `rooms[*].video`.
- **Lighting scope tile** — visible per `lightingScopeVisible`. Same for `rooms[*].lighting`.
- **Crew tile** — list of all crew on this show with role + phone + email tap-to-call/email. Always visible.
- **Contacts tile** — venue contact, in-house AV. Always visible.
- **Transport tile** — visibility is the OR of two branches over the canonical TransportationRow contract: (a) `transportation.driver_name === viewer.name` (the assigned driver), OR (b) `viewer.name ∈ transportation.schedule[*].assigned_names[]` for ANY entry in the schedule array (any tagged passenger or co-driver, even if they are not the primary driver). `assigned_names: string[]` is a first-class field on every `TransportScheduleEntry` — it travels through the parser output, ParseResult, `transportation.schedule` JSONB, `getShowForViewer` projection, and tile predicate without dropping anywhere in the pipeline. Shows vehicle, license plate, color, parking, schedule. Otherwise hidden.
- **Show status tile** — visible to every crew viewer. Carries `shows.coi_status`, dress code, venue notes, and other always-public operational signals. COI lives here, not in Financials, because it's ops, not billing (§4.4).
- **Financials tile** — LEAD only. PO#, Proposal, Invoice, Invoice Notes from `shows_internal.financials`. Hidden entirely for non-LEAD (omitted from data fetch per §7.4 — the JSONB column isn't even queried for them).
- **Pack list tile** — visible to every crew viewer **on set day, strike day, and the travel-out day** when `shows.pull_sheet IS NOT NULL`. Hidden on show days (techs are running the show, not packing). Hidden entirely for shows whose sheet has no PULL SHEET tab. Per-day visibility further filtered by viewer's `stage_restriction` per §6.6: a crew member with `stage_restriction.kind === 'explicit'` and `stages = ["Load In", "Set"]` sees the tile only on set day; with `stages = ["Load Out", "Strike"]` only on strike (and travel-out if their schedule includes it). Unrestricted crew (`stage_restriction.kind === 'none'`) see it on every set/strike/travel-out day. Renders cases in `pull_sheet[]` order; "Show more" disclosure beyond 12 cases. Each case's items render in source order.
- **Notes tile** — any block-level `notes` content, aggregated into a single "Things to know" card.

**Footer:**

- `Last updated <relative time> · live from sheet`
- `Something looks wrong?` link — opens the report dialog (§13.1 surface 4 for crew, §13.1 surface 1-3 for admin views). Both go to the same `/api/report` endpoint with the appropriate body template (§13.2).

### 8.2 Right Now card — time-aware AND viewer-aware states

The card at the top of the page swaps content based on **(today, show dates, viewer's date_restriction)** together. **Viewer date_restriction always takes precedence over show-wide state** — a crew member with `unknown_asterisk` or with explicit days that don't include today must never see "Today: Show day 1" implying they're working.

**State precedence** (top match wins):

| State                   | Trigger                                                                                                                                                                    | Renders                                                                                                                                                                                   |
| ----------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `viewer_unconfirmed`    | `viewer.date_restriction.kind === 'unknown_asterisk'`                                                                                                                      | "Your assigned days aren't confirmed yet" + same body as the schedule tile in §8.1. Replaces every show-wide state.                                                                       |
| `viewer_after_last_day` | `viewer.date_restriction.kind === 'explicit'` AND today > max(`viewer.days`)                                                                                               | "Your assignment is complete · show wraps <travelOut>." Evaluated **before** `viewer_off_day` so a restricted crew member never sees a "Your next assigned day: ???" pointing at nothing. |
| `viewer_off_day`        | `viewer.date_restriction.kind === 'explicit'` AND today is NOT in `days` AND today < max(`viewer.days`) AND today is within the show span (`travelIn ≤ today ≤ travelOut`) | "Not scheduled today" + "Your next assigned day: <date> · <relative time> away" — `<next>` is guaranteed to exist because `viewer_after_last_day` already caught the past-final-day case. |
| `viewer_off_day_pre`    | `viewer.date_restriction.kind === 'explicit'` AND today is BEFORE viewer's first assigned day AND today < travelIn                                                         | "In N days · Your first day: <date>"                                                                                                                                                      |
| `pre_travel`            | today < travelIn − 1 day AND viewer is unrestricted or today is before viewer's first assigned day                                                                         | "In N days · Travel in <weekday>" + "Hotel: <hotel>"                                                                                                                                      |
| `travel_in_day`         | today === travelIn AND (viewer unrestricted OR today is in `viewer.days`)                                                                                                  | "Today: Travel in" + "Hotel check-in: <hotel>, <time>"                                                                                                                                    |
| `set_day`               | today === setDay AND (viewer unrestricted OR today is in `viewer.days`)                                                                                                    | "Today: Set day" + "Load-in: <time> at <venue>"                                                                                                                                           |
| `show_day_n`            | today === showDays[n] AND (viewer unrestricted OR today is in `viewer.days`)                                                                                               | "Today: Show day N of M" + "Call: <time> · <room>" + "Strike: <time>" if last day                                                                                                         |
| `travel_out_day`        | today === travelOut AND (viewer unrestricted OR today is in `viewer.days`)                                                                                                 | "Today: Travel out" + "Hotel check-out: <hotel>"                                                                                                                                          |
| `post_show`             | today > travelOut OR today > viewer's last assigned day                                                                                                                    | "Wrapped <relative time> ago" with link to "view as archive"                                                                                                                              |
| `unknown`               | one or more show dates not parseable but at least one is                                                                                                                   | "Show details: <travelIn> – <travelOut>" with whatever was parsed; missing values render as "—".                                                                                          |
| `dateless`              | no parseable show date at all                                                                                                                                              | "Show details unavailable. Check the sheet's DATES block." Card uses the stale-tint color scheme to signal something is wrong.                                                            |

The first eight rows (`viewer_unconfirmed` through `post_show`) are evaluated only when show dates are parseable. `unknown` and `dateless` are date-data fallbacks that override everything else.

**Compound transitions** (entered from one state, transitioning to another while data also changes):

| From → To                                                                                          | Animation                                                                 |
| -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `pre_travel` → `travel_in_day` (date rollover)                                                     | Crossfade card body; preserve card height.                                |
| `show_day_n` → `show_day_n+1`                                                                      | Same — crossfade body.                                                    |
| `viewer_off_day` → `show_day_n` (today rolls into a viewer's assigned day)                         | Crossfade body.                                                           |
| `show_day_n` → `viewer_off_day` (today rolls out of a viewer's assigned day)                       | Crossfade body.                                                           |
| Any → `unknown` (sync error mid-show)                                                              | Card morphs to last-good state with a "stale" tint, no animation.         |
| Doug fixes `unknown_asterisk` in sheet → next sync → `viewer_unconfirmed` becomes a concrete state | Crossfade body.                                                           |
| Sync update mid-state (data change, state same)                                                    | Bumps a small "updated" pulse on changed fields. No card-level animation. |

### 8.3 Empty state discipline

Per the brainstorm, every drill-down section must be useful even when Doug hasn't filled it in. Concrete rules:

- **Required fields missing** (e.g., venue name): the section renders a "Doug hasn't filled this in yet" placeholder, not an empty card. The placeholder text is intentionally human, not "field undefined."
- **Optional fields missing — per-field empty-treatment**: empty-treatment is field-specific, not blanket. The default rule for generic optional text fields (`event_details.power`, `internet`, `keynote_requirements`, `rooms.scenic`, `notes` columns, etc.) treats `null`, `''`, `'TBD'`, `'N/A'`, `'TBA'` (case-insensitive after trim) as "not filled in" and omits the field — no "—" or "TBD" rendered to crew. **Exception — `event_details.opening_reel`**: per §10's render contract, the renderer FIRST strips all `https?://drive.google.com|docs.google.com/...` URL substrings from the cell value AND removes orphaned `-` connector tokens around them, THEN evaluates emptiness. After stripping: `'YES'`, `'MAYBE'`, `'N/A'`, `'TBA'`, `'BACKUP ONLY'`, and any other free-text residue ARE crew-visible status text rendered as `Opening reel: <stripped value>`; ONLY `'TBD'` (and bare empty / null) AND values whose stripped residue is empty (the cell was a pure URL) are hidden. Mixed values like `'YES - <drive-url>'` render BOTH the URL-stripped text status (`Opening reel: YES`) AND the inline video (M7 only). The implementation lives in `lib/visibility/emptyState.ts` as a per-field dispatch table; new fields with non-default empty rules are added to that table, not as inline checks in tile components. The URL-stripping helper lives at `lib/visibility/openingReelText.ts` (or equivalent) and is the single source of truth for what crew see — tiles MUST import it rather than rendering the raw cell value.
- **Whole tile missing** (e.g., no transport assigned to viewer): tile not rendered. Grid reflows.
- **Stale sync** (per §5.4): tile renders last-good; the page-level footer carries the staleness signal, not per-tile.

### 8.4 Dimensional invariants (page layout)

Mobile target viewport: 390px wide.

- The Right Now card is full-width (`100%` minus container padding) and has a fluid height — content-driven, not fixed. Min-height: 96px to prevent sub-card collapse on minimal data.
- The tile grid is 2 columns on viewports < 640px, 3 columns 640–1024px, 4 columns > 1024px. Tiles within a row stretch to equal height (`align-items: stretch`).
- Each tile has a min-height of 96px. Content overflows internally with a "see more" disclosure on tiles that naturally exceed 240px.
- The footer is sticky to the bottom of the viewport when the content is short; flows naturally when the content is long.

These invariants must be verified with a browser-rendered assertion (Playwright or chrome-devtools `evaluate_script`) calling `getBoundingClientRect()` per `data-testid` — jsdom alone is not sufficient (per global CLAUDE.md guidance).

### 8.5 Responsive desktop posture

Tiles regroup into a 3-or-4-column grid. The Right Now card stays full-width above the grid. No tabs, no sidebar. The page reads as a long single-column scroll on mobile and as a denser dashboard on desktop. No fundamentally different IA per viewport.

---

## 9. Doug's admin UX

The audience for this surface is non-technical. Every screen assumes Doug doesn't know what a service account is, what RLS is, or what a token version is. Failures are described in plain language with one obvious next step (either "fix this in your sheet" or "tell Eric"). Every error code in §12.4 has a paired user-facing message; the codes never appear in the UI text Doug sees.

### 9.0 First-visit onboarding wizard

The first time Doug visits `/admin` (no folder configured, no shows in DB), he sees a three-step wizard. The wizard's purpose is to make the leap from "I have a Google Sheet" to "the app shows my crew their pages" feel obvious and unblockable.

**Step 1 — "Share your show folder."**

A single screen with the service-account email displayed in a large, copyable form, along with plain-English instructions:

> 1. In Google Drive, find the folder where you keep your show sheets (or make a new one).
> 2. Click "Share" on the folder.
> 3. Paste this email and give it Viewer access: `<service-account-email>` _[copy button]_
> 4. Come back here and click "I've shared the folder."

A small disclosure ("What's this email?") expands to two sentences explaining that it's the app's identity in your Drive — it can only see what you share with it, and only the folder you pick.

**Pre-onboarding "Start over" affordance.** Every wizard step (1, 2, 3) — and `/admin` itself when in wizard-mode — renders a small "Start over" link/button (admin-gated). Clicking it always rotates `pending_wizard_session_id` AND `pending_wizard_session_at`, AND purges ALL onboarding surfaces (`pending_syncs WHERE wizard_session_id IS NOT NULL`, `pending_ingestions WHERE wizard_session_id IS NOT NULL`, `onboarding_scan_manifest`) in a single transaction, then redirects back to step 1. This is the operator's recovery path when the wizard tab was closed mid-flight and they want to start fresh — without it, partial pre-onboarding state from a prior abandoned attempt would survive indefinitely (since the post-onboarding `/admin/settings` "Re-run Setup" affordance is gated on `watched_folder_id IS NOT NULL` and is therefore unreachable on first visit). See §4.5 lifecycle for the full SQL contract. After onboarding succeeds the affordance disappears — restart goes through `/admin/settings` instead.

**24-hour auto-rotate (multi-batch finalize gate).** On every wizard-step page-load, the server checks `pending_wizard_session_at < now() - interval '24 hours' AND NOT EXISTS (SELECT 1 FROM wizard_finalize_checkpoints WHERE wizard_session_id = app_settings.pending_wizard_session_id AND batches_completed > 0)`. If both clauses hold, the session is treated as abandoned and the same purge-and-rotate transaction the "Start over" button runs is executed automatically before rendering. The user sees a fresh step-1 with no surviving stale rows. Auto-rotate is silent (no flash banner). **If the staleness clause holds BUT the checkpoint clause fails** (i.e., a multi-batch finalize started and at least one batch committed before the operator paused), auto-rotate is SUPPRESSED: the wizard renders the in-flight step (typically the post-Apply progress page) with a "Resume finalize" affordance and a "Cleanup abandoned finalize" admin action — see §4.5 prong 3 for the cleanup transaction's three-step contract (delete in-flight `published=false` `shows` rows joined via `onboarding_scan_manifest`, delete the checkpoint row, then run the purge-rotate). All staleness predicates — auto-rotate's `pending_wizard_session_at < now() - interval '24 hours'`, the suppression-gate's `c.batches_completed > 0` join, the cleanup helper's session-staleness CAS, and the cleanup helper's checkpoint-recency clause — are evaluated against Postgres `now()` inside the cleanup transaction (no `Date.now()` is read in the cleanup helper or its route handler — see §4.5 prong 3). The route handler MUST NOT pre-screen with a `Date.now()` check before calling the helper; the helper is the sole authority on staleness, and any pre-screen would re-introduce app-vs-DB clock skew at the boundary. The §12.4 `WIZARD_FINALIZE_BATCHES_PENDING` admin-log entry surfaces this state so operators see in `sync_log` that the auto-rotate was suppressed and a manual cleanup action is required. **Render-time fresh-settings invariant.** `purgeAndRotateIfStale` runs BEFORE the wizard render path (`renderWizardOrFinalizeReentry`); its return shape carries the post-mutation `app_settings` row (read inside the same SQL transaction as the rotate/purge so it reflects authoritative state regardless of whether the rotate fired) AND a `rotated` flag. The render path MUST consume the helper-returned `settings`, never the pre-call capture from the page handler — passing pre-mutation `settings` (a W1 id and timestamp the helper just rotated to W2) would cause `renderWizardOrFinalizeReentry` to look up a checkpoint or staged-row state for a session that no longer owns any rows. This invariant applies symmetrically in the suppressed-by-finalize-gate path (the helper returns the unchanged W1 row; the render path correctly observes the live W1 checkpoint) and in the normal not-stale path (the helper returns the unchanged row; the render path proceeds against current state).

**Step 2 — "Verify."**

When Doug clicks "I've shared the folder," the app asks him to paste the folder URL or ID and verifies in real time:

- **Success path:** the app calls `files.list` against the folder, confirms read access, and displays a green check with the folder name and a count of sheets it found. "Found _N_ sheets in _<folder name>_. Ready to bring them in?"
- **Common failure paths**, each with one specific fix message:
  - Folder URL malformed → "That doesn't look like a Google Drive folder URL. It should look like `https://drive.google.com/drive/folders/...`."
  - Folder not shared with the service account → "We can't see this folder yet. Double-check that you shared it with `<service-account-email>` and try again."
  - Service-account credentials misconfigured (operator-side error) → "Something is wrong on our end. The developer has been notified." (Sentry alert + admin-visible banner; not Doug's problem to fix.)

The wizard never says "files.list returned 403." It says one of the three things above.

**Step 3 — "First sheets review."**

After verification, the wizard calls `runOnboardingScan(folderId, wizardSessionId)` (§5.2) which performs a folder-wide scan against the supplied folder ID **without** writing to `app_settings.watched_folder_id` yet. **Round-48 amendment: the scan populates the `onboarding_scan_manifest` table (§4.5)** — one row per Drive item the scan saw, keyed by `(wizard_session_id, drive_file_id)`, with a terminal-lifecycle `status` enum. Step 3 reads from the manifest as the authoritative per-session state source. Per-sheet status:

- **Parsed and ready** (`status='staged'`) — green check; click to review and approve. Post-amendment-9: only **wizard-discovered** first-seen sheets stage here (`ONBOARDING_SCAN_REVIEW` sentinel) plus first-seen sheets that tripped MI-6..MI-14 (relevant MI sentinel). Live-folder first-seen sheets that pass all MI checks auto-apply via Phase 2 and surface as `SHOW_FIRST_PUBLISHED` admin alerts (with 24h unpublish-undo) instead of staged rows.
- **Couldn't parse** (`status='hard_failed'`) — yellow warning with the plain-English MI failure; click to see details.
- **Skipped (not a Google Sheet)** (`status='skipped_non_sheet'`) — gray badge; informational only, auto-resolved.
- **Already in live sync** (`status='live_row_conflict'`) — red warning surfacing the §12.4 `LIVE_ROW_CONFLICT` doug-facing copy; informational badge with no in-wizard action (the operator resolves the live row from the dashboard and re-runs the wizard). Finalize is blocked until the manifest row leaves this state.

Doug walks each sheet through review. Action endpoints transition the manifest row to a terminal state: Apply → `applied`; Discard `try again next sync` → `discard_retryable` (NOT resolved per §6.8.1); Discard `defer_until_modified` → `defer_until_modified`; Discard `permanent_ignore` → `permanent_ignore`; pending_ingestions Retry → resets to `staged` or stays `hard_failed`; pending_ingestions Defer/Ignore → corresponding terminal status. **`live_row_conflict` rows have no in-wizard transition** — they are resolved only by the operator clearing the underlying live row from the dashboard and re-running the wizard (a fresh scan re-evaluates the per-file UPSERT and either succeeds or re-raises the conflict).

**Wizard finalize (§4.5 atomic promotion)** reads the manifest's unresolved set:

```sql
-- M6 batch-10 amendment: 'live_row_conflict' joins the unresolved set so a schema-rollback
-- collision blocks finalize. Without this, the per-file warn-and-continue path silently
-- bypasses the gate (manifest is empty for the file → finalize counts zero unresolved → folder
-- promotes while a real live-row conflict is unresolved).
SELECT drive_file_id, status FROM onboarding_scan_manifest
 WHERE wizard_session_id = $sessionId
   AND status IN ('staged', 'hard_failed', 'discard_retryable', 'live_row_conflict');
```

If the unresolved set is non-empty → `ONBOARDING_NOT_RESOLVED` 409. If empty → run the **DEFERRED-UNTIL-FINALIZE promotion sequence**. **Phase A — pre-commit work (no DB transaction, no per-show locks):** (A.1) `SELECT id, drive_file_id, parse_result, triggered_review_items, staged_modified_time, wizard_approved_by_email, wizard_approved_at, wizard_reviewer_choices, wizard_reviewer_choices_version, (SELECT head_revision_id FROM pending_syncs_drive_pins WHERE drive_file_id = ps.drive_file_id) AS phase_a_head_revision_id FROM pending_syncs ps WHERE wizard_session_id = $sessionId AND wizard_approved = TRUE ORDER BY drive_file_id` — deterministic alphabetical order for deadlock prevention in Phase B; every row carries the durable approval payload per §4.5 symmetry CHECK. **Any row whose `wizard_reviewer_choices_version` is NOT in the current code's supported set MUST abort Phase A immediately with `WIZARD_REVIEWER_CHOICES_VERSION_UNSUPPORTED` 409, demote that row's manifest back to `'staged'` in a separate follow-up transaction, and surface the offending `drive_file_id` to the wizard UI so the operator can re-Apply.** **Capture the per-row `binding.headRevisionId` observed during the §6.8.1 step-3 re-verify (Phase A.2) into `phaseAResults[id].binding.headRevisionId` — this is the immutable token Phase B will re-fetch and CAS-check immediately before each row's commit, closing the Phase-A→Phase-B TOCTOU window.** **Multi-batch protocol.** Client-supplied `?after=<lastDriveFileId>` cursors and `ONBOARDING_BATCH_TOO_LARGE` 409 / `WIZARD_FINALIZE_CURSOR_INVALID` 400 / `next_batch_token` response fields are rejected; the canonical multi-batch contract is server-owned via the `wizard_finalize_checkpoints` registry and a separate Phase D `/finalize-cas` endpoint. The 100-row LIMIT per call is a per-call ceiling (Phase B advisory-lock loops longer than this risk hot-locking the live folder's cron pass), interim-batch `published = false` semantics, and the wizard UI's auto-fire-next-batch behavior all hold — and the cursor is server-derived (Phase A's SELECT against `pending_syncs WHERE wizard_approved = TRUE ORDER BY drive_file_id LIMIT 100` is authoritative because §6.8.1 step-list 6L DELETEs promoted rows, so a re-Approved row whose `drive_file_id` sorts earlier than the prior batch's last row naturally re-enters the next batch's SELECT regardless of where it sorts). The §4.5 atomic-promotion CAS + `published = TRUE` flip + clean-slate DELETE live in Phase D `/finalize-cas`, NOT in any batch's Phase B. (A.2) For each selected row in order: run the §6.8.1 step-3 mandatory Drive re-verify (parents check pinned to `pending_folder_id`); on any `STAGED_PARSE_SOURCE_GONE` / `_OUT_OF_SCOPE` / `STAGED_PARSE_SUPERSEDED`, capture the per-row failure code in memory and skip to A.3 (do NOT abort yet — Phase B does the abort under transaction). (A.3) Snapshot every approved row's diagrams + linked-folder assets to **Storage at the per-(session, drive_file_id) temporary prefix** `diagram-snapshots/_finalize-pending/<wizard_session_id>/<drive_file_id>/<asset_key>` (the temporary prefix is OUTSIDE the canonical `<show_id>/<snapshot_revision_id>/` keyspace so a finalize that aborts cannot leave half-uploaded blobs at a real revision prefix). Capture the resulting paths in memory keyed by `(drive_file_id, asset_key)`. **Phase B — sequence of N per-row commit transactions (manifest lifecycle):** the outer finalize handler iterates `phaseAResults` in deterministic alphabetical order and for each row opens an independent `withShowSyncTransaction`. (B.1) If Phase A.2 captured a per-row failure code for THIS row, abort THIS row's transaction (ROLLBACK), then in a separate follow-up transaction UPDATE its manifest row back to `'staged'` per the manifest-lifecycle rule above, record the per-row failure code in the response body's `per_row` array, and continue to the next row (sibling rows are NOT aborted — best-effort policy). (B.2) Inside the per-row transaction, acquire `pg_advisory_xact_lock(hashtext('show:' || $row.drive_file_id))` (blocking; deterministic alphabetical order prevents deadlocks across concurrent finalize clicks against the same session). **(B.2.pre) MANDATORY pre-commit Drive head re-verify.** IMMEDIATELY after acquiring the per-row advisory lock and BEFORE running any §6.8.1 Phase-2 SQL, re-fetch `files.get(row.drive_file_id, fields='headRevisionId,modifiedTime,trashed,parents', supportsAllDrives: true)` from inside the lock. CAS-check the re-fetched `headRevisionId` against `phaseAResults[row.drive_file_id].binding.headRevisionId` (captured during Phase A.2). On mismatch → abort THIS row's transaction with `STAGED_PARSE_REVISION_RACE_DURING_FINALIZE` (§12.4); the per-row abort follow-up transaction reverts `wizard_approved` to FALSE and clears the four payload columns per the race-row re-Apply contract; the raced row's manifest STAYS `'staged'` (the wizard manifest UPDATE for THIS row is skipped — the manifest demotion happens inline because we abort the row before its `'applied'` write fires); sibling rows continue to process per the per-row abort semantics above. The operator must re-Apply the raced row before the next finalize click; the per-row failure list is returned in the response body so the wizard UI can surface which file(s) need re-Apply. **CAS check is REQUIRED — without it, mid-flight Drive edits between Phase A.2 (re-verify) and the per-row commit silently promote stale data.** ALSO re-check `trashed === false` AND `parents` still contains `pending_folder_id`; failure on either → emit the existing `STAGED_PARSE_SOURCE_GONE` / `STAGED_PARSE_SOURCE_OUT_OF_SCOPE` per §6.8.1 step 3 semantics with the same per-row abort behavior. Run the §6.8.1 step-list 4L → 5L → 6L Phase-2 + sync*audit + DELETE flow against `parse_result`, **passing `wizard_reviewer_choices` as the choices payload** AND **passing `wizard_approved_by_email` + `wizard_approved_at` as the sync_audit attribution fields**. The Phase 2 UPDATE on `shows.diagrams` references the snapshot paths from Phase A.3 — for each diagram entry, set `snapshotPath` to the canonical `<show_id>/<snapshot_revision_id>/<asset_key>` location. **(B.2.a) Storage move from temporary to canonical prefix:** within the per-row sub-statement, after Phase 2 has determined the freshly-minted `snapshot_revision_id`, issue Storage move/copy operations from `_finalize-pending/<wizard_session_id>/<drive_file_id>/<asset_key>` to `shows/<show_id>/<snapshot_revision_id>/<asset_key>` for every captured asset; if any move fails, the per-row sub-statement raises a Storage error and THIS row's transaction rolls back (sibling rows continue to process per the per-row abort semantics above). The same per-row sub-statement also UPDATEs `onboarding_scan_manifest SET status = 'applied' WHERE wizard_session_id = $sessionId AND drive_file_id = $row.drive_file_id` (manifest-lifecycle invariant — this UPDATE commits with the `shows` write, never before).
