(B.3) UPDATE the `wizard_finalize_checkpoints` row's `last_processed_drive_file_id`, increment `batches_completed`, and set `last_processed_at = now()` (observability — the checkpoint is NOT a gating cursor; the next batch's SELECT against `pending_syncs WHERE wizard_approved = TRUE` is authoritative). (B.4) Commit and release the per-row advisory lock. **The §4.5 atomic-promotion CAS, the `published = TRUE` flip, the wizard `deferred_ingestions` clean-slate DELETE, and the `subscribeToWatchedFolder` call ALL move into Phase D — Phase B per-row commits NEVER run them, regardless of whether the row is the last in the session.** After all per-row transactions in the batch complete (each independently committed or aborted), the handler re-SELECTs `count(*) FROM pending*syncs WHERE wizard_session_id = $sessionId AND wizard_approved = TRUE`. If 0 → UPDATE `wizard_finalize_checkpoints SET status = 'all_batches_complete'`and respond`{ status: 'all_batches_complete', per_row: [...] }`. If > 0 → respond `{ status: 'batch_complete', per_row: [...] }`(the wizard UI auto-fires the next`/finalize`call). **If a per-row Phase 2 sub-statement raises an unexpected error inside its own per-row transaction, abort THAT row only (ROLLBACK), then in a separate follow-up transaction UPDATE its manifest back to`'staged'`per the manifest-lifecycle rule, then run a per-row temp-prefix cleanup: DELETE Storage objects under`\_finalize-pending/<wizard_session_id>/<drive_file_id>/`. Sibling rows continue. The per-row failure code is recorded in the response body's `per_row`array.** **Phase C — post-batch best-effort cleanup of superseded temp prefixes:** after the entire batch's per-row transactions have all completed, issue a best-effort Storage DELETE under the`\_finalize-pending/<wizard_session_id>/`prefix to remove any temp blobs left behind for sheets that were superseded during Phase A.2 re-verify. The cleanup is best-effort: a Storage DELETE failure here logs a`sync_log`entry coded`finalize_temp_prefix_cleanup_failed`(with`payload = { wizard_session_id, error }`) but does NOT affect the success of any per-row commit; a Task 7.8 GC sweeper consumes any leftover `\_finalize-pending/*` prefixes older than 24 hours as a backstop. **Phase D — final-CAS endpoint (`POST /api/admin/onboarding/finalize-cas`):** see the cursor section below for the full canonical contract — Phase D reads the checkpoint, verifies `status = 'all*batches_complete'`AND`pending_syncs WHERE wizard_approved = TRUE`count is 0, then runs §4.5 atomic-promotion CAS +`UPDATE shows SET published = TRUE WHERE drive_file_id IN (SELECT drive_file_id FROM onboarding_scan_manifest WHERE wizard_session_id = $sessionId AND status = 'applied')`+`DELETE FROM deferred_ingestions WHERE wizard_session_id = $sessionId`in ONE short transaction (no Drive/Storage I/O), then sets`status = 'final_cas_done'`. Phase D's `subscribeToWatchedFolder(folderId)`runs OUTSIDE the transaction, after commit, preserving the prior Phase C non-transactional semantics for the watch-channel registration (the folder ID is now durable in`watched_folder_id`so a webhook race can do no harm). The manifest is the SOLE finalize gate — row absence in`pending*\*`tables is NOT a substitute (the`discard_retryable`Discard variant deletes pending_syncs with no deferral row, which row-absence inference would silently treat as resolved). **Resolving a`'live_row_conflict'`row requires the operator to (a) resolve the underlying live`pending_syncs`/`pending_ingestions`row from the dashboard, then (b) re-run the wizard so a fresh`runOnboardingScan`re-attempts the per-file UPSERT and either succeeds (manifest transitions to`'staged'`/`'hard_failed'`/ etc.) or re-raises the conflict (manifest stays at`'live_row_conflict'`).\*\*

**Server-owned multi-batch finalize cursor.** A client-driven `?after=<lastDriveFileId>` query parameter is rejected: a strict `>` cursor would diverge from the `STAGED_PARSE_REVISION_RACE_DURING_FINALIZE` per-row semantic (which leaves a row's manifest at `'staged'` so the operator can re-Apply). A row whose `drive_file_id` sorted alphabetically BEFORE the previous client cursor and was re-Approved between batches would be silently invisible to every subsequent batch (the strict `>` cursor would skip it), leaving the row stranded with `wizard_approved = TRUE` AND no path to promotion. The corrected contract is server-driven via the new admin-only `wizard_finalize_checkpoints` table (§4.1 / §4.3 — admin-only list grows from 18 → 19 tables): (i) **DDL** — `wizard_finalize_checkpoints (id uuid pk default gen_random_uuid(), wizard_session_id uuid not null unique, last_processed_drive_file_id text, last_processed_at timestamptz, batches_completed int not null default 0, status text not null default 'in_progress' check (status in ('in_progress', 'all_batches_complete', 'final_cas_done')))`. RLS denies non-admin SELECT/INSERT/UPDATE/DELETE per §4.3. (ii) **Endpoint signature** — `POST /api/admin/onboarding/finalize` (NO query param). (iii) **Per-batch row selection** — `SELECT id, drive_file_id, ... FROM pending_syncs WHERE wizard_session_id = $sessionId AND wizard_approved = TRUE ORDER BY drive_file_id LIMIT 100` (the SELECT is authoritative; previously-promoted rows have already been DELETEd from `pending_syncs` by §6.8.1 step-list 6L; re-Approved rows naturally re-enter regardless of `drive_file_id` ordering). (iv) **First call** — INSERT a checkpoint row with `wizard_session_id = $sessionId` and `status = 'in_progress'`. If a checkpoint row already exists with `status = 'final_cas_done'`, return `{ status: 'finalize_complete' }` (idempotency). If `status = 'all_batches_complete'`, return that status without selecting any rows (the wizard UI should fire the final-CAS endpoint next). (v) **Per-batch UPDATE** — at the end of each Phase B per-row commit loop, UPDATE the checkpoint row: set `last_processed_drive_file_id` to the alphabetically-largest `drive_file_id` of the batch (observability ONLY — NOT a gating cursor), increment `batches_completed`, set `last_processed_at = now()`. After the UPDATE, re-SELECT remaining count: `SELECT count(*) FROM pending_syncs WHERE wizard_session_id = $sessionId AND wizard_approved = TRUE`. If 0 → UPDATE checkpoint `status = 'all_batches_complete'`. (vi) **Final-CAS endpoint** — `POST /api/admin/onboarding/finalize-cas` (Phase D). Reads the checkpoint, verifies `status = 'all_batches_complete'` AND the `pending_syncs` count is 0, then runs §4.5 atomic-promotion CAS + `UPDATE shows SET published = TRUE WHERE drive_file_id IN (SELECT drive_file_id FROM onboarding_scan_manifest WHERE wizard_session_id = $sessionId AND status = 'applied')` + `DELETE FROM deferred_ingestions WHERE wizard_session_id = $sessionId` in ONE short transaction with NO Drive / Storage I/O, then sets `status = 'final_cas_done'`. Phase D's transaction takes <100ms typically. Phase D's `subscribeToWatchedFolder(folderId)` runs OUTSIDE the transaction, after commit. (vii) **Concurrent finalize calls** — TWO parallel POSTs against the same session race on `pg_try_advisory_xact_lock(hashtext('finalize:' || $sessionId))` at Phase B start; loser returns 409 `CONCURRENT_FINALIZE_IN_FLIGHT`. (viii) **Crash mid-batch** — the next call resumes by SELECTing `pending_syncs WHERE wizard_approved = TRUE` (rows the partial commit DELETEd are gone; the rest re-select in deterministic order; the checkpoint is observability only, not a gate). (ix) **Wizard UI** — auto-fires the next `/finalize` call while the response carries `{ status: 'batch_complete' }`; the moment the response carries `{ status: 'all_batches_complete' }`, fires `/finalize-cas` exactly once. The prior `next_batch_token` field is removed from response shapes. (x) **Race-row re-Apply contract** — when a per-row `STAGED_PARSE_REVISION_RACE_DURING_FINALIZE` fires inside Phase B, the per-row abort follow-up transaction additionally runs `UPDATE pending_syncs SET wizard_approved = FALSE, wizard_approved_at = NULL, wizard_approved_by_email = NULL, wizard_reviewer_choices = NULL, wizard_reviewer_choices_version = NULL WHERE wizard_session_id = $sessionId AND drive_file_id = $racedDriveFileId` so the row is excluded from subsequent batches' SELECTs until the operator re-Applies (the §4.5 symmetry CHECK accepts this all-NULLs-with-FALSE state). On re-Apply the row re-acquires the full payload AND `wizard_approved = TRUE`, re-entering the next batch's SELECT regardless of where its `drive_file_id` sorts.

**Admin write-action guard for `published=false` interim-finalize rows.** Pre-Phase-D `shows` rows (`published = false`) are admin-visible (Task 10.6 dashboard's yellow "Publishing…" badge per §9.1) but MUST NOT be mutated by ad-hoc admin write actions while finalize owns them. The earlier draft did not gate the admin Re-sync (`runManualSyncForShow` per §5.4) / Archive / Apply/Discard write routes against `published = false`; a stale dashboard tab clicking "Re-sync" on a Publishing row would race `runManualSyncForShow(driveFileId)` against finalize's per-row Phase B commit and could either (a) break the §4.5 partition guarantee (manual writes target the live partition while wizard finalize still owns the row) or (b) drift the show into a state finalize cannot resolve (e.g., manual sync mints a fresh `pending_syncs` row whose `wizard_session_id = NULL` while the wizard partition's row still exists with `wizard_approved = TRUE`). The corrected contract: every admin write route that mutates a `shows` row OR mints/mutates a `pending_syncs` / `pending_ingestions` row keyed by `drive_file_id` checks the show's `published` column AND `wizard_finalize_checkpoints.status` for the owning wizard session BEFORE doing any work; if `shows.published = FALSE` AND there exists a `wizard_finalize_checkpoints` row joining the show through `onboarding_scan_manifest` whose `status` is `'in_progress'` or `'all_batches_complete'` (i.e., Phase D has not committed yet), the route returns 409 `FINALIZE_OWNED_SHOW` (new §12.4 code; Doug-facing: "This show is currently being published as part of a setup wizard. Wait for the wizard to finish, then try again."). The guard applies to: `runManualSyncForShow(driveFileId, mode = "manual" | "recovery")` (the §5.4 admin "Re-sync" path), `/api/admin/show/[slug]/archive`, `/admin/show/[slug]/preview-as`, `/admin/show/staged/<stagedId>` Apply/Discard for the wizard partition, and the per-show staged-review Apply/Discard at `/admin/show/<slug>?review=staged_id`. Read-only admin routes (`/admin/show/<slug>` GET) are NOT gated — admins need to see in-flight rows. The admin dashboard UI ALSO hides write-action buttons (Re-sync / Archive / Preview-as) on rows whose `published = false` AND replaces them with the static "Publishing…" badge so the operator cannot click them in the first place; the server-side guard is defense-in-depth for stale tabs / scripted access. After Phase D commits and `published = true` is durably written to all session-promoted rows, the guard naturally relaxes (the predicate `shows.published = FALSE` no longer matches) and admin writes resume. **Test (Task 6.7 / Task 10.6 / new propagation regression):** stage 2 sheets in W1, Apply both, run finalize batch 1 (which inserts both with `published = false`), but DO NOT run finalize-cas yet. From a separate admin session, POST to `runManualSyncForShow` for one of the freshly-minted shows. Assert HTTP 409 `FINALIZE_OWNED_SHOW`; assert no rows in `pending_syncs` with `wizard_session_id IS NULL` for that drive_file_id (the manual route bailed before any DB write); assert finalize-cas still completes successfully against the unchanged interim state.

**Per-row Phase B transactions.** Wrapping the entire 100-row Phase B loop in one `withShowSyncTransaction`, holding `pg_advisory_xact_lock(hashtext('show:' || $row.drive_file_id))` per row inside that transaction along with sequential Drive `files.get` + Storage move/copy I/O for every row, would mean: with 100 rows × ~200ms per row of Drive + Storage I/O, the transaction holds the wizard's per-show advisory locks for ~20 seconds AND the connection's transaction snapshot for the same window — long enough to seriously contend with concurrent live cron passes whose per-show writes acquire the SAME `show:<drive_file_id>` advisory lock. The design: Phase B runs as a SEQUENCE of N **per-row** transactions, NOT one batch-wide transaction. The outer finalize handler iterates `phaseAResults` in deterministic alphabetical order and for each row opens an independent `withShowSyncTransaction` that (a) acquires the per-row advisory lock, (b) re-fetches the per-row Drive head and CAS-checks against `phaseAResults[row].binding.headRevisionId`, (c) runs the §6.8.1 step-list 4L → 5L → 6L Phase 2 + sync_audit + DELETE flow + Storage move from `_finalize-pending/` to canonical prefix + manifest UPDATE to `'applied'`, (d) UPDATEs the `wizard_finalize_checkpoints` row's `last_processed_drive_file_id` and increments `batches_completed`, and (e) commits and releases the lock. A per-row abort affects ONLY that row (manifest demoted to `'staged'`, `wizard_approved` reverted to FALSE per the race-row re-Apply contract); subsequent rows in the batch continue to process (best-effort policy; the response body lists per-row outcomes). After all per-row commits succeed, the handler re-SELECTs the remaining count and conditionally flips checkpoint `status = 'all_batches_complete'` if the count is 0. The §4.5 atomic-promotion CAS + `published = TRUE` flip + clean-slate DELETE all move into the **Phase D final-CAS endpoint** (a separate request, separate short transaction, no Drive/Storage I/O). **Concurrency win:** cron's live per-show advisory lock acquisition against any of the 100 wizard rows now waits at most for one per-row Phase B sub-transaction (~200ms) instead of the full batch-wide transaction (~20s); cron does NOT block on Phase A (which never acquires per-show locks); cron passes against unrelated live shows are completely unaffected. **Phase B abort semantics:** "per-row rollback unwinds only that row; sibling rows already committed remain committed." This is consistent with the multi-batch published-flag protocol — interim-batch rows are NEVER publicly visible until Phase D, so a partial batch is identical (from the crew's perspective) to a partial multi-batch finalize where Phase D simply runs against fewer rows. **Test (new regression — Task 9.x):** stage 50 rows in W1, Apply all, kick off finalize. From a separate connection, run `runScheduledCronSync` against the existing live folder during finalize's Phase B. Assert (a) Phase B's per-row advisory locks are released between rows (instrument `pg_advisory_unlock` at row N's commit; cron's lock-acquire timestamp on an UNRELATED live show is < 200ms after Phase B starts, NOT 20+s); (b) cron's per-show advisory lock acquire on a DIFFERENT drive_file_id never blocks; (c) total finalize batch wall-clock time is comparable to the batch-wide single-tx version. **Failure-mode regression:** make the 25th row's Phase 2 throw. Assert (a) rows 1–24 commit with `published = false` and manifest `'applied'`; (b) row 25's manifest demotes to `'staged'` and `wizard_approved` reverts to FALSE in a separate follow-up transaction; (c) rows 26–50 STILL process to commit; (d) the response body lists row 25 in the `failed` array; (e) the wizard UI re-fires the next batch which SELECTs only row 25 (after operator re-Applies it); (f) Phase D fires once after the final batch, atomically flipping all 50 rows to `published = true`.

**Wizard-session CAS on every scan write.** Every UPSERT into `pending_syncs`, `pending_ingestions`, AND `onboarding_scan_manifest` is gated by `WHERE EXISTS (SELECT 1 FROM app_settings WHERE pending_wizard_session_id = $myWizardSessionId)` so a slow W1 scan whose start preceded W2's takeover cannot clobber W2's freshly-staged rows. On supersession, W1 logs `WIZARD_SESSION_SUPERSEDED_DURING_SCAN` and exits cleanly.

**Shadow surface (`shows_pending_changes`) for already-live `shows` updates during multi-batch finalize.** A naive design — Phase B's per-row sub-transaction running the §6.8.1 step-list 4L → 5L → 6L Phase-2 UPDATE on `shows` directly for every approved row, INCLUDING rows whose lock-time `SELECT id, published FROM shows WHERE drive_file_id = $1 FOR UPDATE` returns an EXISTING live row (`existing_show_id IS NOT NULL`, typically `published = TRUE`) — would let `publishVisibility = lockedShow[0].published` keep the rows crew-visible during finalize, but the rest of the Phase-2 payload — title, client_label, template_version, financials snapshot, diagrams, transportation, hotel_reservations, rooms, contacts, last_seen_modified_time, parse_warnings, raw_unrecognized — would land on the live row immediately. If the operator then abandoned the multi-batch finalize and clicked "Cleanup abandoned finalize," `cleanupAbandonedFinalize`'s `DELETE FROM shows WHERE published = FALSE AND drive_file_id IN (manifest-applied)` would remove only the FIRST-SEEN rows; the already-live rows would keep the wizard's mid-applied content with no path to revert. Crew would see the wizard's half-applied changes on a live show indefinitely. The contract: Phase B's per-row sub-transaction branches on the lock-time `SELECT`. (a) **First-seen branch (lock-time SELECT returns 0 rows):** unchanged from the prior contract — `INSERT INTO shows (...) VALUES (..., published = false, ...)`, write `sync_audit`, DELETE `pending_syncs`, Storage move, manifest UPDATE to `'applied'`, checkpoint UPDATE. Phase D's `UPDATE shows SET published = TRUE WHERE drive_file_id IN (manifest-applied)` flips this row to TRUE. `cleanupAbandonedFinalize`'s `DELETE FROM shows WHERE published = FALSE AND drive_file_id IN (manifest-applied)` removes this row on abandonment. (b) **Existing-show branch (lock-time SELECT returns 1 row, regardless of its `published` value):** Phase B's per-row sub-transaction does NOT mutate the live `shows` row. Instead, it `INSERT INTO shows_pending_changes (wizard_session_id, drive_file_id, show_id, payload, applied_by_email, applied_at_intent) VALUES (...) ON CONFLICT (wizard_session_id, drive_file_id) DO UPDATE SET payload = EXCLUDED.payload, applied_by_email = EXCLUDED.applied_by_email, applied_at_intent = EXCLUDED.applied_at_intent, staged_at = now()`. The `payload` is the full Phase-2 column set the prior contract would have written: every sheet-derived column, the freshly-minted `snapshot_revision_id`, and the diagram entries pointing at the canonical Storage paths from the per-row Storage move (the move STILL runs in Phase B per the existing temp-prefix → canonical-prefix invariant; the canonical paths under `shows/<show_id>/<new_revision_id>/<asset_key>` are derived from the existing live show's `id`). The same per-row sub-transaction STILL runs the `pending_syncs` DELETE, the `onboarding_scan_manifest` UPDATE to `'applied'`, the checkpoint UPDATE, and the temp→canonical Storage move; only the `UPDATE shows SET ...` is replaced by the `INSERT INTO shows_pending_changes ...`. Crew continue to see the live show's pre-finalize content during the entire multi-batch window because no `shows` UPDATE ever fires. (c) **Phase D apply step:** Phase D's transaction adds, after the existing `published = TRUE` flip and BEFORE the §4.5 atomic-promotion CAS, a per-row apply loop that reads every `shows_pending_changes` row for `$sessionId` and runs `UPDATE shows SET <payload-columns> WHERE id = $show_id` under a per-show advisory lock for each (the per-row apply CAS-gates `last_seen_modified_time IS NULL OR last_seen_modified_time <= $payload.last_seen_modified_time` per the §6.8.1 manual-mode semantics — a strictly-newer live row blocks the apply with `STAGED_PARSE_OUTDATED_AT_PHASE_D`, ROLLBACKs only that show, leaves the staged row in `shows_pending_changes` for the operator to clear via "Cleanup abandoned finalize" or for the next finalize click to re-apply against the new live state, and records the failure in the response body's `per_row` array). After every staged row applies (or the row's CAS fails), Phase D writes the `sync_audit` row using `applied_by_email` + `applied_at_intent` from `shows_pending_changes` (Doug's Apply-time attribution, NOT Eric's Phase-D-time clock — preserving the operator-attribution contract), DELETEs the `shows_pending_changes` rows for `$sessionId`, then runs the existing §4.5 atomic-promotion CAS + clean-slate DELETE. (d) **Cleanup path:** `cleanupAbandonedFinalize` adds a single statement at the start of its destructive-work block: `DELETE FROM shows_pending_changes WHERE wizard_session_id = $sessionId`. No `shows` data is touched for already-live rows; the live show is exactly as it was before finalize started. The first-seen DELETE (`DELETE FROM shows WHERE published = FALSE AND drive_file_id IN (manifest-applied)`) continues to remove first-seen interim rows. (e) **`FINALIZE_OWNED_SHOW` guard expansion:** the admin-write guard (which fires when `shows.published = FALSE`) ALSO fires when a `shows_pending_changes` row exists for the show's `drive_file_id` AND its joined `wizard_finalize_checkpoints.status` is `'in_progress'` or `'all_batches_complete'`. After Phase D commits (`status = 'final_cas_done'`) and DELETEs the `shows_pending_changes` rows, the guard naturally relaxes. (f) **Symmetry / abort semantics:** if a per-row Phase B sub-transaction aborts (e.g., Storage move failure, Drive head re-verify race, unexpected error), the per-row rollback unwinds the `INSERT INTO shows_pending_changes` along with the manifest UPDATE / checkpoint UPDATE / pending_syncs DELETE / Storage move (consistent with the per-row-tx invariant). The post-rollback follow-up demotes manifest to `'staged'` and reverts `wizard_approved`. No partial shadow row remains.

**Live-row isolation (read-side propagation + LIVE_ROW_CONFLICT manifest write).** Wizard UPSERTs target ONLY the wizard's own session partition (`ON CONFLICT (drive_file_id, wizard_session_id) WHERE wizard_session_id IS NOT NULL`); they NEVER overwrite a NULL-session row. A NULL-session `pending_syncs` / `pending_ingestions` row IS the shape of a live cron/push/manual-owned row, and overwriting it would clobber the live show's authoritative state. The §4.5 schema accordingly declares two partial unique indexes per table (live partition `WHERE wizard_session_id IS NULL`; wizard partition `WHERE wizard_session_id IS NOT NULL`), enabling coexistence of one live row and one wizard row per drive_file_id. Wizard reads (`/admin` step-3 manifest renderer, finalize gate, action endpoints) scope to `wizard_session_id = $myWizardSessionId`; dashboard reads ("Sheets we couldn't auto-apply" panel, Active Shows panel) scope to `wizard_session_id IS NULL`. Apply / Discard routes scope by source kind — onboarding rows route to wizard step 3, live rows route to dashboard. **All read sites MUST add the source-scope predicate:** the cron/push watermark calc (`pending_syncs.staged_modified_time` lookup), the existing-show stage-wins guard, the first-seen race-detection in `handleDriveFetchFailure`, every Apply/Discard/retry/defer/ignore selector, every fixture verification query — every read on `pending_syncs` / `pending_ingestions` keyed by `drive_file_id` carries either `AND wizard_session_id IS NULL` (live/automatic paths) or `AND wizard_session_id = $myWizardSessionId` (wizard paths). An unscoped read against a coexisting live + wizard pair returns ambiguous data and can target the wrong partition.

**LIVE_ROW_CONFLICT detection contract.** Detection has TWO parts. **(A) `pg_indexes` schema-state probe at scan start.** Before issuing any session-partitioned UPSERT, `runOnboardingScan` queries `pg_indexes` for the four expected partial unique indexes (`pending_syncs_live_drive_file_idx`, `pending_syncs_session_drive_file_idx`, `pending_ingestions_live_drive_file_idx`, `pending_ingestions_session_drive_file_idx`). If any are missing, the scan ABORTS with `WIZARD_ISOLATION_INDEXES_MISSING` (operator-facing migration-state error) BEFORE writing anything. **(B) per-row SQLSTATE catch on each wizard UPSERT.** A missing partial-index arbiter raises `42P10` _invalid_column_reference_; a fallback to the original `drive_file_id PRIMARY KEY` raises `23505` _unique_violation_ against the live row. Either SQLSTATE is the `LIVE_ROW_CONFLICT` signal. **Zero RETURNING rows is NEVER a `LIVE_ROW_CONFLICT` signal under the corrected design** — it is the GOOD path (CAS-gate fired; no real collision; W2 took over mid-scan if `app_settings.pending_wizard_session_id` no longer matches). The earlier draft's "zero RETURNING rows = LIVE_ROW_CONFLICT" heuristic was incorrect: a missing arbiter raises a hard SQL error, not a successful zero-row return. The catch-and-translate happens inside the per-file try/catch; any SQLSTATE other than `42P10` / `23505` re-throws.

**LIVE_ROW_CONFLICT manifest write contract.** When the wizard's per-file UPSERT into `pending_syncs` or `pending_ingestions` raises `LIVE_ROW_CONFLICT` (the schema-rollback failure mode caught via the SQLSTATE detection in part B above, where the partial-index arbiter is missing OR the table fell back to its original `drive_file_id` PK), the per-file warn-and-continue path MUST also UPSERT a row into `onboarding_scan_manifest` with `status = 'live_row_conflict'`. Without this manifest write, the finalize gate (which reads the manifest as its sole resolution-state source) sees nothing for the conflicted file and counts zero unresolved rows — promoting the folder while a real live-row collision is unresolved. The manifest UPSERT carries the same wizard-session CAS gate as every other onboarding scan write (`WHERE EXISTS (SELECT 1 FROM app_settings WHERE pending_wizard_session_id = $myWizardSessionId)`); a superseded scan's conflict-manifest write is correctly no-op'd. The manifest row stays at `'live_row_conflict'` until the next wizard run's `runOnboardingScan` re-attempts the per-file UPSERT after the operator resolves the live row from the dashboard; on success the row transitions to `'staged'` / `'hard_failed'` / `'skipped_non_sheet'`, on re-collision it stays at `'live_row_conflict'`.

**After onboarding.** "Re-run Setup" from `/admin/settings` writes a fresh `pending_wizard_session_id` (without touching `watched_folder_id`); cron continues using the live folder while the new wizard runs. Wizard supersession purges prior-session rows across all three onboarding surfaces (`pending_syncs`, `pending_ingestions`, `onboarding_scan_manifest`).

**Re-run Setup checkpoint-aware suppression.** The `/admin/settings` "Re-run Setup" server action MUST run the SAME `wizard_finalize_checkpoints` suppression gate the auto-rotate path runs (§4.5 prong 3). Inside the same transaction as the rotate-and-purge DML, the action probes `SELECT EXISTS (SELECT 1 FROM wizard_finalize_checkpoints c JOIN app_settings a ON c.wizard_session_id = a.pending_wizard_session_id WHERE a.id = 'default' AND c.batches_completed > 0)`. If the EXISTS yields TRUE — i.e., the CURRENT `pending_wizard_session_id` owns a checkpoint with at least one committed batch — the action MUST refuse to rotate or purge: it INSERTs a `sync_log` entry coded `WIZARD_FINALIZE_BATCHES_PENDING` AND `redirect('/admin?show_finalize=true')` so the operator lands on the FinalizeInProgress / ReadyToPublish surface (per the dispatch logic the `/admin` route already runs based on checkpoint status). Without this gate, an operator who clicks Re-run Setup from a stale tab between finalize batches OR while Phase D is racing strands the in-flight session's `published=FALSE` `shows` rows AND the checkpoint with no UI path to recovery — the unconditional purge would delete `onboarding_scan_manifest` (the durable join that identifies which `shows` rows belong to the in-flight set) and the rotate would clear `pending_wizard_session_id` (the lookup key the FinalizeInProgress surface uses). The gate is symmetric to the §4.5 auto-rotate suppression: both refuse to mutate state while a multi-batch finalize from the current session has committed at least one batch, and both surface the operator to the same recovery affordances.

**Wizard-scoped per-row re-apply route (per-row finalize failure recovery).** When a multi-batch finalize's per-row Phase B aborts a single row (`STAGED_PARSE_REVISION_RACE_DURING_FINALIZE` from the head re-verify, or `STAGED_PARSE_SOURCE_GONE` / `STAGED_PARSE_SOURCE_OUT_OF_SCOPE` / `STAGED_PARSE_SUPERSEDED` from the §6.8.1 step-3 re-verify, or `WIZARD_REVIEWER_CHOICES_VERSION_UNSUPPORTED` from the version gate, or any unexpected per-row Phase 2 throw), the per-row abort follow-up transaction reverts `wizard_approved` to FALSE, clears the four payload columns, demotes the manifest row back to `'staged'`, AND records the failure code in a new `pending_syncs.last_finalize_failure_code text` column. The failed row lives in `pending_syncs WHERE wizard_session_id = $sessionId AND wizard_approved = FALSE AND last_finalize_failure_code IS NOT NULL` until the operator re-Applies OR Discards. **Re-Apply MUST go through a wizard-scoped route, NOT the live first-seen route at `/admin/show/staged/[stagedId]`.** The new admin-only route at `/admin/onboarding/staged/[wizardSessionId]/[driveFileId]/page.tsx` keys lookups on `(wizard_session_id, drive_file_id)` (not `staged_id`), scopes to `wizard_session_id = $wizardSessionId` (not `IS NULL`), and renders the same `<StagedReviewCard>` shape as wizard step 3 with these specifics: (a) the per-row failure code from `last_finalize_failure_code` is displayed with its §12.4 doug-facing copy; (b) the `triggered_review_items[]` reviewer-choice controls are re-rendered (the operator may need to re-make their choices because the source sheet changed between original Apply and failed finalize); (c) Apply submits to `POST /api/admin/onboarding/staged/[wizardSessionId]/[driveFileId]/apply` which acquires `pg_advisory_xact_lock(hashtext('show:' || $driveFileId))`, re-SELECTs with the wizard-partition CAS predicate (`wizard_approved = FALSE` ensures only re-Apply candidates are accepted; idempotent if the operator clicks twice), runs §6.8.2 reviewer-choices validation, re-fetches Drive head + parents + trashed (mandatory re-verify), re-parses, then UPDATEs the row to `wizard_approved = TRUE` with freshly-captured payload + `last_finalize_failure_code = NULL` AND restores the manifest row to `'applied'` in one transaction; (d) Discard submits to `POST /api/admin/onboarding/staged/[wizardSessionId]/[driveFileId]/discard` which deletes the row with the same wizard-scoped semantics as wizard step-3 Discard (`try_again_next_sync` / `defer_until_modified` / `permanent_ignore` — wizard-scoped `deferred_ingestions` writes per §4.5 clean-slate). Routing failed wizard rows to the live first-seen route would either 404 (the live partition has no matching `WHERE wizard_session_id IS NULL` row for that `staged_id`) OR (worse) operate on the wrong partition if the same `drive_file_id` happens to have a coexisting live row from cron during the wizard run, racing the next finalize batch's per-show advisory lock against a freshly-minted live `shows` row. The finalize endpoint's `per_row` response array carries `{ drive_file_id, wizard_session_id, code, re_apply_url }` for every failed row, where `re_apply_url = '/admin/onboarding/staged/<wizard_session_id>/<drive_file_id>'` — the wizard UI renders the link verbatim, never composing the URL itself. **Symmetric §4.5 schema amendment**: `pending_syncs.last_finalize_failure_code text` is added to the schema; the §4.5 symmetry CHECK is updated to allow it to be NON-NULL whenever `wizard_approved = FALSE` AND the four payload columns are NULL.

**Stale `all_batches_complete` dispatch (combined Publish + Cleanup affordance).** The `/admin` re-entry dispatch logic distinguishes fresh from stale `all_batches_complete` checkpoints by `last_processed_at`. Fresh (`> now() - 24h`) → render `<ReadyToPublish />` with ONLY a Publish button (cleanup at this stage would discard fully-approved shows seconds from publication). Stale (`<= now() - 24h`, indicating Phase D has been failing OR the operator abandoned the wizard between batch-complete and Publish) → render `<StaleReadyToPublish />` with BOTH a Publish button (to retry Phase D against the unchanged interim state) AND a Cleanup-abandoned-finalize button (for operators who want to discard the entire wizard run). The render-time staleness check is **informational only** — it determines which surface renders but does NOT authorize destructive action; both downstream actions are gated by SQL-clock predicates in their respective endpoints (§4.5 prong 3 cleanup helper guards 3 + 4 evaluated against Postgres `now()` inside the helper's transaction). App-vs-DB clock skew at the 24h boundary can flicker the rendered surface between `<ReadyToPublish />` and `<StaleReadyToPublish />`, but cannot authorize a destructive action against a fresh checkpoint — the cleanup helper's session-staleness CAS refuses with `CLEANUP_REQUIRES_STALE_SESSION` reason `session_too_fresh` if the helper's DB-time check observes the checkpoint as fresh, regardless of what the render-time check thought. Cleanup of a stale `all_batches_complete` session DELETEs the manifest-applied `published=FALSE` `shows` rows (the cleanup helper's existing logic — joining `shows.published = FALSE` against `onboarding_scan_manifest WHERE wizard_session_id = $sessionId AND status = 'applied'` — naturally captures 100% of an `all_batches_complete` session's approved rows; the cleanup correctly discards all of them).

### 9.0.1 In-app help and tour

Once the dashboard is active, contextual help is available everywhere:

- A "?" icon next to every section header that opens a small tooltip with one paragraph of explanation in plain language.
- A "Take the tour" link in the dashboard footer that walks through the dashboard, a per-show parse panel, and the preview-as flow.
- Every error message links to "What does this mean?" with a one-paragraph plain-language explanation.

These are first-class spec requirements, not "nice-to-have polish." The error catalog in §12.4 is the source of truth for every text string a non-technical user sees.

### 9.1 `/admin` dashboard

The dashboard has two panels stacked top-to-bottom:

**Panel 1 — Active shows.** A list of `shows` rows with per-row status:

| Column    | Content                                                                   |
| --------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Title     | `RPAS Central 2026`                                                       |
| Dates     | `3/22 → 3/26/26`                                                          |
| Crew      | `4`                                                                       |
| Last sync | `12 min ago · ✓` (or `2h ago · ⚠ 2 warnings` or `1d ago · ✗ parse error`) |
| Actions   | `Open · Preview as · Re-sync · Archive`                                   |

Empty state if no shows: instructions to share the Drive folder with the service account email, with the email displayed as a copy-button.

**Panel 2 — Sheets we couldn't auto-apply.** Combines two queues, each with distinct row actions:

- **`pending_ingestions` rows** (brand-new sheets that hard-failed during fetch or parse): each row shows `drive_file_name`, first-seen timestamp, attempt count, and `last_error_code` + `last_error_message`. Actions: "Open in Drive", "Retry now". **Retry MUST NEVER auto-apply for first-seen rows.** When no `shows` row exists for the `drive_file_id` (the canonical case for `pending_ingestions`), Retry runs a stage-only Phase-1-only helper (`runManualStageForFirstSeen`) that can produce at most `parsed_pending_review` (a `pending_syncs` row appears for Doug to review) or `still_failed` (the `pending_ingestions` row's `attempt_count` increments). It MUST NOT mint a `shows` row even when every MI invariant passes — first-seen sheets ALWAYS route to STAGE per the §5.2 routing precedence and §9.1.1 first-seen-mandatory-review rule. Doug must explicitly Apply from the resulting first-seen `pending_syncs` row to create the `shows` row. (When a `shows` row already exists for `drive_file_id` — possible after a `sheet_unavailable→DRIVE_FETCH_FAILED→re-share` path leaves a `pending_ingestions` row alongside the existing show — Retry routes through the full manual sync path and may auto-apply because the show is already public.)
- **`pending_syncs` rows for first-seen shows** (the show has no `shows` row yet because the parse passed MI-1..MI-5b but tripped a stage-for-approval invariant): each row shows the candidate `title`/`dates` from `pending_syncs.parse_result.show`, the staged_id, and the triggered invariants. Actions: "Review and Apply" (opens the dedicated first-seen staged-review surface at `/admin/show/staged/<stagedId>` — a slug-less URL because no `shows.slug` exists yet for the candidate; the page loads its data by `pending_syncs.staged_id` and renders the same review-card UI shape as `/admin/show/<slug>?review=staged_id` from §9.2 sub-section 0. On Apply, a `shows` row is INSERTed with the slug derived from `parse_result` per §6.9, the `pending_syncs` row is DELETEd in the same transaction, and the operator is 302-redirected to `/admin/show/<derived-slug>` for any follow-on review), "Discard" (deletes the `pending_syncs` row, no `shows` row created).

Both queues live here so brand-new sheets that need attention are visible alongside successful shows. **No public `/show/<slug>` URL is reserved until first successful Apply** — Discard cannot leak slugs.

### 9.1.1 Existing-show staged-review surface

Any existing show with a matching `pending_syncs` row (i.e., a re-stage of an already-live show; not a first-seen) appears with a **distinct status badge in the dashboard's Active Shows panel** — not in the "Sheets we couldn't auto-apply" panel (which is for first-seen). The active-shows row's status badge becomes "⚠ Review staged changes" (yellow), the "Last sync" cell shows the staged_modified_time + the count of triggered review items, and the row's primary action becomes "Review staged changes" linking directly to `/admin/show/<slug>?review=staged_id` (the review surface inside the per-show parse panel — see §9.2 below).

A show in re-stage state continues to render its prior approved snapshot to crew (per §5.2 Phase 1 outcome 2: re-stage updates `last_sync_status` to `pending_review` but doesn't touch the live data). The dashboard makes this state findable so it cannot sit indefinitely.

**Both first-seen and re-stage queues are durable**: first-seen `pending_syncs` rows live in the dashboard's "Sheets we couldn't auto-apply" panel; re-stage `pending_syncs` rows live in the Active Shows panel as "Review staged changes." A staged row never disappears without an Apply or Discard action.

### 9.2 `/admin/show/<slug>` — per-show parse panel

Four sub-sections (the first appears only when a `pending_syncs` row exists for this show):

0. **Staged review (when `pending_syncs.drive_file_id = shows.drive_file_id` exists)** — appears at the top of the panel as a yellow "Action required" card. Lists every `triggered_review_items[]` entry with its plain-language description (looked up via §12.4 codes), the staged Apply/Discard pair of buttons, and the diff between prior and incoming for each affected section (crew, hotels, rooms, etc.). Apply submits the §6.8.2 reviewer-choices payload; Discard runs §6.8.1's restore-prior-status flow. The card also surfaces `staged_modified_time` ("staged from edits Doug made on …") so admin knows what version they're approving. While this card is present, the §9.2 1–3 sub-sections render below as informational context. Re-stage of an existing show is the canonical path through this surface; **first-seen review uses the same review-card UI but is hosted at `/admin/show/staged/<stagedId>` — a slug-less variant of `/admin/show/<slug>` because no `shows.slug` exists yet for a candidate that hasn't been Applied. Loading is keyed off `pending_syncs.staged_id` (not slug). On Apply the route INSERTs the `shows` row + DELETEs the `pending_syncs` row in one transaction and redirects to `/admin/show/<derived-slug>` (per §6.9 slug derivation). The §9.2 1–3 informational sub-sections do NOT render on `/admin/show/staged/<stagedId>` since they assume an existing `shows` row (last 5 sync attempts, parse_warnings history, crew preview links — none of these exist yet for a candidate). Reached via the dashboard's "Sheets we couldn't auto-apply" panel.**

1. **Sync health** — last 5 sync attempts with status and duration. Manual re-sync button.
2. **Parse warnings** — list of `parse_warnings` entries. Each warning has:
   - Severity icon
   - Human-readable message ("Calvin Saller has `***` flag but no day restriction in cell")
   - Raw snippet (`<pre>` showing the offending row)
   - "Report this to Eric" button → opens GitHub issue (§13)
   - Dismiss (does nothing destructive; just hides locally for this admin until next sync)
3. **Crew preview links** — each crew member's name with a "Preview as" link → `/admin/show/<slug>/preview/<crew-id>`.

### 9.3 `/admin/show/<slug>/preview/<crew-id>` — impersonation

Renders the exact crew page for that crew member, with:

- Sticky top banner: `Previewing as Eric Weiss (A1) — [Exit preview]`. The banner is `position: sticky; top: 0; z-index: 100;` and uses a distinct color (yellow tint) to make impersonation unmistakable.
- All role-based filtering applied as if the admin were that user.
- A "Report this view" button on the banner (in addition to any in-page "Report" links).

### 9.4 Connecting a new sheet (folder polling, not direct paste)

Per the brainstorm decision: Doug doesn't paste URLs. Instead, on first setup:

1. Doug visits `/admin` and sees: "Share a Drive folder with `<service-account-email>`. Any sheet you put in it will be synced automatically."
2. Doug shares the folder (one-time, in Drive UI).
3. Doug returns to `/admin` and clicks "I've shared the folder" (or the app polls and discovers automatically).
4. Within ~5 min, sheets appear in the dashboard.

For **dev mode** (Eric operating): Eric authenticates the dev-environment Drive client with his own OAuth credentials so that a folder shared with Eric works without provisioning a separate service account. Production swaps to a service-account credential file (`GOOGLE_SERVICE_ACCOUNT_JSON`) and Doug shares the watched folder with that service-account email. The dev/prod switch is a single env-var swap; the underlying client library and per-folder permissioning model are identical.

---

## 10. Linked Drive content

Per §2 deferral list, agenda PDF parsing is out. But linked content is rendered with discretion:

| Link kind                                           | Source field                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 | v1 rendering                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         |
| --------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Agenda PDF (`.pdf`, `.docx`)                        | `agenda_links[].fileId` or `.url`                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            | "Open agenda" button. On tap: in-page sheet with PDF.js inline preview (or `<iframe>` for native Drive preview as fallback). `.docx` falls back to "Open in Drive" (no inline preview).                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              |
<!-- spec-id: -immutable-pin-amendment -->

| Diagrams (linked folder OR embedded images OR both) | `diagrams.linkedFolder.driveFolderId` and/or `diagrams.embeddedImages[]` and/or `diagrams.linkedFolderItems[]`                                                                                                                                                                               | "Diagrams" tile. On tap: full-screen image gallery (swipeable). **Both sources go through the same snapshot/proxy path** — no live-Drive read at request time. **Round-44 amendment: linked-folder enumeration is FROZEN at Phase 1 with the immutable approval tuple** (per §6.11): `parseResult.diagrams.linkedFolderItems[]` captures `(driveFileId, mimeType, alt, drive_modified_time, headRevisionId, md5Checksum)` per item. Apply downloads via `revisions.get(driveFileId, headRevisionId, alt='media')` (Pattern A — exact bytes) or via `alt=media` + buffer-then-verify md5 (Pattern B fallback); modtime alone is NOT a fence (TOCTOU window). Apply does NOT re-enumerate the folder. Embedded entries carry `sheetsRevisionId` + `embeddedFingerprint`; entries with `embeddedFingerprint = null` are restage-only and Apply fails closed for them. Each downloaded blob lands at `diagram-snapshots/shows/<show_id>/<snapshot_revision_id>/folder-<driveFileId>.<ext>` with the resolved path stored in the row. Embedded images carry `sourceFolder: "embedded"`; linked items carry `sourceFolder: "linked"`. Gallery serves every image through `/api/asset/diagram/<show>/<rev>/<assetKey>` per §7.3. See §6.11 for the full snapshotting + immutable-pin model. |
| Opening reel video                                  | `event_details.opening_reel` (free-text status; **rendered with all `https?://` URL substrings stripped** — see render contract below) plus the parser's structured Phase 1 output `parseResult.openingReel = { driveFileId, drive_modified_time, headRevisionId, mimeType: string \| null } | null`(full immutable pin tuple; the 4-field type matches the four`shows.opening*reel*\*` columns so partial-column persistence is impossible at type-check time) populated from the same cell when a Drive URL is detected                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           | **URL extraction is a substring match**, not start-anchored: the parser uses `/(https?:\/\/)?(drive\.google\.com | docs\.google\.com)\/[^\s]+/`(no`^`anchor) to find a Drive URL anywhere in the cell value, including mixed-value cells like`YES - https://drive.google.com/file/d/...` and `LOOP VIDEO - <url>`. If matched, the parser extracts the Drive `fileId` from the URL path. The sync layer then enriches via `files.get(fileId, fields='mimeType,modifiedTime,headRevisionId,md5Checksum')` at Phase 1 stage time. **MIME-type gate**: if `mimeType` does NOT start with `'video/'` (e.g., `application/vnd.google-apps.document`, `application/vnd.google-apps.presentation`, `image/*`, `application/pdf`), the enrichment emits `OPENING_REEL_NOT_VIDEO` (§12.4) and produces `parseResult.openingReel = null` so Phase 2 persists ALL FOUR `opening_reel_*` columns as NULL atomically (driveFileId, drive_modified_time, head_revision_id, mime_type). Crew page renders text-only opening reel; no inline `<video>` is ever emitted for non-video MIME types. If `mimeType` DOES start with `'video/'`, enrichment emits `parseResult.openingReel = { driveFileId, drive_modified_time, headRevisionId, mimeType }` and Phase 2 persists all four columns non-NULL. **At Apply time, §6.11.1's full four-step flow re-verifies the reel drift via `headRevisionId` AND `mimeType` AND classifies 403 as drift, and persists ALL FOUR columns atomically** (`shows.opening_reel_drive_file_id`, `shows.opening_reel_drive_modified_time`, `shows.opening_reel_head_revision_id`, `shows.opening_reel_mime_type`). If the cell is text-only (`MAYBE`, `YES`, `N/A`, etc.) or has no Drive URL substring, `parseResult.openingReel = null` and all four columns are set to NULL. **Milestone split: inline `<video>` rendering ships in M7, NOT M4.** **Render contract: the cell text is NEVER rendered verbatim to crew when it contains a Drive URL.** Rendering "mixed `YES - <url>` cells as `Opening reel: <verbatim cell value>`" would leak the raw `https://drive.google.com/...` substring into crew DOM, violating the proxy-only auth boundary asserted later in this section ("the crew page never sees the raw Drive URL"). The render contract: BEFORE rendering the `Opening reel:` text line, the renderer applies `value.replace(/(https?:\/\/)?(drive\.google\.com | docs\.google\.com)\/[^\s]+/g, '').replace(/\s+-?\s*$/, '').replace(/^\s*-?\s\*/, '').trim()`so all Drive/Docs URL substrings AND the orphaned` - `connector tokens around them are removed; the resulting human status text (e.g.,`YES`, `MAYBE`, `N/A`, `BACKUP ONLY`, `LOOP VIDEO`) is what crew sees. After stripping, if the residual text is empty (the entire cell value WAS the URL), no `Opening reel:`text line renders at all. The underlying parsed`parseResult.openingReel.driveFileId` lives ONLY in server-internal state and feeds the M7 inline-`<video>`route via`/api/asset/reel/[show]`— never as a Drive URL in HTML. The crew page at M4 (Task 4.14 / AC-4.5) renders the stripped text only — NO`<video>`element is emitted. Once M7 Task 7.6 lands the`/api/asset/reel/<show>`route, the same crew page additively renders inline`<video controls src="/api/asset/reel/<show>">`(which streams via`revisions.get(headRevisionId, alt='media')`or buffer-then-verify md5 per §7.3) whenever ALL FOUR persisted pin columns are non-NULL — verified by AC-7.25. Mixed values like`YES - <url>` get both at M7: the URL-stripped text status (`YES`) AND the embedded `<video>`; at M4 only the stripped text. Text-only cells (no URL substring) render only the text line at every milestone. |
| Test pattern, Aptos fonts, II LED logo              | various                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      | NOT surfaced to crew. These are operations files. They appear in admin under a "Production assets" disclosure.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       |

**Caching strategy** (revision-aware end-to-end so Apply invalidates implicitly via URL rotation):

- Diagram lists are derived from `shows.diagrams.{embeddedImages,linkedFolderItems}` — read straight from Postgres on every request, no list-level caching layer. List size is small (typically ≤10 items) so DB reads are cheap.
- Individual diagram images are served via revision-versioned URLs (`/api/asset/diagram/<show>/<rev>/<key>`). Every fetch revalidates with the server (`Cache-Control: private, max-age=0, must-revalidate`); the URL identifies which revision is requested but the auth check runs every time. Revisioning solves stale-bytes-after-Apply (URL rotates); `must-revalidate` solves immediate-revocation-on-session-end (revoked sessions can't reuse cached responses without a server check that returns 410).
- Opening reel videos are streamed through `/api/asset/reel/<show>` (per §7.3 routing) with the same `Cache-Control: private, max-age=0, must-revalidate` policy as diagrams. v1 doesn't snapshot reels into Storage (they aren't typically edited per show) — but the auth contract matches diagrams: every request re-runs auth, revocation propagates immediately.
- **No manual cache-purge is required** on Apply because every Apply rotates the URL space. The diagram GC cron (§6.11) is the only cleanup; it removes orphaned revision blobs after the 7-day grace window.

**Caps on unbounded content:**

- **Diagrams gallery:** up to 12 images shown in initial render (embedded images prioritized, linked-folder images filling the remainder); "Show more" reveals the rest. The combined cap across BOTH sources is 60: embedded counts toward the cap first; if `embeddedImages.length >= 60` the linked-folder content is suppressed entirely and a `DIAGRAMS_EMBEDDED_CAP_EXCEEDED` admin warning fires. Otherwise the linked folder fills up to `60 - embeddedImages.length` images per the existing folder-cap rules.
- **Notes tile (aggregated from every block's `notes`):** per-source items truncated at 280 characters with a "tap to expand" affordance. The tile itself shows up to 8 source items; remainder collapsed under "+N more notes."
- **Crew tile:** all crew members are shown; observed max is 6, theoretical max ≈ 12 — within reason. No truncation.
- **Hotel reservations:** up to 4 observed; rendered all. > 4 (defensive) reflows into a vertical list.

**Auth note:** Drive content fetches use the service account credentials. The crew page never sees the raw Drive URL; it always goes through an app-controlled URL like `/api/asset/diagram/<show>/<filename>`. This avoids leaking Drive folder access to non-crew.

## 11. Edit/sync semantics

| Scenario                                            | v1 behavior                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          |
| --------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| **Crew member removed from sheet**                  | The post-upsert `delete-not-in-set` step in §5.2 removes their `crew_members` row on next sync. Signed-link path: the per-request `(show_id, name)` lookup (§7.2) fails, returning 410 with `you've been removed from this show — contact Doug`. Google-login path: same, the email→`crew_members` match fails, redirects to "no access." They drop from `/me`.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      |
| **New crew member added**                           | Their row appears in `crew_members` on next sync. Doug shares the URL/link out-of-band. App does not auto-email. Their Google login starts working as soon as the sync completes.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    |
| **Sync failure**                                    | Page renders last-good with the staleness signal in the footer. After 6h stale, the footer turns red and surfaces `couldn't sync — contact Doug`. Page never goes blank.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             |
| **Sheet renamed/moved in Drive**                    | We track `drive_file_id` which survives rename/move. No effect.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      |
| **Sheet deleted, un-shared, or moved out of scope** | Detected by §5.2 step 4 (diff Drive listing against `shows` rows). Marked `last_sync_status = 'sheet_unavailable'`. `last_seen_modified_time` is preserved so the cached parsed data still renders on the crew page. Doug's admin shows "this sheet is no longer accessible — re-share or restore." If the sheet returns to the watched folder later, the next sync detects it via the listing and resumes normal updates. The legacy `files.get 404` path remains as a defensive secondary detection for the narrow race where a file disappears between list and fetch within the same run.                        |
| **Template version changes mid-show**               | Per-pull version detection (§6.4) re-dispatches. Field aliases handle most renames; net-new fields land in `shows_internal.raw_unrecognized`.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        |
| **No version marker matches**                       | Parser emits `MI-1_VERSION_DETECTION_FAILED` and the run hard-fails per MI-1 (§6.8). The prior-snapshot data is retained on the live page (or, for first-seen sheets, the failure surfaces in `pending_ingestions`). **There is no permissive v1-fallback render** — earlier rounds of this spec described one, but it conflicts with MI-1's hard-fail contract and could push partial / incorrect data into the live snapshot. Hard-fail is the single contract: don't trust an unrecognized template. Doug's parse panel surfaces this as a hard-to-miss banner with the exact markers the parser was looking for. |
| **Crew role changes**                               | Re-fetch on next page load applies new role-based filtering. **No session invalidation needed and no signed-link re-issue needed.** Per §7.2 the JWT carries no `role` claim; role is always derived fresh from the current `crew_members.role_flags`. A demotion from LEAD to A1 takes effect on the very next request to the page, with no token rotation.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         |
| **Show date moves**                                 | Right Now card recomputes on next load and on every Realtime update.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 |

## 12. Error handling and observability

### 12.1 Layers

- **Parser:** every field extraction is fault-tolerant. Missing fields produce `null`, not exceptions. Hard errors only on unrecoverable structural failures (no INFO block at all).
- **Sync:** wraps the parser + Drive fetch + DB write in a single try/catch. Records to `sync_log` regardless of outcome. Never blows away last-good data on failure.
- **Render:** Server Components cannot throw past the boundary; they fall back to a "this section couldn't load — last good data shown" state with a report link. Client components have an Error Boundary that renders a similar fallback.
- **Auth:** unmatched Google login → "your email isn't on the crew list for this show; ask Doug to add you or share a signed link." Invalid JWT → "this link has expired or been revoked; ask Doug for a new one."

### 12.2 Observability

- **Sentry** for unhandled errors (Vercel + browser).
- **Supabase `sync_log` table** as the authoritative source of sync history.
- **Vercel Analytics** for page views (free tier).

### 12.3 Crew-side error UX

The page never shows a stack trace, an HTTP status code, or a "something went wrong" generic. Every error has an actionable message. See §12.4 for the canonical mapping.

### 12.4 User-facing message catalog

Every error code, parse warning, and admin notification produced anywhere in the app maps to **exactly one** user-facing message string. Engineers do not write copy ad-hoc; they pick the appropriate code and the renderer looks up the message from this table. Doug and crew never see a code, an HTTP status, or a stack trace; they see the "Doug-facing message" or "Crew-facing message" column. The "Follow-up" column is the action the UI suggests.

**Conventions:**

- "Doug-facing" means it appears in `/admin` or in the per-show parse panel.
- "Crew-facing" means it appears on a `/show/<slug>` or `/show/<slug>/p#t=...` page rendered to a non-admin viewer. `—` means the code never reaches a crew render.
- Codes are stable identifiers; messages may evolve over time. The bug-report pipeline (§13) carries the code; the developer translates back via this table.
- Plain language is the rule. "Sheet" not "Drive document"; "your show" not "the resource"; "the developer" not "the maintainer."
- **Admin-log-only codes**: a row whose `Doug-facing message` cell is `(admin log only ...)` / `—` and `Crew-facing message` cell is `—` is **admin-log-only** — the code is emitted to structured logs and `sync_log` for operator/Eric debugging, but is NEVER rendered to Doug's UI or crew's UI. These codes are exempt from the §9.0.1 `<ErrorExplainer>` wiring requirement (the explainer renders for codes that DO reach Doug; admin-log-only codes never do). The X.1 extractor normalizes the row's `dougFacing` and `crewFacing` to `null` and the YAML appendix MUST omit the `helpfulContext` key for any admin-log-only code. The Task 10.9 explainer-coverage test explicitly skips codes whose `dougFacing` is null. Examples (non-exhaustive): `STALE_WRITE_ABORTED`, `STALE_PUSH_ABORTED`, `WEBHOOK_NOOP_ALREADY_SYNCED`, `CONCURRENT_SYNC_SKIPPED`, `WIZARD_SESSION_SUPERSEDED_DURING_SCAN`, `LOCK_OWNERSHIP_ASSERTION_FAILED`, `STAGED_PARSE_REVISION_RACE`, `LINK_CROSS_SHOW_REUSE`, `UNEXPECTED_PARENT`, `DIAGRAMS_TAB_MISSING`, `TYPO_NORMALIZED`.
- **Em-dash normalization**: when a code is admin-log-only, the corresponding markdown table cells (`Doug-facing message`, `Crew-facing message`, and `Follow-up` where applicable) MUST be rendered as a literal `—` (em-dash) or empty cell — NOT pseudo-null sentinel text like `null`, `none`, `n/a`, `(admin log only)` interleaved with copy, or any other prose that the X.1 extractor would have to disambiguate from real Doug-facing copy. The extractor treats `—` and empty cells as the canonical "null" marker; any other shape risks a false-positive Doug-facing classification, which then fails the X.1 invariant when the YAML appendix correctly omits the entry. Codes whose `Doug-facing message` cell needs to convey both "admin-log-only" semantics AND a one-line operator hint MUST use a parenthetical preamble with em-dash separator (`(admin log only — short hint)`) — the extractor recognizes the leading `(admin log only` token as the admin-log-only sentinel and normalizes the whole cell to `null`. This convention removes the need for any per-row prose to explain the cell's null-ness.
- **`helpfulContext` (machine-parseable)**: every code with non-null `dougFacing` ALSO has a non-null `helpfulContext` — a one-paragraph plain-language explanation rendered by the §9.0.1 "What does this mean?" link. The catalog implementation (M9 Task 9.4) carries `helpfulContext` as a fourth column alongside `dougFacing` / `crewFacing` / `followUp`. **Batch-10 Fix 1**: to make §12.4 fully machine-parseable for ALL four `SpecCodePayload` fields (`dougFacing` / `crewFacing` / `followUp` / `helpfulContext`), the canonical `helpfulContext` strings live in the structured `<!-- §12.4 helpfulContext appendix -->` YAML block immediately following the table. The four-column markdown table below remains the visual source of truth for `dougFacing` / `crewFacing` / `followUp`; the YAML appendix is the source of truth for `helpfulContext` (carried as a fifth field that would make the table too wide to read). The X.1 extractor (`scripts/extract-spec-codes.ts`) parses BOTH the markdown table AND the YAML appendix and emits a single `SPEC_CODES` manifest where every entry carries all four fields verbatim. The X.1 parity test deep-compares each `SpecCodePayload` field-by-field — a `helpfulContext` edit in the YAML appendix that doesn't propagate to `lib/messages/catalog.ts` fails the parity test the same way a `dougFacing` edit in the table does. Codes whose `dougFacing` is `—` / null don't need `helpfulContext` because they're admin-log-only and never surface to Doug; the YAML appendix omits those keys entirely (the extractor normalizes "missing key" to `helpfulContext: null`). Any prose that describes `helpfulContext` for a code outside the YAML appendix is non-authoritative — only the appendix is parsed.

| -------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------ | --- | --- |

Ask Doug for a new one."                                            | Crew → text Doug                                 |

Ask Doug for a new link."                                     | Crew → text Doug                                 |

Ask Doug for a new link."                                      | Crew → text Doug                                 |
