Ask Doug for a new link."                                        | Crew → text Doug                                 |
| `LINK_NO_CREW_MATCH`                                     | crew row referenced by JWT has been removed from sheet                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               | —                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         | "You've been removed from this show. Contact Doug if this is a mistake."                    | Crew → text Doug                                 |
| `LEAKED_LINK_DETECTED`                                   | `?t=` query-param URL detected                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       | "A signed link was opened with `?t=` in the URL — we treat that as a possible leak. The affected link has been auto-revoked and the crew member's row is in 'no live link' state. Click 'Issue new link' for them when you're ready."     | "This link format isn't supported and has been revoked. Ask Doug for a new one."            | Doug → Issue new link                            |
| `CSRF_DENIED`                                            | `/api/auth/redeem-link` rejected a POST whose `Sec-Fetch-Site` is not `same-origin` (or whose `Origin` doesn't match the site origin), OR whose bootstrap nonce is missing entirely / replayed (already-consumed) / body-cookie mismatched / wrong-show-id (attacker swap). **Strictly the malicious / cross-site / tampered branch** — the benign "user dawdled past the 30s window" condition is `CSRF_NONCE_EXPIRED`, NOT this code. Defense against login-CSRF: SameSite=Lax does NOT prevent forced cross-origin POSTs of attacker-controlled JWTs that mint a session cookie bound to the attacker's identity. | (operator-only structured log entry — admin sees the source `Origin`, `Sec-Fetch-Site`, and presence/absence of bootstrap nonce; no Doug-facing copy because this should never fire under normal use)                                     | "We couldn't open this link. Try the original link Doug shared again, in the same browser." | Crew → reopen original link; if persistent, Eric |

| `PARSE_ERROR_LAST_GOOD` | stale-data footer surfacing `shows.last_sync_status='parse_error'` on an existing approved show. Distinct from the parser hard-fail codes (`MI-1`/`MI-2`/etc.) which are admin-facing parse-panel detail; this code is the crew-facing "what you see is older than the latest edit" footer message. | `WIZARD_SESSION_SUPERSEDED` | Apply or Discard against an onboarding-staged row whose wizard session is no longer current | "Your setup wizard was superseded by another wizard. Refresh and start setup again." | — | Doug → restart wizard |
| `WIZARD_REVIEWER_CHOICES_VERSION_UNSUPPORTED` | wizard finalize Phase B SELECT'd a `pending_syncs` row whose `wizard_reviewer_choices_version` is not in the current code's supported set (e.g., the row was approved under a future shape revision that this build does not implement, or — more commonly — under an OLDER shape that has since been retired). Finalize MUST refuse to replay the payload through the wrong validator/derivation table because doing so would silently mis-derive auth side-effects. Phase B aborts BEFORE per-row Phase 2 work; the manifest row is demoted back to `'staged'` in a separate follow-up transaction (per the manifest-lifecycle rule); the operator must re-Apply under the current version. | "We made an update to the review process since you approved this sheet. Please review and Apply it again to finish setup." | — | Doug → re-Apply the affected sheet |
| `STAGED_PARSE_REVISION_RACE_DURING_FINALIZE` | wizard finalize Phase B's per-row pre-commit Drive head re-verify (acquired AFTER the advisory lock, BEFORE the Phase-2 SQL) detected that `headRevisionId` advanced between Phase A.2's re-verify and Phase B's lock-hold re-fetch. Doug edited the sheet during the Phase A → Phase B window; the snapshot bytes Phase A captured no longer represent the current head, and committing them would promote stale data. Per-row abort: skip Phase 2 for THIS row, leave its manifest at `'staged'` (the per-row Phase 2 + manifest 'applied' UPDATE is gated on this re-verify so the manifest never advances), continue Phase B for the unaffected rows. Distinct from `STAGED_PARSE_REVISION_RACE` (which fires during Phase 1 enrichment, not finalize) — the during-finalize variant means the operator already approved this sheet and a SUBSEQUENT edit raced into the finalize window. Operator must re-Apply (re-review the new edit) before the next finalize click; the response body lists the affected `drive_file_id`. | "_<sheet-name>_ was edited again while we were finishing setup. Please re-review and Apply it, then click Finalize again." | — | Doug → re-Apply the affected sheet |
| `ONBOARDING_FINALIZE_INTERNAL_ERROR` | wizard finalize (the batch publish endpoint `/api/admin/onboarding/finalize` OR its final compare-and-swap step `/api/admin/onboarding/finalize-cas`) threw an UNEXPECTED error the route has no typed code for (e.g. a `parse_result` / `wizard_reviewer_choices` jsonb that fails the read coercer because it is genuinely corrupt — not merely a legacy double-encoded scalar, which the coercer decodes — or an unanticipated DB fault). Both finalize handlers wrap their transaction so any such throw becomes a 500 with a JSON body carrying this code rather than an empty 500 body (an empty body made the client's `response.json()` fail with "Unexpected end of JSON input" — the M12 Phase 0.F smoke-3 symptom); the underlying error message is written to the structured operator log. Admin-log-only — no Doug-facing UI surface (`dougFacing` is `—`); Eric inspects the logged message to diagnose. | — | — | Eric → investigate |
| `WIZARD_FINALIZE_BATCHES_PENDING` | the 24h auto-rotate at `/admin` (wizard-mode) detected `pending_wizard_session_at` was past the 24h horizon BUT `wizard_finalize_checkpoints.batches_completed > 0` for the same session — i.e., a multi-batch finalize was started, at least one batch committed, and the operator paused before completing the final batch. Auto-rotate is suppressed (because purging `onboarding_scan_manifest` would orphan the interim `published=false` `shows` rows the in-flight finalize already committed); the wizard surface renders "Resume finalize" and "Cleanup abandoned finalize" affordances per §4.5 prong 3. Admin-log-only — operators see this code in `sync_log` to understand why an auto-rotate did not fire. Equivalent to `WIZARD_FINALIZE_BATCHES_PENDING` ALSO emitted when the finalize endpoint refuses to start a fresh promotion against a session whose checkpoint shows `batches_completed > 0` from a prior wizard. | (admin log only — operator must Resume or Cleanup before a fresh wizard can run) | — | Doug → click Resume finalize OR Cleanup abandoned finalize |

| `STAGED_PARSE_OUTDATED` | Drive `modifiedTime` advanced past staged version (non-onboarding source) | "The sheet was edited again since you reviewed this parse. We've discarded the staged version; a fresh parse will be ready in a few minutes." | — | Doug → wait, review next |
| `STAGED_PARSE_REVISION_RACE` | §5.2 same-revision binding window detected a revision race. Triggers: (1) post-enrichment `files.get` head re-verify returned a different `headRevisionId` than `binding.headRevisionId`; (2) `revisions.export(driveFileId, binding.headRevisionId, mimeType)` returned 404 / notFound mid-flight (bound revision retired); (3) `spreadsheets.get` for the bound revision returned 404 / notFound mid-flight; (4) `drive.revisions.list(spreadsheetId)` succeeded but did NOT include `binding.headRevisionId` (revision was trimmed between binding-capture and enrichment); (5) any enrichment-time pinned read (`revisions.get` / `revisions.export`) returned 404 specifically because the bound revision is gone (NOT because the file itself is gone — that's `STAGED_PARSE_SOURCE_GONE`). All five trigger classes have the same root cause (Doug edited the sheet mid-flight; `binding.headRevisionId` is no longer addressable) and the same retry semantics: Phase 1 aborts before any commit; no row is staged; no watermark advances; the next cron pass captures a fresh `binding.headRevisionId` and re-runs the full chain. **Exponential cooldown to bound retry storms**: a per-`(drive_file_id, raced_head_revision_id)` cooldown via the admin-only `revision_race_cooldowns` table (§4.1 + §4.3 — admin-only list contains 18 tables); cron and push consult the cooldown BEFORE retrying and skip with `STAGED_PARSE_REVISION_RACE_COOLDOWN` (admin-log-only, transient) if the same `head_revision_id` was raced within `min(60s × 2^retry_count, 600s)`. Manual re-sync from `/admin/show/<slug>` and `sheet_unavailable`-recovery skip the cooldown gate (admin override). After a successful sync, matching cooldown rows are cleared. Without this cooldown a hot sheet would burn quota indefinitely. | (admin log only — informational; transient by definition since the next pass — gated by the cooldown — converges) | — | — |
| `STAGED_PARSE_REVISION_RACE_COOLDOWN` | cron/push consulted `revision_race_cooldowns` for `(drive_file_id, raced_head_revision_id)` and found a recent race; skipped retry to avoid storm. Manual re-sync bypasses this gate. | (admin log only — transient backoff state; no Doug-facing surface) | — | — |
| `SHOW_REALTIME_BROADCAST_AUTH_FAILED` | `<ShowRealtimeBridge>` failed to mint a Broadcast subscriber JWT via `POST /api/realtime/subscriber-token` — the bridge's `__Host-fxav_session` cookie failed validation (signed-link cookie expired / revoked, OR Google session expired) at token-mint time. The bridge falls back to no-op (no retry storm; v1 fails open per §8 realtime contract). The viewer's NEXT navigation or `router.refresh()` will hit `getShowForViewer` server-side and resolve the auth state correctly (success → fresh render; failure → 410 → bootstrap). | (admin log only — transient or normal-expiry; no Doug-facing surface; the next viewer interaction self-heals) | — | — |
| `SHOW_REALTIME_SUBSCRIPTION_FAILED` | `<ShowRealtimeBridge>` minted a subscriber JWT successfully but `channel.subscribe()` to the `show:<showId>:invalidation` Broadcast topic returned an error (network glitch, Realtime server unavailable, topic ACL mismatch). Falls back to no-op (no retry storm). The viewer continues to see the SSR'd snapshot until they navigate or manually refresh. **Distinct from `SHOW_REALTIME_BROADCAST_AUTH_FAILED`**: that code fires when token mint fails (cookie-side problem); this code fires when subscribe fails (transport-side problem). | (admin log only — transient; no Doug-facing surface) | — | — |
| `SHOW_REALTIME_CROSS_SHOW_FORBIDDEN` | `/api/realtime/subscriber-token` invoked `resolveShowViewer(req, slug)` and the helper returned `{ kind: 'forbidden', reason: 'cross_show_link_session' \| 'cross_show_google_session' }` — the requester's `__Host-fxav_session` cookie OR Google session validated successfully for a DIFFERENT show than the slug being requested (cross-show cookie reuse, cross-show subscriber-token request). 403 response. **Distinct from `SHOW_REALTIME_BROADCAST_AUTH_FAILED`** (401, no credentials present): this code is admin-info severity (security-telemetry signal — a real authenticated user attempting to subscribe to a show they aren't credentialed for); the `denied` 401 path is admin-debug (routine no-cookie request). The discrimination drives downstream UX: a 401 surface re-prompts for sign-in; a 403 surface tells the viewer they're authenticated but not authorized for this show. | (admin-info log; no Doug-facing surface in v1 — but the elevated severity surfaces it in any future security-event aggregator) | — | — |
| `SHOW_VERSION_CROSS_SHOW_FORBIDDEN` | `/api/show/[slug]/version` invoked `resolveShowViewer(req, slug)` and the helper returned `{ kind: 'forbidden' }` — same semantics as `SHOW_REALTIME_CROSS_SHOW_FORBIDDEN` but on the version-token route. 403 response. The `forbidden` arm is structurally distinct from `denied` so the route deterministically returns 403 (cross-show) vs 401 (no credentials) without route-side guessing. | (admin-info log; no Doug-facing surface) | — | — |
| `SHOW_REALTIME_JWT_RENEWED` | `<ShowRealtimeBridge>` ran the JWT-renewal sequence on a Supabase `system` `'disconnected'` event OR on a channel subscribe-status callback returning `'CHANNEL_ERROR'` / `'TIMED_OUT'` / `'CLOSED'`. The renewal sequence re-calls `POST /api/realtime/subscriber-token` (5-minute JWT exp), `client.realtime.setAuth(newJwt)`, `removeChannel(oldChannel)`, re-creates the channel for the same `show:<showId>:invalidation` topic, and runs a `/api/show/[slug]/version` catch-up after the new subscribe resolves. Logs both `outcome: 'success'` (renewed transparently) AND `outcome: 'failed'` (mint returned 401 because the underlying cookie itself expired, OR the re-subscribe failed) variants — admins use this code to trace renewal cadence and to diagnose pages that lose live invalidations after long open sessions. Without the renewal flow, any page open >5min that experiences a routine WiFi blip would silently drop the subscription. | (admin log only — `outcome: 'success'` is normal-operations; `outcome: 'failed'` is benign for the user [next navigation self-heals via 410 → bootstrap] but worth tracing if it spikes) | — | — |
| `LINK_SESSION_KEY_ROTATED` | §7.2.2 step 3a: the per-row `link_sessions.signing_key_id` does not match the active `app_settings.active_signing_key_id`. The operator ran the global JWT-signing-secret rotation workflow (§7.2.3 "Global rotation"); the user's redeemed-link session pre-dates the rotation and is terminally killed. Validator DELETEs the offending row and returns 401. The user re-opens the original signed link to mint a fresh JWT under the new key, which redeems to a fresh `link_sessions` row carrying the current key id. | "Sessions have been rotated; please open your original signed link again." | — | User → re-open original signed link |
| `LINK_REDEEM_KEY_ROTATED` | §7.2.3 redeem-time kid-rotation gate: `/api/auth/redeem-link` verified the submitted JWT under kid `k1`, then read `app_settings.active_signing_key_id` and found `k2` — the operator ran the §7.2.3 global rotation between the JWT's mint and the redemption. Closes the verify→INSERT race that would otherwise let a row land in `link_sessions` with `signing_key_id` mismatched against the JWT's actual signing kid. 403 response. NO `link_sessions` row is INSERTed; NO `__Host-fxav_session` cookie is minted; the bootstrap nonce is left atomically consumed (single-use). Distinct from `LINK_SESSION_KEY_ROTATED` (which fires at validation time, AFTER a session was already redeemed under the old key); this code fires at redemption time, BEFORE any session is established. The user must re-open the original signed link — bootstrapping under the new active kid mints a fresh JWT that redeems cleanly to a row carrying `signing_key_id = k2`. | "Sessions have been rotated; please open your original signed link again." | — | User → re-open original signed link |
| `STAGED_PARSE_SOURCE_GONE` | Apply re-verify found the source sheet has been deleted, unshared, or trashed | "The source sheet is no longer accessible. The staged parse has been discarded. Re-share or restore the sheet to bring this show back." | — | Doug → restore sheet |

| `LINKED_ASSET_DRIFTED` | a linked-folder image's current Drive `headRevisionId` (and/or `md5Checksum`) differs from the immutable approval tuple pinned at stage; bytes were NOT downloaded (the revision/checksum pair is the authoritative byte-fence per §6.11; `modifiedTime` alone has a TOCTOU window). | "A linked-folder diagram has been edited in Drive since the last review. Crew see a placeholder for that image until your next sheet edit re-stages it." | — | Doug → re-edit sheet to re-stage |
| `REEL_DRIFTED` | opening-reel `headRevisionId` (and/or `md5Checksum`) differs at Apply time from the immutable pin tuple captured at stage; ALL FOUR persisted reel columns (`opening_reel_drive_file_id`, `opening_reel_drive_modified_time`, `opening_reel_head_revision_id`, `opening_reel_mime_type`) set to NULL atomically per §6.11.1. The revision pin is the authoritative byte-fence; `modifiedTime` is informational only; partial-NULL states are forbidden — see Task X.6 traceability invariants for the §X.6 4-column atomic-NULL invariant. | "The opening-reel video has been edited since you reviewed this parse. Crew see the text status only until your next sheet edit re-stages the new reel." | — | Doug → re-edit sheet |
| `OPENING_REEL_NOT_VIDEO` | operator pasted a non-video Drive URL (Google Doc, Slides, Sheet, image, or any MIME type that does NOT match `video/_`) into `event\*details.opening*reel`. The substring URL extractor resolved a `driveFileId`, but Phase-1 enrichment detected the non-video MIME type via `files.get(fields='mimeType,modifiedTime,headRevisionId,md5Checksum')`and persisted ALL FOUR`opening_reel\*\*`columns as NULL atomically (per §4.1 column note). Crew page renders text-only opening reel; no inline`<video>`is emitted;`/api/asset/reel/<show>`returns 410 if hit (single 410 contract per AC-7.24). | "The opening-reel link is not a video file. Crew see the text status only — replace the link with a video file URL to enable inline playback." | "Opening reel link is not a video file" | Doug → re-edit sheet |
|`OPENING_REEL_PERMISSION_DENIED` | the staged opening-reel Drive file is no longer accessible to the service account at Phase-1 enrichment, Apply-time re-verify (§6.11.1), or runtime route (`/api/asset/reel/<show>`). Drive returns 403 / `permissionDenied`(file shared was revoked, file made private, or file moved out of a shared drive). The classification persists ALL FOUR`opening_reel_*`columns as NULL atomically (matching the trashed/404 contract) so the crew page falls back cleanly. The runtime route returns 410 (NOT 403) so cache headers + UI placeholder match the existing single-410-contract per AC-7.24. | "The opening-reel video is no longer shared with FXAV. Crew see the text status only — re-share the video file (or replace the link) to restore inline playback." | "Opening reel access revoked" | Doug → re-share / replace link |
|`EMBEDDED_RECOVERY_REQUIRES_RESTAGE`| an embedded image entry has`embeddedFingerprint = null`(the Sheets API didn't supply a content-derived approval token at extraction time), so`asset_recovery`cannot heal it. The show transitions to`partial_failure_restage_required`terminal status; only a fresh sheet edit can mint a new`sheetsRevisionId`+`embeddedFingerprint`and unblock the recovery. | "A diagram in this sheet can't be re-downloaded automatically. Save the sheet (any edit advances the version) and crew will see the image again on the next sync." | — | Doug → save sheet to advance version |
| `AGENDA_GONE_FOR_CREW` | `AgendaPdfViewer` proxy at `app/api/asset/agenda/[show]/[id]/route.ts` returned HTTP **410 Gone** OR **403 Forbidden** — every asset-side and authorization-side failure whose crew-recovery is "ask Doug for a fresh link." Covers asset-gone (Drive errors, mimeType mismatch, oversize, missing-from-`agenda_links`), unpublished-show + non-admin viewer, revoked-link-session fallback, cross-show link/Google envelope, and viewer-show mismatch. Distinct from transient network failure (retry-able 5xx path) and from mid-stream byte-limit (which surfaces as an aborted body, not 410). See `route.ts` + `lib/auth/validateCrewAssetSession.ts` for the comprehensive header-emitting trigger list; Task 9.M7-D2 owns the exhaustive status→code TDD coverage. | — | "This agenda isn't available anymore. Ask Doug for a fresh link." | Crew → message Doug |
| `AGENDA_UNAUTHENTICATED` | `AgendaPdfViewer` proxy returned HTTP **401 Unauthorized** — every live 401 outcome from the link-or-Google validator chain whose crew-recovery is "reopen Doug's most recent signed link." Covers no-credentials, recoverable session-expiry (`SESSION_NOT_FOUND` / `SESSION_ABSOLUTE_TIMEOUT` / `SESSION_IDLE_TIMEOUT`), terminal `LINK_SESSION_KEY_ROTATED`, and Google `continue` fallthroughs (missing auth session, no user/email, no crew match). Distinct from 403 cross-show (covered by `AGENDA_GONE_FOR_CREW`) and 410 revoked-link (also `AGENDA_GONE_FOR_CREW`). See `lib/auth/validateLinkSession.ts` + `lib/auth/validateGoogleSession.ts` + `lib/auth/validateCrewAssetSession.ts` for the comprehensive trigger list; Task 9.M7-D2 owns the exhaustive status→code TDD coverage. | — | "Your link to this agenda expired. Reopen Doug's latest message to view it." | Crew → reopen signed link |
|`ASSET_RECOVERY_REVISION_DRIFT`| a fresh Phase-2 Apply landed a newer`snapshot_revision_id`while`asset_recovery`'s lock-free pre-pass was streaming bytes; the streamed bytes were verified against the OLD revision's pin tuples and uploading them into the new revision's prefix would mark the wrong revision recovered. Recovery captures `previewRev`BEFORE the byte-fetch pass; inside the per-show advisory lock it re-reads`lockedRev`and aborts cleanly when they differ — discards all pre-pass tempfiles, ROLLBACKs the locked transaction, never mutates`shows.diagrams`. On each emission, the orchestrator UPSERTs into `recovery_drift_cooldowns (show_id, preview_revision_id, last_drift_at, retry_count)`so the next cron tick consults the cooldown gate (see`ASSET_RECOVERY_DRIFT_COOLDOWN`below). Transient (auto-resolves on the next cron tick — gated by the cooldown — which re-evaluates against the new revision). | "Diagram recovery paused because the show changed while recovery was checking files. We'll retry against the latest version on the next run." | — | informational only |
|`ASSET_RECOVERY_DRIFT_COOLDOWN`| cron consulted`recovery_drift_cooldowns`for`(show_id, preview_revision_id)`and found a recent drift; skipped the asset_recovery pre-pass to avoid storm. Without this gate, every 60s asset_recovery cron tick re-runs the full byte-fetch pre-pass against a hot show — burning Drive API quota and CPU on hashing for entries that will never reach the locked DB-write phase. Cron computes`cooldown_seconds = LEAST(60 * (2 ^ retry*count), 600)`and skips if`now() < last_drift_at + cooldown_seconds`. Cap at 600s (10 minutes). After a successful asset_recovery completion, matching cooldown rows are DELETEd. Manual re-sync from `/admin/show/<slug>`bypasses this gate (admin override) AND clears matching rows on success. | "Diagram recovery is backing off briefly because this show keeps changing during recovery. We'll retry automatically after the cooldown." | — | informational only |
|`APPLY_PROMOTE_PENDING`| the Apply HTTP route returned 202 Accepted to the operator client immediately after the Phase-2 DB transaction committed; the post-commit promoter (Storage rename + manifest verify + atomic JSONB cutover) runs asynchronously in a fire-and-forget background worker. Without the async split, an Apply landing while another show's promoter held the`promote:`advisory lock would block the HTTP request indefinitely; if the client disconnected, the promoter outcome would be ambiguous to the operator. The split keeps Apply's HTTP latency bounded by the Phase-2 commit alone; the operator client polls the idempotent status endpoint`/api/admin/show/<slug>/apply/<applyId>/status`to learn the eventual outcome. Emitted exactly once per Apply, at the 202 boundary. | (admin log only — informational; the operator UI surfaces the polled status, not this code) | — | — |
|`ASSET_RECOVERY_BYTES_EXCEEDED`|`asset_recovery`'s lock-free pre-pass detected the per-recovery-run byte ceiling was exceeded — `entries.length > 60`OR an entry's`size > 50MB`OR`sum(entries.size) > 3GB`. Recovery aborts BEFORE acquiring the per-show advisory lock and BEFORE downloading any bytes (the cap check fires off the per-entry metadata `size`from`files.get`, not the response body). UPSERTed admin alert + no `shows.diagrams` mutation. The ceiling exists so the per-show advisory lock window stays short (DB-writes-only); without it, recovery for a show with 60 × 50MB images could pin the lock for many minutes and serialize every concurrent cron/push/manual sync. | "This show's diagram set is too large to recover automatically (more than 60 images, an image >50MB, or >3GB total). Crew see placeholders for the missing diagrams. Tell the developer if you need this raised, or trim the gallery." | — | Doug → trim gallery / Eric → raise cap |
| `DIAGRAMS_EMBEDDED_REVISIONS_UNAVAILABLE` | `drive.revisions.list(spreadsheetId)` returned no usable revision token for the spreadsheet, so the embedded-image freeze tuple cannot be captured (rare; happens for files created via APIs that don't track Drive revisions). Step ordering: this gate ONLY fires when at least one embedded image-like `embeddedObject` was already resolved on the DIAGRAMS tab — for linked-only sheets and no-DIAGRAMS-tab sheets, `drive.revisions.list` is NEVER called and revisions-API unavailability is irrelevant. For first-seen sheets carrying actual embedded images, this is a Phase 1 hard-fail recorded in `pending_ingestions.last_error_code`; for existing shows with prior approved diagrams it's a Phase 1 stage-for-approval review item; for existing shows with no prior diagrams it's a status-only `drive_error` UPDATE. **The prior approved diagrams are NEVER replaced with an empty gallery.** **Apply contract:** Apply on this triggered review item is **NON-MUTATING for `shows.diagrams`** — the staged row is marked applied (`pending_syncs` deleted, `last_seen_modified_time` advances, non-diagram sheet-derived columns update via the normal Phase 2 path), BUT `shows.diagrams` is NOT touched at all (same `snapshot_revision_id`, same entries, same `snapshotPath`s, same `snapshot_status`). The Phase 2 UPDATE explicitly excludes the `diagrams` column on this code path. Convergence requires a fresh sheet edit that mints a usable `sheetsRevisionId` + `embeddedFingerprint` via Phase 2; only THAT path mutates `shows.diagrams` and only THEN is a fresh `snapshot_revision_id` minted. This is the technical-failure-recovery contract — distinct from `DIAGRAMS_EMBEDDED_NONE_FOUND`'s operator-confirmation Apply contract (which DOES mutate `shows.diagrams` and mints a fresh `snapshot_revision_id`). | "_<sheet-name>_'s diagrams couldn't be safely captured this sync. The previous version of those images is still showing. The developer has been notified." | — | Eric → investigate; Doug → optionally Report |

| `DIAGRAMS_EMBEDDED_NONE_FOUND` | `spreadsheets.get` returned no `embeddedObjects` for the resolved DIAGRAMS tab AND the parsed sheet body carries no linked-folder URL (sheet appears configured for embedded delivery but produced zero images). **Routing — three branches:** (a) **First-seen** (no `shows` row): Phase 1 stage-for-approval, append a `DIAGRAMS_EMBEDDED_NONE_FOUND` triggered review item — its OWN variant in `TriggeredReviewItem`, NOT aliased to `DIAGRAMS_EMBEDDED_REVISIONS_UNAVAILABLE` (DISTINCT Apply contracts). (b) **Existing show with non-empty current `embeddedImages[]` AND/OR non-empty `linkedFolderItems[]`**: do NOT auto-apply. Route to Phase 1 stage-for-approval, appending a `DIAGRAMS_EMBEDDED_NONE_FOUND` triggered review item; the prior approved gallery stays live (`shows.diagrams.snapshot_revision_id` unchanged) until the operator clicks Apply. **An ambiguous empty `spreadsheets.get` response MUST NOT silently wipe an approved gallery** — auto-applying could let a transient API hiccup (or a sheet with the DIAGRAMS tab temporarily emptied) destroy crew-visible imagery without operator review. (c) **Existing show with already-empty current `embeddedImages[]` AND empty `linkedFolderItems[]`**: idempotent no-op auto-apply path — Phase 2 advances `last_seen_modified_time`; the diagrams JSONB shape is unchanged. The snapshot-mutation invariant still applies whenever non-diagram sheet-derived columns change in this Phase 2 (the column is rewritten with the same content + a fresh `snapshot_revision_id`); when the entire Phase 2 is a strict no-op (nothing else changed either), `shows.diagrams` is NOT touched at all and `snapshot_revision_id` stays the same. **Apply contract distinction:** Apply on a `DIAGRAMS_EMBEDDED_NONE_FOUND` review item DOES mutate `shows.diagrams` (operator-confirmation that the gallery is intentionally empty); Apply on a `DIAGRAMS_EMBEDDED_REVISIONS_UNAVAILABLE` review item does NOT mutate `shows.diagrams` at all (technical-failure recovery; prior approved snapshot stays live). Replaces the retired `files.export(application/zip)` fallback path, which couldn't supply a content-derived `embeddedFingerprint`. **Mandatory regression:** existing show with 5 approved diagrams + Drive returns zero embedded objects AND no linked-folder URL → review item created, `shows.diagrams.snapshot_revision_id` unchanged, gallery still serves all 5 diagrams via `/api/asset/diagram/<show>/<rev>/<key>`. | (first-seen) "_<sheet-name>_ looks like it should have diagrams but we didn't find any embedded images. Confirm before we publish, or paste in the images and re-sync." (existing show with prior gallery) "_<sheet-name>_'s DIAGRAMS tab returned no embedded images this sync — confirm before we replace the existing gallery with empty, or paste in the images and re-sync." | — | Doug → confirm or add images |

| `FINALIZE_OWNED_SHOW` | an admin write route (`runManualSyncForShow`, `/admin/show/[slug]/archive`, per-show staged-review Apply/Discard, etc.) was invoked against a `shows` row whose `published = false` AND whose owning wizard session's `wizard_finalize_checkpoints.status` is `'in_progress'` or `'all_batches_complete'` (i.e., Phase D has not yet committed). 409 response. The route bails BEFORE any DB write so the in-flight finalize state is unaffected. The admin dashboard ALSO hides write-action buttons on `published=false` rows; this server-side guard is defense-in-depth for stale tabs / scripted access. | "This show is currently being published as part of a setup wizard. Wait for the wizard to finish, then try again." | — | Doug → wait for wizard finalize to complete |
| `WIZARD_FINALIZE_CHECKPOINT_MISSING` | `/api/admin/onboarding/finalize-cas` (Phase D) was called against a wizard session that has no `wizard_finalize_checkpoints` row OR whose checkpoint `status` is not `'all_batches_complete'`. The wizard UI should NEVER fire this endpoint until a `/finalize` batch responds with `{ status: 'all_batches_complete' }`; this code surfaces only when the operator manually drives the endpoint OR when the UI's auto-firing logic has a bug. 409 response. | "Setup isn't ready to publish yet. Click 'Promote next batch' until all sheets are processed, then publish." | — | Doug → continue clicking 'Promote next batch' |
| `WIZARD_FINALIZE_UNRESOLVED_ROWS` | defense-in-depth gate on `/api/admin/onboarding/finalize-cas` (Phase D) and on the `/finalize` batch's `'all_batches_complete'` checkpoint transition. A single-predicate gate (`count(pending_syncs WHERE wizard_approved = TRUE) == 0`) would miss the per-row failure-demotion case: when a row's Phase B aborts with `STAGED_PARSE_REVISION_RACE_DURING_FINALIZE` or similar, the per-row rollback follow-up reverts its `wizard_approved` to FALSE AND demotes its manifest from `'staged'` (or never-promotes it from `'staged'`). With ONLY the approved-pending-syncs predicate, that row would be excluded from the count, the count erroneously hits 0, and Phase D would fire while the operator still has an unresolved sheet. The gate requires BOTH (a) zero approved `pending_syncs` for the session AND (b) zero unresolved manifest rows (`status IN ('staged', 'hard_failed', 'discard_retryable', 'live_row_conflict')`). Phase D 409s with this code if predicate (b) fails — the operator must re-Apply / re-Discard the unresolved manifest rows before retrying Phase D. Surfaces in the wizard UI as "Some sheets in this folder still need review." | "Some sheets still need review before we can finish setup. Resolve the rows highlighted on the wizard screen, then click 'Publish' again." | — | Doug → re-Apply or re-Discard the unresolved rows |
| `CSRF_NONCE_EXPIRED` | `/api/auth/redeem-link` POST passed the Origin / `Sec-Fetch-Site` gate AND found a matching `bootstrap_nonces` row at the body's `(nonce_hash, show_id)` (i.e., the request DID originate from a same-origin bootstrap render this browser performed) BUT either (a) `now - issued_at > 30s` (the user dawdled — phone-lock window, idle tab, slow network) OR (b) the matching cookie-array entry was age-evicted because the user opened more than 5 bootstrap shells in the 30s window. Distinct from `CSRF_DENIED` (which signals an attacker-forged or cross-site POST, a missing/replayed/tampered nonce, or a `show_id`-swap attack): this code signals "you raced too many tabs in <30s" or "you took longer than 30s to redeem" — both benign UX conditions. The wizard / sign-in surfaces render a friendly retry message ("Please refresh and click the link again — your bootstrap window expired") instead of the generic CSRF failure. 403 response. **Producer-matrix invariant**: a 31-second-old otherwise-valid nonce MUST resolve to this code, NOT `CSRF_DENIED` — the regression test enumerated in AC-5.13 is what guards the distinction. **Telemetry contract (mandatory):** redeem-link emits a structured operator log entry with shape `{ code: 'CSRF_NONCE_EXPIRED', reason: 'expired' \| 'cookie_evicted', nonce_age_seconds: number, cookie_array_size_at_redeem: number, client_ip_hash: string, show_id: uuid, ts: timestamptz }` — `reason: 'expired'` when `now - issued_at > 30s` for an otherwise-valid row+cookie pair; `reason: 'cookie_evicted'` when the row is otherwise valid but no matching entry exists in the `__Host-fxav_bootstrap_v` cookie array (the user opened more than 5 bootstrap shells in 30s and the array's eviction policy dropped the entry); `nonce_age_seconds` is `EXTRACT(EPOCH FROM now() - issued_at)::int`; `cookie_array_size_at_redeem` is the parsed cookie array length at redeem-link entry (0 if cookie absent); `client_ip_hash` is SHA-256 of the request IP (NEVER raw IP). Distinguishing the two reasons in telemetry lets ops detect "users are dawdling — extend the 30s window?" vs "users are tab-spamming — raise the array cap?". Required regression coverage: 31-second-old nonce → `reason: 'expired'` AND `nonce_age_seconds >= 31`; cookie-array eviction (6th render evicts oldest, then redeem the evicted nonce) → `reason: 'cookie_evicted'` AND `cookie_array_size_at_redeem == 5`. | "Your sign-in link expired before you finished. Refresh the page and click the link again." | "Your sign-in window expired. Click your link again to continue." | Crew → re-click signed link; Doug → refresh and re-click |
| `CSRF_KEY_ROTATED` | `/api/auth/redeem-link` POST passed the Origin / `Sec-Fetch-Site` gate AND found a matching `bootstrap_nonces` row at the body's `(nonce_hash, show_id)` (the request DID originate from a same-origin bootstrap render this browser performed) BUT the cookie envelope's `signing_key_id` field doesn't match `app_settings.active_signing_key_id` AND DOES match the `bootstrap_nonces` row's `signing_key_id` column. This is the benign "operator ran the §7.2.3 global signing-key rotation between the bootstrap shell render and the redeem POST" condition: the cookie was correctly signed under the kid that was active at render time, the kid simply got retired before the redeem completed. Distinct from `CSRF_DENIED` (which signals attacker-forged / cross-site / tampered POSTs — including a bootstrap cookie whose `signing_key_id` matches NO row in `bootstrap_nonces` for this `(nonce_hash, show_id)` pair) AND distinct from `CSRF_NONCE_EXPIRED` (benign 30s-window timeout / cookie eviction): this code signals "the operator rotated keys mid-flight, please refresh and click the link again — the next bootstrap render will mint a cookie under the new kid that redeems cleanly." 403 response with the same recovery UX as `CSRF_NONCE_EXPIRED` (refresh + re-click). The bootstrap nonce row is left atomically consumed (single-use; do NOT un-consume — the user re-renders the bootstrap shell on retry). Order of evaluation inside redeem-link: (1) Origin/Sec-Fetch → fail = `CSRF_DENIED`; (2) row-existence → zero rows = `CSRF_DENIED`; (3) replay → `CSRF_DENIED`; (4) body/cookie nonce_hash match → mismatch = `CSRF_DENIED`; (5) cookie envelope `signing_key_id` field decode → if absent / unparseable = `CSRF_DENIED`; (6) cookie's `signing_key_id` = row's `signing_key_id` → mismatch = `CSRF_DENIED` (cookie wasn't minted by this server's bootstrap-shell render at all — tampering / forgery); (7) cookie's `signing_key_id` ≠ `app_settings.active_signing_key_id` AND row's `signing_key_id` matches the cookie's = `CSRF_KEY_ROTATED` (benign rotation race); (8) age check → `CSRF_NONCE_EXPIRED`; (9) atomic consume race-loss → `CSRF_DENIED`. Without this discrimination, every signing-key rotation that races bootstrap-render → redeem-POST surfaces as `CSRF_DENIED` and operators cannot tell whether they're seeing actual cross-site attacks or just users who clicked through a rotation window. Required regression test: seed `app_settings.active_signing_key_id = 'k1'`; render `/show/<slug>/p` (bootstrap row + cookie envelope both carry `signing_key_id = 'k1'`); execute `UPDATE app_settings SET active_signing_key_id = 'k2'`; POST `/api/auth/redeem-link` with the cookie + body from the render. Assert: 403 with `CSRF_KEY_ROTATED` (NOT `CSRF_DENIED`); structured operator log entry carries `{ code: 'CSRF_KEY_ROTATED', cookie_kid: 'k1', row_kid: 'k1', active_kid: 'k2' }`; `bootstrap_nonces` row remains `consumed_at IS NOT NULL` (atomic-consume already fired in step 6 of the consume sequence; the rotation discrimination is checked AFTER the consume so a malicious replay still gets DENIED on the second hit); no `link_sessions` row INSERTed; no session cookie minted. Inverse: when `active_signing_key_id` is unchanged AND cookie kid matches row kid AND the request is otherwise within the 30s window, the redeem succeeds normally. | "Sessions have been rotated; please open your original signed link again." | "Your sign-in session was rotated. Refresh the page and click your link again." | Crew → re-click signed link; Doug → refresh and re-click |
| `BOOTSTRAP_GENERIC` | `/show/<slug>/p` Bootstrap.tsx caught a non-success outcome from either the bootstrap mint step or the redeem-link POST and could not safely surface the underlying §A code to crew. Consolidates the multiple underlying codes (`CSRF_DENIED`, `CSRF_NONCE_EXPIRED`, `CSRF_KEY_ROTATED`, `LINK_REDEEM_KEY_ROTATED`, `LINK_VERSION_MISMATCH`, `LINK_REVOKED_FLOOR`, `LINK_REVOKED_SURGICAL`, `SESSION_NOT_FOUND`, `GOOGLE_NO_CREW_MATCH`, and any unexpected non-200 from `/api/auth/redeem-link`) into a single crew-facing message that points the user toward Google sign-in as a recovery path. The underlying code is still emitted by the §A surface that produced it (and reaches admin via its own `admin_alerts` / structured-log channel); this code is purely the crew-facing consolidation. Distinct from `NETWORK_UNREACHABLE` which fires when the POST itself never reached the server (no §A code was emitted). Doug-facing is null because Doug sees the underlying §A code in admin surfaces; surfacing both would double-render. | (admin log only — Doug sees the underlying §A code via its own admin surface) | "Couldn't reach the server. Try signing in instead." | Crew → try `/auth/sign-in` |
| `NETWORK_UNREACHABLE` | client-side fetch failed before reaching the server — typically a `TypeError` on `fetch` (offline, DNS failure, captive portal, CORS preflight blocked by network policy, browser extension blocking the request). Distinct from server-emitted error codes: no §A code is emitted because the request never arrived, and no admin trail exists for the failure (the server has no record of it). Surfaced by any client-side surface that needs to fail closed on connectivity loss — currently `components/shared/ReportModal.tsx` (the report-submit POST) but reusable by any other client-side `fetch` site that wants catalog-routed copy instead of an inline string. Distinct from `BOOTSTRAP_GENERIC` (which consolidates §A errors that DID reach the server but returned non-2xx). Doug-facing copy is operator-flavored to acknowledge the missing admin trail; crew-facing is the same recovery prompt because the failure shape is identical from the user's seat. | "Couldn't reach the server. Check your connection and try again — there's no admin trail because the request never arrived." | "Couldn't reach the server. Check your connection and try again." | Either → check connection, retry; persistent → Eric |
| `WIZARD_SESSION_SUPERSEDED_DURING_SCAN` | a `runOnboardingScan` write was blocked because `app_settings.pending_wizard_session_id` no longer matches the scan's session (admin started a new wizard mid-scan) | (admin log only — informational; the new wizard's UI shows the fresh scan state) | — | Doug → use the active wizard tab |
| `LIVE_ROW_CONFLICT` | a `runOnboardingScan` UPSERT collided with a live (NULL-session) `pending_syncs` / `pending_ingestions` row on the same `drive_file_id` AND the schema migration providing per-session partial unique indexes is not in place (rollback / mismigration). Coexistence is the normal path; this code surfaces only the rollback failure mode. \*\*The per-file warn-and-continue MUST also write an unresolved row into `onboarding_scan_manifest` (status `'live_row_conflict'`); without that, the wizard finalize gate (which reads the manifest as its sole source of truth) sees nothing for the file and treats the conflict as resolved, promoting the folder while a real live-row collision is unresolved. The `'live_row_conflict'` status is in §4.5's CHECK and in the §9.0 / §10.5 unresolved set. The rollback signal is a per-file SQLSTATE catch (`42P10` \_invalid_column_reference_ or `23505` _unique_violation_ against the original `drive_file_id` PK), NOT a zero RETURNING-row return — zero rows is the GOOD path under this design.** | "A sheet is already being processed by the live folder sync, so we're skipping it during setup. Resolve it from the dashboard, then re-run setup if needed." | — | Doug → resolve live row from dashboard, then re-run setup |
| `WIZARD_ISOLATION_INDEXES_MISSING` | `runOnboardingScan` ran a `pg_indexes` schema-state probe at scan start and found that fewer than all four expected partial unique indexes (`pending_syncs_live_drive_file_idx`, `pending_syncs_session_drive_file_idx`, `pending_ingestions_live_drive_file_idx`, `pending_ingestions_session_drive_file_idx`) are present. The wizard scan ABORTS before issuing any UPSERT; without these indexes the ON CONFLICT predicates are malformed and per-row writes would all error, leaving an inconsistent partial scan. Operator-facing migration-state error. | "We can't safely scan your folder right now — a recent database update hasn't been applied yet. Eric has been notified; setup will be available again in a few minutes." | — | Eric → apply migration; Doug → retry wizard once migration completes |
| `PENDING_SNAPSHOT_PROMOTE_STUCK` | a `pending_snapshot_uploads` row has been in `promote_started_at IS NOT NULL AND promoted_at IS NULL` state for >15 minutes — a Storage rename / promotion phase has stalled or the promoter process crashed mid-flight. The reclaim-expired sweep refuses to touch rows with `promote_started_at IS NOT NULL` (non-reclaimable promotion state), so manual admin recovery is required. Admin alert + admin-log entry; no auto-recovery. The repair flow LISTs the canonical and temp prefixes, reconciles via the rename audit log, completes the move OR reverse-renames atomically, then clears `promote_started_at` and releases the claim. | "A diagram snapshot promotion has been stuck for more than 15 minutes. Eric needs to run the snapshot-promote repair tool before cleanup can finish." | — | Eric → run snapshot-promote-repair admin tool |
| `PENDING_SNAPSHOT_ROLLBACK_STUCK` | a Storage rollback during snapshot promotion failed mid-flight (some reverse-renames succeeded, then a subsequent reverse-rename failed). The row is left with `promote_started_at IS NOT NULL` AND assets split across temp + canonical prefixes; the GC sweep refuses to act on rows in this state; admin manual repair only. The repair endpoint `/api/admin/snapshot-rollback/[id]/repair` runs a reconciliation routine that LISTs both prefixes, computes the union manifest, decides per-asset which prefix is authoritative based on the rename audit log, performs final reverse-renames of remaining canonical-side assets, then clears `promote_started_at` and releases the claim. | "A diagram snapshot rollback stalled after moving some assets. Eric needs to run the snapshot-rollback repair tool before cleanup can finish." | — | Eric → run snapshot-rollback-repair admin tool |
| `BRANCH_PROTECTION_DRIFT` | The `scripts/verify-branch-protection.ts` workflow step queried GitHub branch protection / rulesets API for the `main` branch and found that one or more of the EIGHT required X.* status checks (`traceability-audit`, `x1-catalog-parity`, `x2-no-raw-codes`, `x3-trust-domain`, `x4-no-global-cursor`, `x5-email-canonicalization`, `verify-branch-protection-status`, `x6-pg-cron-pivot`) is NOT in `required_status_checks.contexts`, OR `required_pull_request_reviews.required_approving_review_count < 1`, OR `enforce_admins != true`. The privileged verification runs on every `push` to `main` AND weekly (cron); it does NOT run on `pull_request` from forks (secrets are not sent to fork-triggered workflows — `pull_request_target` is explicitly NOT used because it would expose secrets to untrusted PR_HEAD code). PR coverage of fork branches is provided by the lightweight `verify-branch-protection-status` reader (auto-injected read-only `GITHUB_TOKEN` only, safe on forks) which queries the privileged job's history on `main` and asserts an 8-day freshness window. Drift detected → privileged workflow fails + admin alert emitted. Without this verification, the manual one-time branch-protection admin step can be skipped or later reverted, leaving the X.* suite advisory. The 7th required check is `verify-branch-protection-status` (the lightweight reader, NOT the privileged job itself, because making the privileged job PR-required would deadlock every external/fork contribution — fork PRs cannot access the secrets the privileged job needs). Recursive-bootstrap property still holds: the privileged script asserts the reader is in the required-checks set; the reader requires the privileged job to have succeeded recently — so removing either name from required-checks, or breaking the privileged job, fails the merge gate within 8 days. | "Branch protection no longer matches the X.6 contract. Restore the required checks and review settings before merging." | — | Eric → restore branch protection per X.6 contract |
| `BRANCH_PROTECTION_MONITOR_AUTH_FAILED` | The `scripts/verify-branch-protection.ts` workflow step could not authenticate against the GitHub API: BOTH `GH_APP_TOKEN` AND `BRANCH_PROTECTION_PAT` env vars are absent OR neither authenticates (the protection / rulesets API calls returned 401 / 403 / token-expired). Treated as an alertable control failure rather than a silent operator misconfiguration: a verifier that goes blind cannot detect downstream drift, so an admin alert fires AND the privileged workflow fails. Persistent auth failure on `main` causes the PR-required reader `verify-branch-protection-status` (which requires a successful privileged run within an 8-day window) to start failing merges within 8 days — closing the loop without exposing privileged secrets to fork PRs. Context payload: `{ gh_app_token_set: boolean, pat_set: boolean, http_status: number \| null, last_successful_auth: timestamptz \| null, repo: '<owner>/<repo>' }`. **Escalation procedure:** if this code fires, an admin must rotate the GH App credentials (or the PAT) within 24h or branch-protection drift can ship undetected. | "Branch-protection monitoring cannot authenticate with GitHub. Rotate the GH App token or PAT within 24 hours." | — | Eric → rotate GH App / PAT within 24h |

| `MISSING_PENDING_INGESTION_MODTIME` | `/api/admin/pending-ingestions/[id]/discard` with `kind='defer_until_modified'` was called against a row whose `last_seen_modified_time` is NULL. Should be impossible — every UPSERT site (Phase 1 hard-fail, `handleDriveFetchFailure`, `runManualStageForFirstSeen` re-UPSERT) populates this column from the just-fetched `fileMeta.modifiedTime`. A NULL signals corruption / mismigration. The handler returns 500 rather than silently writing a `deferred_ingestions` row with a null watermark (which would cause cron to permanently skip the file). | "Something is wrong on our end with this sheet's tracking data — we can't safely defer it without a watermark. The developer has been notified. Try 'Permanently ignore' if you want to dismiss this row." | — | Eric → investigate; Doug → use Permanently ignore as workaround |
| `PENDING_INGESTION_TRANSITIONED` | `/api/admin/pending-ingestions/[id]/retry` or `/discard` acquired the per-show advisory lock and then re-SELECTed the row authoritative state with `FOR UPDATE`, but the row no longer exists. A sibling Retry restaged it (DELETE + INSERT into `pending_syncs`) OR a sibling Discard wrote a deferral and removed it. 409 response with `{ id, transitioned_to_state: 'unknown' }`. The handler aborts before any state-mutating effect to prevent retry-then-discard races from writing `deferred_ingestions` against an already-restaged row. | "Another browser tab acted on this sheet a moment before you. Refresh the dashboard to see the latest state." | — | Doug → refresh dashboard |
| `LOCK_OWNERSHIP_ASSERTION_FAILED` | defensive 500 emitted by the dashboard pending-ingestions retry/discard routes if the post-lock re-SELECT returns a row whose `drive_file_id` differs from the bootstrap read used to derive the lock key. Theoretically unreachable (the column is immutable), but logged so a buggy migration that violates the invariant is surfaced as an operator error rather than silently ignored. | (admin log only — defensive; should never fire in production) | — | Eric → investigate |
| `ADMIN_ALERT_NOT_FOUND` | `/api/admin/admin-alerts/[id]/resolve` (global) or `/api/admin/show/[slug]/alerts/[id]/resolve` (show-scoped) was called with an `id` that doesn't match any row, OR (show-scoped only) the alert's `show_id` doesn't match the slug-resolved show id. 404 response. The show-scoped variant uses 404 (not 403) for cross-show forgery so the route doesn't leak the alert's existence. | "We couldn't find that alert anymore. It may have been resolved already. | `ALERT_REQUIRES_SHOW_SCOPED_RESOLVE` | `/api/admin/admin-alerts/[id]/resolve` (the global route) was called against an alert row whose `show_id IS NOT NULL`. The global route is strictly for global alerts (`show_id IS NULL`); per-show alerts must be resolved via the show-scoped route to preserve §4.6's per-show resolution model (operator clicks through, views show context, then resolves). 400 response. The body carries `{ id, show_id, redirect_to: '/api/admin/show/<slug>/alerts/<id>/resolve' }` (or `redirect_to` omitted if the show was deleted) so the client can retry against the correct route. The SQL UPDATE additionally carries `AND show_id IS NULL` as belt-and-suspenders. | "This alert belongs to a specific show. | **Auth — OAuth round-trip** | | | | |
| `OAUTH_STATE_INVALID` | Supabase Google OAuth callback at `/auth/sign-in` arrived with a missing/expired/mismatched `state` parameter. CSRF defense for the OAuth round-trip. The auth library generates the `state` value on the redirect-out and stores it in a short-lived cookie; the callback compares the URL `state` against the cookie. Mismatch → reject. **Implementation detail:** `/auth/callback` triggers this on PKCE-verifier / state-cookie failures via Supabase `exchangeCodeForSession` (state-mixup, expired/replayed code, dual-tab interference); on rejection the route 302-redirects the user to `/auth/sign-in?code=OAUTH_STATE_INVALID&next=<validated-next>` (canonical error-code URL handoff via `code` URL param) and logs the underlying Supabase error code to the structured operator log. The sign-in page validates the URL `code` param against the §12.4 allowlist `{ OAUTH_STATE_INVALID, OAUTH_REDIRECT_INVALID }` and renders `<ErrorExplainer code="OAUTH_STATE_INVALID" />` so this row's `crewFacing` / `dougFacing` copy surfaces inline. | "Something interrupted your sign-in. Please click the original link from Doug again to start over." | "Something interrupted your sign-in. Please click the original link from Doug again to start over." | Crew → reopen the link; Eric if persistent |
| `OAUTH_REDIRECT_INVALID` | Supabase Google OAuth callback's `redirect_to` parameter doesn't match the allow-list of valid post-sign-in destinations (the canonical site origin + `/show/<slug>`, `/admin`, or `/me` paths). Open-redirect defense — without this guard, an attacker could trick the auth round-trip into landing on a malicious origin while the session cookie is still being minted. **Implementation detail:** `/auth/sign-in` and `/auth/callback` route every `next` parameter through `lib/auth/validateNextParam(raw): string`, which canonicalizes via `new URL(input, NEXT_PUBLIC_SITE_ORIGIN)` and matches against the allowlist regex `^\/(show\/[a-z0-9-]+\|admin(\/.*)?\|me(\/.*)?)$`. **`/show/<slug>/p` is NEVER a valid `next` destination** — the validator has an explicit step-5 rejection (`^\/show\/[a-z0-9-]+\/p$`) because the bootstrap surface mints a session ONLY when `#t=<jwt>` is present and URL fragments do not survive the OAuth round-trip. On any guard failure the route falls back to `/admin` and emits a structured `OAUTH_REDIRECT_INVALID` operator log entry with the offending input verbatim. | "Sign-in landed somewhere we don't recognize. Please click the original link from Doug again to start over." | "Sign-in landed somewhere we don't recognize. Please click the original link from Doug again to start over." | Crew → reopen the link; Eric if persistent |

The shared Apply read mapping (`mapPendingSyncRowForApply`, used by both live and wizard Apply) converts the typed coercion failure into this result rather than dereferencing `.show` on a stub and throwing an uncaught exception; Apply refuses with a parseable JSON response instead of an empty 500. | "This staged sheet's saved data is corrupted, so it can't be applied safely. | **Show lifecycle (M12.2 B2)** | | | | |
| `SHOW_ARCHIVED_BY_ADMIN` | M12.2 B2 — archive action-result disclosure (NOT an admin_alert). | "Archived. Crew links are dead until you re-publish and issue a new link." | — | Doug → re-publish + issue new link when ready |
